Al-Sanusi's Graded Texts and Commentaries
Editor describes al-Sanusi's graded texts and commentary method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi designed a graded curriculum of theological texts and commentaries to guide students from beginner to mastery.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi’s graded texts and commentaries form a ladder for students to master kalam step by step.

This lesson introduces the pedagogical genius of Imam Abdallah al-Sanusi. Rather than writing a single advanced work, he authored six texts of increasing difficulty, each with an accompanying commentary. This method allowed students to gradually build their understanding and enter the field of kalam with solid grounding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the list of six texts and the sequence.
The first phrase 'عنا بخافٍ' is unclear in the source.
2
Understand the method
Reflect on why writing graded texts with matching commentaries is beneficial for learning. Think about how each level builds on the previous.
This method respects varying student levels.
3
Appreciate the goal
The passage ends with the student reaching full strength and entering kalam firmly. Consider how structured progression leads to mastery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله السنوسي عنا بخافٍ، حيثُ ألف ستة متونٍ في هذا الفن، وهي: (المُقدمات ، والعقيدة الكبرى، والعقيدة الوسطى، ثم الصغرى ، ثم صغرى الصغرى ، ثم الحفيدة ثم وضع على كل متن شرحا يناسبه ، وهذه طريقة في التأليف عظيمة النفع ، تناسب مستويات الطلاب فيرتقي بقراءة هذه الكتب حتى يبلغ الطالبُ أَشُدَّهُ ، فيلج في علم الكلام ولوج متمكن واقف على ساقيه بإحكام لا يَتمَلْمَل .
Abdallah al-Sanusi [؟] authored six texts in this art, which are: (al-Muqaddimat, al-‘Aqida al-Kubra, al-‘Aqida al-Wusta, then al-Sughra, then Sughra al-Sughra, then al-Hafida; then he placed upon each text a commentary suitable for it. And this method of authorship is of great benefit, suitable for the levels of students; so the student rises through reading these books until he reaches his full strength, and enters into the science of kalam with a firm entry, standing on his legs with solidity, not wavering.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage defines the method of Imam Abdallah al-Sanusi in composing graded texts on theology. It enumerates six texts in order of difficulty: al-Muqaddimat, al-‘Aqida al-Kubra, al-‘Aqida al-Wusta, al-Sughra, Sughra al-Sughra, and al-Hafida. Then he wrote a commentary for each that matches its level. The editor praises this method as highly beneficial because it allows students to gradually advance until they become solid in the field.

Checkpoint

A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's method of authoring six graded texts with matched commentaries provides a structured path for students to master kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you try to skip steps in your religious learning or practice because you feel impatient? What would it cost you to commit to a gradual, structured path like al-Sanusi's, starting from the basics and building up? Write down one specific area where you will embrace slow, steady progress starting today.
?
Are you truly standing on your own legs in your understanding of faith, or are you relying on borrowed opinions without solid foundation? What is one core belief you haven't fully studied from its source? Will you trace it back to the fundamentals before moving forward?
?
In what part of your life are you 'wavering' because you missed a step? What is the smallest, most foundational step you can take right now to rebuild stability in that area—and when will you take it?

Significance of Jawharat al-Tawhid and Ithaf al-Murid
Editor praises al-Laqani's poem and his son's commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the poem Jawharat al-Tawhid and its commentary Ithaf al-Murid hold a special place in Islamic education.

Core Idea
A poem and commentary so valued that scholars wrote over fifteen glosses on them.

This lesson introduces two foundational texts in the science of tawhid: a blessed poem and its commentary. The editor testifies to their acceptance and the extensive scholarly service they received, highlighting their importance for students of sacred knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the editor's praise and the description of the works.
Pay attention to the phrases describing the poem as 'smooth' and 'blessed'.
2
Identify the two key works
Find the names of the poem and its commentary mentioned in the passage. Note who authored each.
The poem is by Ibrahim al-Laqani, the commentary by his son Abd al-Salam.
3
Understand the scholarly reception
Look for evidence of how scholars engaged with these texts: commentary, annotation, teaching, and the number of glosses.
The editor mentions over fifteen glosses on the commentary alone.
4
Reflect on the educational value
Consider why the editor argues this commentary should be part of the curriculum. How does the scholarly reception support his claim?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هذا الطرق أيضا صنيعُ الإمام إبراهيم اللقاني حيث ألف نظماً سَلِسًا مُباركا في علم التوحيد سماه: جوهرة التوحيد» ليسهل على الطلاب حفظه واستحضار مسائله، وهو نظم غني عن التعريف، لا يُنكِرُ أَنَّ اللهَ قد وضعَ له القبول والبركة إلا ذو قلب مريض وبصرٍ ضعيف ـ وحيثُ كانَ بهذه المثابة اهتم به العلماء شرحا وتحشية وتدريسا (۱) ، ومن بين هذه الشروح شرحُ ولده الشيخ عبد السلام إتحاف المريد بشرح جوهرة التوحيد» وهو شرح مَرْجِيٌّ سَلِس كمتنه، وهو مِن الكتب التي توارد العلماء على الاهتمام بها أيما اهتمام، حيث خدموها ووضعوا عليها الحواشي والتقريرات ودرَّسُوها لطلابهم، وقد وقفت على أكثر من خمسة عشر حاشية وتقرير على هذا الشرح المبارك ، ولعمري إنه كتابٌ حَقيق أنْ يكونَ في المنهج التعليمي لطلاب العلم الشرعي، لما لقي من قبولٍ وخِدمة لدى العلماء، لا بدَّ مِن الرُّجوع إلى تلك الكتب الدراسية التى كانَ علماؤنا يُؤَسِّسون عليها طلابهم كي يصعدوا بهم (۱) سيأتي ذكر بعض أسماء شروح وحواشي متن «الجوهرة» تحت عنوان: شجرة تعريفية بشروح جوهرة التوحيد وسنذكر فيها أيضا الحواشي والتقريرات التي وضعها العلماء على كتابنا هذا إتحاف المريد» .
And from this methods also is the work of Imam Ibrahim al-Laqani, as he composed a smooth, blessed poem in the science of tawhid, which he named 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' to facilitate for students its memorization and recall of its issues. It is a poem that needs no introduction; none denies that Allah has placed acceptance and blessing upon it except one with a sick heart and weak sight. And since it was in such a status, scholars paid attention to it in commentary, annotation, and teaching (1). Among these commentaries is the commentary of his son, Sheikh Abd al-Salam, 'Ithaf al-Murid bi-Sharh Jawharat al-Tawhid', which is a hoped-for, smooth commentary like its matn. It is among the books that scholars focused on with utmost attention, as they served it, wrote glosses and commentaries on it, and taught it to their students. I have come across more than fifteen glosses and commentaries on this blessed commentary. By my life, it is a book worthy of being in the educational curriculum for students of sacred knowledge, due to the acceptance and service it received from scholars. It is necessary to refer to those academic books upon which our scholars established their students so that they may ascend with them (1) We will mention some names of commentaries and glosses on the matn 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' under the title: 'A family tree introducing the commentaries of Jawharat al-Tawhid', and we will mention there also the glosses and commentaries that scholars wrote on this book of ours, 'Ithaf al-Murid'.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage highlights two key elements: first, the poem Jawharat al-Tawhid by Imam Ibrahim al-Laqani, described as a smooth, blessed work that scholars highly valued. Second, the commentary written by his son Abd al-Salam, titled Ithaf al-Murid, which itself received over fifteen glosses and commentaries, attesting to its importance in the educational curriculum. The editor argues that this book should be part of the curriculum for students.

Key Terms

إتحاف المريد
شرح
تحشية
تدريس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that only the original text 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' is important and that commentaries are secondary or less significant.
Correction: The passage shows that the commentary 'Ithaf al-Murid' itself received extensive scholarly attention, with over fifteen glosses and commentaries written on it, demonstrating its central role in the curriculum and not merely a secondary status.

Checkpoint
How many glosses and commentaries did the editor find on the commentary 'Ithaf al-Murid'?
A) Ten
B) More than fifteen
C) Twenty
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The poem Jawharat al-Tawhid and its commentary Ithaf al-Murid are both highly valued in Islamic learning, as evidenced by the many glosses and commentaries scholars produced on them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a text that scholars have universally praised and served with their writings, do you approach it with humility and a desire to benefit, or do you allow your own doubts to hold you back? Examine your heart: is there any 'sickness' that prevents you from fully embracing the acceptance that Allah has placed upon such works?
?
The editor states that only a person with a sick heart denies the blessing of Jawharat al-Tawhid. What areas of your faith might be weak or afflicted, causing you to undervalue the scholarly tradition? Commit to seeking out and studying such accepted texts with full conviction.
?
If you were to teach Ithaf al-Murid one day, what would it take for you to serve it as the scholars did—writing glosses, teaching it, and ensuring its place in the curriculum? Are you willing to invest the time and effort to become a vessel for passing on this blessed knowledge?

Author Biography: Name, Lineage, and Birth
Opening of the author's biography: name, lineage, scholarly description, unknown birth, and nisbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the name, lineage, and biographical details of Imam Burhan al-Din al-Laqani, the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid, including the fact that his birth date is unknown.

Core Idea
A scholar's life often begins with a name and a village.

This lesson introduces the author of our text, Burhan al-Din al-Laqani. Knowing who wrote a work helps us appreciate its context and authority. The biography opens with his full lineage and a striking story about his ancestor, then describes his scholarly stature and the known facts of his life—including the notable omission of his birth date.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the biography begins with a title and then the full name.
2
Identify the full name and lineage
Find the complete chain of ancestors from Ibrahim al-Laqani back to Muhammad ibn Harun. Notice the repetition of 'Ali' in the lineage.
The lineage is long; it underscores the family's piety.
3
Reflect on the anecdote about the ancestor
Read the story about Muhammad ibn Harun standing for the father of al-Dasuqi. What does this anecdote convey about the family's spiritual status?
This story is from Tabaqat al-Sha'rani.
4
Consider his scholarly reputation and birth
Note the description of his expertise in hadith, its sciences, and kalam. Then observe that his birth date is not recorded, but his death date is known.
This lacuna is a common feature of pre-modern biographies.
5
Understand the nisbah 'al-Laqani'
Learn that 'al-Laqani' refers to the village of Laqana in Egypt. This connects the scholar to his geographic origin.
Laqana is described as a village in al-Buhayra.

Source Text

الشيخ إبراهيم بن إبراهيم بن حسن بن علي بن علي بن علي بن عبد القدوس بن الولي الشهير محمد بن هارون المُتَرجَم في طبقات الشعراني، وهو الذي كان يقوم لوالد سيدي إبراهيم الدسوقي إذا مرَّ عليه ويقول: في ظهره ولي يبلغ صِيتُه المغرب والمشرق ..
الإمام أبو الإمداد الملقب بـ برهان الدين اللقاني المالكي أحد الأعلام المشار إليهم بسعة الاطلاع في علم الحديث والدراية والتبحر في الكلام،
وكان إليه المرجع في المُشكلات والفتاوى في وقته بالقاهرة.

Biography of the author Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani. Biography of the author: The learned scholar Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani al-Maliki. His name and lineage: (1) Al-Shaykh Ibrahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ibn 'Ali ibn 'Ali ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd al-Quddus ibn al-Wali al-Shahir Muhammad ibn Harun — who is mentioned in Tabaqat al-Sha'rani, and who used to stand for the father of Sayyidi Ibrahim al-Dasuqi when he passed by him and say: 'In his back is a saint whose fame will reach the West and the East.' The Imam Abu al-Imdad, nicknamed Burhan al-Din al-Laqani al-Maliki, one of the notable figures pointed to for his ample knowledge in hadith, its sciences, and mastery in kalam. He was the reference for difficult issues and fatwas in his time in Cairo. As for his birth, the biographical works did not specify his birth date, but his death date is recorded in them as year 1041 AH, as in Khulasat al-Athar and others. His lineage: to Laqana, like 'sahaba' (a cloud), a village in al-Buhayra among the villages of Egypt — as mentioned by al-Zubaydi in (1) I benefited this biography with very slight modification from the introduction of the edition of Shaykh Marwan al-Bajawi for the book 'Hidayat al-Murid' published by Dar al-Basa'ir, except for some minor additions, with reference to some sources to verify some of the information in the biography.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the author's biography. It provides his full name and lineage: Ibrahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ... up to Muhammad ibn Harun, and notes a story about an ancestor who predicted that al-Dasuqi's son would be a great saint. It then describes al-Laqani's scholarly stature: he was a prominent Maliki scholar known for his knowledge of hadith, its sciences, and mastery of kalam (theology). He was the reference for difficult problems and fatwas in Cairo. The passage then addresses a lacuna: the exact date of his birth is not recorded in biographical works, but his death is well-known as 1041 AH. It also gives the origin of his nisbah (al-Laqani) to the village of Laqana in Egypt. The footnote at the end informs the reader that the biography is derived from a published edition with slight adaptations.

خُلاصة الأثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might assume that al-Laqani's birth date is known and recorded.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that biographical works did not specify his birth date; only his death date is recorded.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The biography of al-Laqani establishes his scholarly authority and traces his noble lineage, while acknowledging that his birth date remains unknown, reminding us that historical records are sometimes incomplete.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Laqani's birth date is unknown, yet his legacy as a scholar endures centuries later. What will remain of your life when your own beginnings are forgotten? Are you building something that outlasts you?
?
An ancestor of al-Laqani honored a child (al-Dasuqi's father) sensing future greatness. Whom in your life have you dismissed or overlooked because they seem insignificant now? Will you change how you treat others starting today?
?
Al-Laqani was the reference for difficult issues and fatwas in his time. In your sphere of influence – family, community, work – are you a source of reliable guidance? What steps will you take to become more knowledgeable and dependable for those who rely on you?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

The Virtues and Spiritual Rank of Imam al-Laqqani
A biographical description of Imam al-Laqqani's qualities and a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the character and spiritual rank of Imam al-Laqqani as illustrated by his personal qualities and a witnessed miracle.

Core Idea
Imam al-Laqqani's life exemplified the union of sacred law and spiritual reality.

This lesson introduces us to the person of Imam al-Laqqani, the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid. Before we delve into his theological text, it is valuable to appreciate the man behind it. His contemporaries unanimously acknowledged his majesty, and a remarkable incident involving the Prophet's presence at his lesson confirms his high station.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of Imam al-Laqqani's character and the narrated incident.
Pay attention to the flow from his qualities to the miracle story.
2
Identify key qualities
List the personal qualities attributed to al-Laqqani: spiritual strength, awe-inspiring dignity, detachment from people, combining shari'a and haqiqa, and possessing miracles.
These qualities show why he was revered.
3
Analyze the miracle
Consider the incident narrated by al-Bashbishi: a fellow scholar saw the Prophet at al-Laqqani's lesson. Reflect on what this indicates about al-Laqqani's spiritual rank.
This miracle (karamah) is a direct confirmation from the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تواضعاً كان الإمام اللقاني عليه رحمة الله قويَّ النَّفس عظيم الهيبة ، تخضع له الدولة ويقبلون شفاعته، وهو منقطع عن التردد إلى واحد من الناس ، يصرفُ وقته في الدرس والإفادة، وله نسبة هو وقبيلته إلى الشرف لكنه لا يظهره منه ، وكان جامعا بين الشريعة والحقيقة ، له كرامات خارقة ومزايا باهرة. قال المُحبّي : حكى الشهاب البشبيشي قال: ومما اتفق أنَّ الشيخ العلامة حجازي الواعظ وقفَ يوما على درسه ؛ فقال له صاحب الترجمة: تذهبون أو تجلسون ؛ فقال له : أصبر ساعة، ثم قال : والله يا إبراهيم ما وقفت على درسك إلا وقد رأيتُ رسول الله واقفا عليه وهو يَسمَعُكَ حتى ذهب . وفي الجملة كان متفقا على جلالته وعلو شأنه .
[In humility, Imam al-Laqqani — may Allah's mercy be upon him — was strong in spirit, great in awe-inspiring dignity; the state submitted to him and they accepted his intercession. He was detached from visiting any of the people, spending his time in teaching and benefiting [others]. He and his tribe had a connection to nobility, but he did not display it. He combined sacred law and spiritual reality. He had extraordinary miracles and brilliant merits. Al-Muhibbi said: al-Shihab al-Bashbishi narrated: Among the incidents is that the scholar Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'iz stopped by his lesson one day; the subject of the biography said to him: 'Will you leave or sit?' He replied: 'Let me stay an hour.' Then he said: 'By Allah, O Ibrahim, I did not stop at your lesson except that I saw the Messenger of Allah standing over it, listening to you until you finished.' In summary, there was agreement on his majesty and high station.]
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch describing the virtues and rank of Imam al-Laqqani. It begins by listing his personal qualities: he was spiritually strong, awe-inspiring, and so respected that the ruling authorities sought his intercession. Yet he was detached from frequenting people, devoting his time to teaching and spreading knowledge. Though he and his family were of noble lineage, he did not flaunt it. He combined outward religious law (shari'a) with inner spiritual truth (haqiqa), and possessed extraordinary miracles (karamat) and brilliant merits. The passage then supports this with a narrated incident: Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'iz, a renowned preacher, once attended al-Laqqani's lesson. When asked whether he would stay or leave, he asked to remain for an hour, then revealed that he had seen the Prophet Muhammad standing over the lesson, listening attentively. This incident confirms al-Laqqani's high spiritual station. The passage concludes that there was unanimous consensus on his majesty and exalted rank.

Key Terms
قوي النفس
الهيبة
الشفاعة
الكرامات
الشريعة والحقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that worldly authority implies a scholar is compromised in his religious integrity.
Correction: Al-Laqqani's humility and detachment show that true spiritual authority does not require worldly compromise; he was both respected by the state and deeply devoted to knowledge and spirituality.

Checkpoint
What did Shaykh Hijazi see when he attended Imam al-Laqqani's lesson?
A) Angels writing down the knowledge
B) The Prophet Muhammad standing and listening
C) A light emanating from the teacher
D) The teacher's shaykh secretly observing

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Laqqani was revered for his spiritual strength, humility, and the witnessed miracle of the Prophet attending his lesson.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet were to attend your gathering or lesson today, what would he hear? Would he find you sincerely teaching or learning for Allah, or for show? How will you ensure your intention is pure?
?
Al-Laqqani had noble lineage but never displayed it. What do you boast about—your knowledge, family, or status? Can you commit to hiding your good deeds and achievements this week as an act of humility?
?
He combined sacred law and spiritual reality. Are you neglecting one for the other? Which area of your practice needs more attention: outward obedience or inward sincerity? What one action will you take today to integrate both?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

The Teachers of Imam al-Laqqani
Listing of al-Laqqani's teachers by madhhab and Sufi path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse educational background of Imam al-Laqqani through his teachers from different madhhabs and the Sufi tradition.

Core Idea
Imam al-Laqqani studied under scholars from multiple madhhabs and Sufi orders.

This passage provides a fascinating glimpse into the traditional Islamic education system by listing the teachers of Imam al-Laqqani. It shows that he did not confine himself to one madhhab but sought knowledge from leading scholars of the Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanafi schools, as well as from Sufi masters. The passage also highlights his most influential teacher, al-Sanhuri.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the categories
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the teachers are grouped by madhhab: Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanafi, and then Sufi path.
The listing is systematic.
2
Observe the pattern of description
For each group, al-Laqqani mentions names and often a brief qualification or authorship. For example, al-Sanhuri is identified as a Maliki scholar, al-Bakri as a Shafi'i gnostic, etc.
This shows the breadth of his education.
3
Focus on the concluding part
The passage ends by emphasizing that al-Laqqani studied most with al-Sanhuri, and describes his rigorous study routine of completing a major hadith book every three years during specific months.
This indicates the depth of his relationship with that teacher.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how studying under multiple madhhabs and Sufi orders shaped al-Laqqani's own scholarship, especially his work in kalam (as seen in Jawharat al-Tawhid).
This connects to his later contributions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيوخه من المالكية: العلامة الشيخ أبو النجا محمد بن سالم السنهوري، والشيخ أحمد المنياوي، والشيخ عبد الكريم البرموي محشي مختصر خليل، وغيرهم. ومن الشافعية: علامة الإسلام العارف بالله الشيخ محمد بن أبي الحسن البكري الصديقي ، والشيخ الإمام محمد الرملي صاحب نهاية المحتاج في شرح المنهاج، والعلامة الشيخ أحمد بن قاسم العبادي، صاحب الآيات البينات على الورقات ، وغيرهم. ومن الحنفية شيخ الإسلام العلامة علي بن غانم المقدسي ، والشمس محمد النحريري ، والعلامة الشيخ عمر بن نجيم صاحب التصانيف في مذهب الحنفية . ومن مشايخه في طريق الصوفية: الشيخ أحمد البلقيني الوزيري، والشيخ محمد بن الترجمان ، والشيخ أحمد عرب الشرنوبي، وجماعة كثيرة غيرهم. وذكر الإمام اللقاني أنه لم يكثر عن أحد منهم مثل ما أكثر عن الإمام الهمام أبي النجا سالم السنهوري ويليه الشيخ محمد البهنسي ؛ لأنه كان يختم في كل ثلاث سنين كتابا من أمهات الحديث في رجب وشعبان ورمضان ليلا ونهارا ويليه الشيخ يحيى القرافي المالكي إمام الناس في الحديث تحريرا وإتقانا، شيخُ رواق ابن معمر بجامع الأزهر آنذاك.
[His teachers: From the Malikis: the scholar Shaykh Abu al-Naja Muhammad ibn Salim al-Sanhuri, and Shaykh Ahmad al-Minyawi, and Shaykh Abd al-Karim al-Barmawi, commentator of Mukhtasar Khalil, and others. From the Shafi'is: the banner of Islam, the gnostic of Allah, Shaykh Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi, and the Imam Shaykh Muhammad al-Ramli, author of Nihayat al-Muhtaj in the commentary of al-Minhaj, and the scholar Shaykh Ahmad ibn Qasim al-Abbadi, author of al-Ayat al-Bayyinat on al-Waraqat, and others. From the Hanafis: the Shaykh al-Islam, the scholar Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi, and Shams Muhammad al-Nahrirri, and the scholar Shaykh Umar ibn Nujaym, author of works in the Hanafi school. And from his shaykhs in the Sufi path: Shaykh Ahmad al-Bulqini al-Waziri, and Shaykh Muhammad ibn al-Turjuman, and Shaykh Ahmad Arab al-Sharnubi, and many other groups. And Imam al-Laqqani mentioned that he did not take much from any of them like he took from the noble Imam Abu al-Naja Salim al-Sanhuri, followed by Shaykh Muhammad al-Bahnasi; because he would complete in every three years a book from the major hadith collections in Rajab, Sha'ban, and Ramadan, night and day, followed by Shaykh Yahya al-Qarafi al-Maliki, the imam of people in hadith in verification and mastery, the shaykh of Riwaq Ibn Ma'mar at al-Azhar at that time.]
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a classification of Imam al-Laqqani's teachers (shuyukh) arranged by madhhab and discipline. First, it lists his Maliki teachers: Abu al-Naja Muhammad ibn Salim al-Sanhuri, Ahmad al-Minyawi, and Abd al-Karim al-Barmawi (who wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil). Then his Shafi'i teachers: Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi, Muhammad al-Ramli (author of Nihayat al-Muhtaj), and Ahmad ibn Qasim al-Abbadi (author of al-Ayat al-Bayyinat on al-Waraqat). Next are his Hanafi teachers: Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi, Shams Muhammad al-Nahrirri, and Umar ibn Nujaym (a prolific author in Hanafi fiqh). Then his Sufi masters: Ahmad al-Bulqini al-Waziri, Muhammad ibn al-Turjuman, and Ahmad Arab al-Sharnubi, along with many others. The passage concludes by noting that al-Laqqani himself stated that he did not study extensively with any teacher as much as he studied with Abu al-Naja Salim al-Sanhuri, followed by Muhammad al-Bahnasi. The reason mentioned is that al-Sanhuri would complete a major hadith book every three years, studying intensely during the months of Rajab, Sha'ban, and Ramadan both day and night. Then it mentions another teacher, Yahya al-Qarafi al-Maliki, who was a prominent hadith scholar and head of a riwaq (residential hall) at al-Azhar. This enumeration shows the breadth of al-Laqqani's education across multiple schools and disciplines.

الشافعية
الحنفية
الصوفية
السنهوري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Laqqani studied only within one madhhab.
Correction: He actually studied under teachers from the Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanafi schools and Sufi path.

Checkpoint

B) Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi
C) Abu al-Naja Salim al-Sanhuri
D) Ahmad al-Bulqini al-Waziri

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Laqqani's education was broad, spanning multiple madhhabs and Sufi orders, with his most significant teacher being Abu al-Naja al-Sanhuri.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Imam al-Laqqani's Students: A Legacy of Scholars
Listing of his prominent students and a statement about their large number.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam al-Laqqani was a central teacher whose students included many prominent scholars, reflecting the widespread influence of his knowledge.

Core Idea
Imam al-Laqqani taught the scholars of his era, leaving a legacy of multiple notable students.

This lesson explores the list of Imam al-Laqqani's students as recorded in his biography. The passage names several individuals and emphasizes that he had more students than any other scholar of his time. Understanding this helps appreciate his role in transmitting Islamic knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the names
Read the Arabic list and its translation. Notice the varied geographical origins of the students.
2
Reflect on the significance
Consider what it means for a scholar to have many students. How does this reflect his teaching influence? The passage says he was unmatched in number of students among his contemporaries.
3
Check your understanding
Use the quiz to test recall of the names and avoid the common misunderstanding that only his son was notable.

Source Text

تلاميذه أخذ عنه الكثير من الأجلاء منهم ولده عبد السلام، والشمس البابلي، والعلاء الشَّبْرَامَسِي، ويوسف الفيشي، وياسين العليمي الحمصي، وحسين النماوي، وحسين الخفاجي وأحمد العجمي، ومحمد الخرشي المالكي، وغيرهم ممن لا يحصون كثرة ، ولم يكن أحد من علماء عصره أكثر تلامذة منه .

And there was no one among the scholars of his time who had more students than him.]
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a list of Imam al-Laqqani's notable students (talamidh). It names several distinct individuals: his own son Abd al-Salam, Shams al-Babili, al-Ala al-Shabramallisi, Yusuf al-Fayshi, Yasin al-Ulaymi al-Himsi, Husayn al-Namawi, Husayn al-Khafaji, Ahmad al-Ajami, and Muhammad al-Kharshi al-Maliki. It then adds that there were many others beyond counting. The passage concludes by stating that al-Laqqani was unmatched among the scholars of his time in the number of his students. This highlights his central role as a teacher and the wide dissemination of his knowledge.

Al-Laqani's Diverse Teachers
Lists al-Laqani's teachers from Shafi'i, Hanafi, and Sufi disciplines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of al-Laqani's education through his teachers from the Maliki/Shafi'i, Hanafi, and Sufi traditions.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani studied with scholars from multiple madhhabs and the Sufi path.

This passage from al-Laqani's biography lists the distinguished scholars he studied with. It shows how his education spanned across different schools of thought and spiritual paths. As you read, note the variety and the respect he had for each teacher.

ترجمة صاحب المتن برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني شرح المنهاج، والعلامة الشيخ أحمد بن قاسم العبادي، صاحب الآيات البينات على الورقات، وغيرهم. ومن الحنفية شيخ الإسلام العلامة علي بن غانم المقدسي، والشمس محمد النحريري، والعلامة الشيخ عمر بن نجيم صاحب التصانيف في مذهب الحنفية. ومن مشايخه في طريق الصوفية: الشيخ أحمد البلقيني الوزيري، والشيخ محمد بن الترجمان، والشيخ أحمد عرب الشرنوبي، وجماعة كثيرة غيرهم. وذكر الإمام اللقاني أنه لم يكثر عن أحد منهم مثل ما أكثر عن الإمام الهمام أبي النجا سالم السنهوري ويليه الشيخ محمد البهنسي؛ لأنه كان يختم في كل ثلاث سنين كتابا من أمهات الحديث في رجب وشعبان ورمضان ليلا ونهارا ويليه الشيخ يحيى القرافي المالكي إمام الناس في الحديث تحريرا وإتقانا، شيخُ رواق ابن معمر بجامع الأزهر آنذاك.
Translation of the author Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani. [He studied with] the commentator on al-Minhaj, and the eminent Shaykh Ahmad ibn Qasim al-ʿAbbadi, author of al-Ayat al-Bayyinat on al-Waraqat, and others. Among the Hanafis: Shaykh al-Islam the eminent ʿAli ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi, and al-Shams Muhammad al-Nahriri, and the eminent Shaykh ʿUmar ibn Nujaym, author of works in the Hanafi school. Commentary

It then lists his Sufi shaykhs. Finally, it mentions Yahya al-Qarafi as an expert hadith scholar and head of a riwaq at al-Azhar.

Al-Laqani's Numerous Students
Lists al-Laqani's prominent students and notes his exceptional number of students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of al-Laqani's scholarly influence through the names and volume of his students.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani had more students than any scholar of his time.

This passage from the biographical introduction to Jawharat al-Tawhid highlights the extraordinary reach of al-Laqani's teaching. By naming several of his most prominent students and noting that his students were too many to count, the author establishes al-Laqani's central role in transmitting Islamic creed. As you read, notice how the list moves from his own son to other well-known scholars, ending with a powerful claim of his unmatched number of students.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of names
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the named students. Try to recognize the pattern: it begins with his son, then names several scholars with distinctive titles.
Many of these scholars were themselves influential teachers.
2
Notice the quantitative claim
The passage ends with two statements: 'others too many to count' and 'no scholar of his time had more students than him.' Ask yourself why this detail is important for establishing al-Laqani's authority.
3
Reflect on scholarly transmission
Consider how listing students serves as evidence of a teacher's impact. In traditional Islamic learning, the number and quality of one's students is a key measure of a scholar's legacy.
This connects to the broader theme of the sanad (chain of transmission) in Islamic knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلاميذه أخذ عنه الكثير من الأجلاء منهم ولده عبد السلام، والشمس البابلي، والعلاء الشَّبْرَامَسِي، ويوسف الفيشي، وياسين العليمي الحمصي، وحسين النماوي، وحسين الخفاجي وأحمد العجمي، ومحمد الخرشي المالكي، وغيرهم ممن لا يحصون كثرة، ولم يكن أحد من علماء عصره أكثر تلامذة منه.
His students: many eminent people studied with him, among them his son ʿAbd al-Salam, and al-Shams al-Babili, and al-ʿAlaʾ al-Shabramasi, and Yusuf al-Fishi, and Yasin al-ʿUlaymi al-Himsi, and Husayn al-Namawi, and Husayn al-Khafaji and Ahmad al-ʿAjami, and Muhammad al-Khurashi al-Maliki, and others too many to count, and there was no scholar of his time who had more students than him.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage lists al-Laqani's notable students. It begins with his own son, then names several well-known scholars such as al-Shams al-Babili and al-ʿAlaʾ al-Shabramasi. The passage emphasizes the vast number of his students by stating they cannot be counted and concludes that no contemporary scholar had as many students as he did.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is simply a random list of names with no significance.
Correction: The list is carefully chosen: starting with his son shows familial transmission, and the mention of various regional and scholarly titles demonstrates his wide influence. The quantitative claim at the end is a deliberate statement of his unmatched stature.

Al-Laqani had more students than any scholar of his time, including his own son. Is there even one person today who would consider you their teacher in something that truly matters for the Hereafter? If not, what are you doing to invest in someone else's faith right now?
?
The passage lists students from various regions and with diverse backgrounds. Are you intentionally seeking knowledge from a variety of teachers, or are you stuck in a comfortable bubble? Who is the last person you learned from who challenged your complacency?
?
Al-Laqani's students included many 'eminent' people. Given the weight of your influence on those around you, would those people be described as 'eminent' in their connection to the truth? What steps will you take this week to elevate those you influence?

Al-Laqani's Masterpieces: Jawharat al-Tawhid and Its Commentary
Describes al-Laqani's major works, especially Jawharat al-Tawhid and its commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of al-Laqani's Jawharat al-Tawhid and its major commentary, and appreciate the historical context of their composition.

Core Idea
Jawharat al-Tawhid: a poem composed in one night that became a cornerstone of Sunni theology.

This lesson introduces you to two of al-Laqani's most important works: his famous theological poem Jawharat al-Tawhid and its encyclopedic commentary 'Umdat al-Murid. These works represent a culmination of the Ash'ari theological tradition and remain widely studied today. The passage below presents remarkable stories about their composition and the scholarly devotion they inspired.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Laqani's works
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: it lists his works and then focuses on Jawharat al-Tawhid and its commentary.
The passage mentions two specific works with notable details.
2
Identify the key works
Identify Jawharat al-Tawhid and 'Umdat al-Murid. Note their roles and the stories surrounding their composition.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these works are so important: they are foundational texts in kalam and still studied today.
The commentary is described as an encyclopedia of kalam.

مؤلفاته: ألف اللقاني التآليف النافعة، في مختلف العلوم، ورغبَ الناس في استكتابها وقراءتها، وقد أكمل أكثرها له. فمن مؤلفاته التي أكملها ۱ - جوهرة التوحيد: منظومته الشهيرة في علم العقائد، وهي أنفع تآليفه وأشهرها، حُكي أنه أنشأها في ليلة بإشارة شيخه في التربية والتصوف صاحب المُكاشفات وخوارق العادات الشيخ أحمد عرب الشرنوبي، ثم إنه بعد فراغه منها عرضها على شيخه المذكور فحمده ودعا له ولمن يشتغل بها لمزيد النفع، وأوصاه شيخه المذكور: أن لا يعتذر لأحدٍ عن ذنبٍ أو عيب بلغه عنه، بل يعترف له به ويظهر له التصديق على سبيل التورية تركا لتزكية النَّفس؛ فما خالفه بعد ذلك أبدا. وحكي أنه كان شرع في إقراء المنظومة المذكورة فكتب منها في يومٍ واحد خمس مئة نسخة. وقد شرحها بثلاثة شروح كما سيأتي ذكره. ۲ - عمدة المريد الجوهرة التوحيد وهو أكبر شروحه على الجوهرة وأوسعها، وهو يعد موسوعة كلامية غنيا بالفوائد أكثر فيه من الاستدلال والمناقشات وانتهى من تأليفه سنة ۱۰۱۹هـ. وقد طبع أخيرا في دار الكتب العلمية، ثم طبع بعد ذلك بفترة قصيرة في دار النور المبين الأردنية مقابلا على أربع نسخ مخطوطة في أربع مجلدات بتحقيق مجموعة من الشيوخ وهم: الشيخ يوسف إدريس، والشيخ الدكتور جاد الله بسام صالح، والشيخ
His works: al-Laqani authored beneficial works in various sciences, and people desired to copy them and read them, and he completed most of them. Among his completed works: 1 - Jawharat al-Tawhid: his famous poem on theology, which is the most beneficial and most famous of his works. It is related that he composed it in one night upon the instruction of his spiritual and Sufi shaykh, the possessor of unveilings and extraordinary acts, Shaykh Ahmad ʿArab al-Sharnubi. Then, after finishing it, he presented it to that shaykh, who praised him and prayed for him and for those who would occupy themselves with it for increased benefit. That shaykh advised him: not to apologize to anyone for a sin or flaw that reached him about someone, but rather to acknowledge it and show him confirmation by way of dissimulation (tawriya), avoiding self-justification; so he never contradicted that after that. And it is related that when he began teaching this poem, he wrote five hundred copies of it in a single day. He wrote three commentaries on it, as will be mentioned. 2 - ʿUmdat al-Murid li-Jawharat al-Tawhid: which is his largest and most comprehensive commentary on al-Jawhara, and it is considered an encyclopedic work on kalam, rich in benefits, abundant in proofs and discussions. He completed its composition in the year 1019 AH. It was recently published by Dar al-Kutub al-ʿIlmiyya, then shortly after by Dar al-Nur al-Mubin in Jordan, collated from four manuscript copies in four volumes, edited by a group of shaykhs: Shaykh Yusuf Idris, Shaykh Dr. Jada Allah Bassam Salih, and Shaykh [unfinished].
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage describes al-Laqani's major works. It first notes that he wrote beneficial books in various fields. The first work listed is Jawharat al-Tawhid, his famous poem on theology. The passage provides several remarkable stories: it was composed in one night on the instruction of his Sufi teacher; after completion, his teacher praised him and prayed for those who study it; the teacher also advised him not to make excuses for others' faults but to use tawriya (dissimulation) to avoid self-praise, and al-Laqani never disobeyed that advice. Additionally, it is said that he wrote five hundred copies of the poem in one day when he began teaching it. The passage then mentions that he wrote three commentaries on it, and the second work described is ʿUmdat al-Murid, his largest commentary, which is a comprehensive kalam encyclopedia. It was completed in 1019 AH and has been recently published in two editions, with a critical edition based on four manuscripts. The list of editors is partially given.

Key Takeaway
Al-Laqani's Jawharat al-Tawhid, composed under divine inspiration in one night, and its commentary 'Umdat al-Murid, are foundational texts in Ash'ari theology.

Al-Laqqani's Major Works and Their Significance
List of al-Laqqani's works with anecdotes and descriptions.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani's works, especially Jawharat al-Tawhid, shaped Sunni creed for centuries.

Before diving into the theological content of Jawharat al-Tawhid, it is helpful to know its author and the scholarly tradition he represents. This passage from the commentary provides a biographical sketch of Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani, listing his major works. As you read, notice how the text emphasizes the popularity and influence of his poem, as well as the care he took in composing commentaries on it.

ترجمة صاحب المتن برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني
ألف اللقاني التآليف النافعة، في مختلف العلوم، ورغبَ الناس في استكتابها وقراءتها، وقد أكمل أكثرها له

۱ - جوهرة التوحيد»: منظومته الشهيرة في علم العقائد، وهي أنفع تآليفه وأشهرها ، حُكي أنه أنشأها في ليلة بإشارة شيخه في التربية والتصوف صاحب المُكاشفات وخوارق العادات الشيخ أحمد عرب الشرنوبي، ثم إنه بعد فراغه منها عرضها على شيخه المذكور فحمده ودعا له ولمن يشتغل بها لمزيد النفع ، وأوصاه شيخه المذكور : أن لا يعتذر لأحدٍ عن ذنبٍ أو عيب بلغه عنه ، بل يعترف له به ويظهر له التصديق على سبيل التورية تركا لتزكية النَّفس ؛ فما خالفه بعد ذلك أبدا.
وحكي أنه كان شرع في إقراء المنظومة المذكورة فكتب منها في يومٍ واحد خمس مئة نسخة . وقد شرحها بثلاثة شروح كما سيأتي ذكره . ۲ - (عمدة المريد الجوهرة التوحيد وهو أكبر شروحه على الجوهرة وأوسعها، وهو يعد موسوعة كلامية غنيا بالفوائد أكثر فيه من الاستدلال والمناقشات وانتهى من تأليفه سنة .۱۰۱۹هـ . وقد طبع أخيرا في دار الكتب العلمية ، ثم طبع بعد ذلك بفترة قصيرة في دار النور المبين الأردنية مقابلا على أربع نسخ مخطوطة في أربع مجلدات بتحقيق مجموعة من الشيوخ وهم: الشيخ يوسف إدريس، والشيخ الدكتور جاد الله بسام صالح، والشيخ عبد المنان الإدريسي، والقاضي بهاء الخلايلة، فجزاهم الله تعالى خيرا على إخراج على هذا الكتاب العظيم بصورة تليق به.
۳ - تلخيص التجريد لعمدة المريد» وهو شرحه الأوسط على الجوهرة حجما وتاريخا، قيل ألفه للشيخ المعروف بقاضي زاده ، وقيل لم يحرره ، ومنه نسخ مخطوطة كاملة بالأزهرية.
٤ - «هداية المريد الجوهرة التوحيد»: وهو شرحه الصغير على الجوهرة، وهو صغير بالنسبة لشرحي المؤلف الكبير والأوسط، أما بالنسبة لشروح غيره على الجوهرة بحواشيها فيعد بالنسبة لها كبيرا. وانتهى من تأليفه سنة ١٠٢٩هـ . وقد طبع وخرج إلى عالم المطبوعات عن دار البصائر في مجلدين كبيرين بتحقيق الشيخ الفاضل مروان البجاوي حفظه الله تعالى ، وهو تحقيق علمي رصين حلاه المحقق بوضع الحواشي المختلفة على الكتب من النسخ المخطوطة ، أسأل الله تعالى أن يجزي الشيخ مروان البجاوي خيرا على هذا العمل المتقن النافع وللكتاب طبعة أخرى عن دار المعارف اللبنانية في مجلد واحد .
ه - «قضاء الوطر من نزهة النظر في توضيح نخبة الفكر حاشية على شرح الحافظ ابن حجر على نخبته ، جمع فيها بين حاشية ابن قطلوبغا تلميذ ابن حجر ، وبين حاشية ابن أبي شريف ، فرغ في رمضان سنة ١٠٢٣هـ .
منه
- إجمال الوسائل وبهجة المحافل بالتعريف برواة الشمائل .
- منار أصول الفتوى وقواعد الإفتاء بالأقوى».
His works:
Translation of the author Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani
Al-Laqqani authored beneficial works, in various sciences, and people desired to write them down and read them, and he completed most of them.
Among his works that he completed:
1. 'Jawharat al-Tawhid': his famous poem in the science of beliefs, and it is the most beneficial of his works and the most famous. It is narrated that he composed it in one night at the indication of his shaykh in spiritual training and Sufism, the possessor of unveilings and extraordinary habits, Shaykh Ahmad Arab al-Sharnubi. Then after finishing it, he presented it to the aforementioned shaykh, who praised him and prayed for him and for whoever occupies himself with it for increased benefit. And his aforementioned shaykh advised him: not to apologize to anyone for a sin or defect that had been reported about him, but rather to acknowledge it to him and show him agreement by way of dissimulation, leaving aside self-justification. So he never opposed him after that at all. And it is narrated that he began teaching the aforementioned poem, and five hundred copies of it were written in one day. And he explained it with three commentaries as will be mentioned.
2. 'Umdat al-Murid 'ala Jawharat al-Tawhid' – it is his largest commentary on al-Jawhara and its most comprehensive, and it is considered a kalam encyclopedia rich in benefits, containing much argumentation and discussion. He finished composing it in the year 1019 AH. It was recently printed in Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya, then after a short period it was printed in Dar al-Nur al-Mubin in Jordan, collated against four manuscript copies in four volumes, edited by a group of shaykhs: Shaykh Yusuf Idris, Shaykh Dr. Jada Allah Bassam Salih, Shaykh Abd al-Mannan al-Idrisi, and Judge Baha' al-Khalayila. May Allah reward them for producing this great book in a manner befitting it.
3. 'Talkhis al-Tajrid li-Umdat al-Murid' – it is his middle commentary on al-Jawhara in size and date. It is said he wrote it for the shaykh known as Qadi Zada, and it is said he did not revise it. There are complete manuscript copies in al-Azhar.
4. 'Hidayat al-Murid ila Jawharat al-Tawhid' – it is his small commentary on al-Jawhara, and it is small compared to the author's large and middle commentaries. However, compared to others' commentaries on al-Jawhara with their glosses, it is considered large. He finished composing it in the year 1029 AH. It has been printed and emerged into the world of publications from Dar al-Basa'ir in two large volumes, edited by the virtuous Shaykh Marwan al-Bajjawi. It is a solid scholarly edition; the editor adorned it by placing various glosses from the manuscript copies. I ask Allah to reward Shaykh Marwan al-Bajjawi for this proficient beneficial work. The book also has another edition from Dar al-Ma'arif al-Lubnaniyya in one volume.
5. 'Qada' al-Watar min Nuzhat al-Nazar fi Tawdih Nukhbat al-Fikr' – a gloss on the commentary of al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar on his Nukhba, in which he combined the gloss of Ibn Qutlubugha, a student of Ibn Hajar, and the gloss of Ibn Abi Sharif. He completed it in Ramadan of the year 1023 AH.
From them:
- Ijmal al-Wasa'il wa-Bahjat al-Mahafil bi-l-Ta'rif bi-Ruwat al-Shama'il.
- Manar Usul al-Fatwa wa-Qawa'id al-Ifta' bi-l-Aqwa.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of the works of Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani, the author of the poem Jawharat al-Tawhid. It begins by stating that al-Laqqani authored beneficial works in various sciences and that people eagerly sought to copy and read them. It then lists his completed works, starting with his most famous, Jawharat al-Tawhid. A story is told about its composition: he wrote it in one night at the suggestion of his Sufi shaykh, Ahmad al-Sharnubi, who praised it and prayed for al-Laqqani and future students of the poem. The shaykh also gave him a piece of spiritual advice: never to deny a sin or fault reported about him, but to acknowledge it with ta'riya (dissimulation), avoiding self-justification. Al-Laqqani adhered to this. The poem spread rapidly; five hundred copies were handwritten in a single day when he taught it. He later wrote three commentaries on it. Next, the passage describes his largest commentary, 'Umdat al-Murid, completed in 1019 AH, a comprehensive kalam encyclopedia. It was recently printed in scholarly editions. The middle commentary, Talkhis al-Tajrid, is described as medium in size, possibly written for Qadi Zada, with manuscripts in al-Azhar. The small commentary, Hidayat al-Murid, completed in 1029 AH, is small compared to al-Laqqani's own works but large relative to other commentaries. It was printed by Dar al-Basa'ir in two volumes. Then two additional works are mentioned: a gloss on Ibn Hajar's Nukhbat al-Fikr (completed 1023 AH), and two other works (Ijmal al-Wasa'il and Manar Usul al-Fatwa). This passage is purely informative and contains no doctrinal arguments; it serves to establish the author's scholarly output and the significance of Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Readers might expect this passage to contain theological doctrine from Jawharat al-Tawhid.
Correction: This passage is purely biographical; it provides background on the author and his works, not creedal content.

Key Takeaway
Al-Laqqani's Jawharat al-Tawhid and its three commentaries form the core of his legacy, and his other works demonstrate his broad scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

نصيحة الإخوان باجتناب شرب الدخان» ، وقد عارضها معاصره
الشيخ علي بن محمد الأجهوري المالكي برسالة أولى وثانية أثبت فيهما القول بحل شربه ما لم يضر .
١٠ - تحفة ذُريَّة سيدي علي أبهلول بأسانيد جوامع أحاديث الرسول» وهي رسالة في إجازة حديثية. طبع في دار التوفيقية المسيلة الجزائر، مع

۱۱ ـ كشف الكروب لملاقاة الحبيب والتوسل بالمحبوب»: منظومة
في التوسل بالنبي .
Biography of the author Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani. Abd al-Mannan al-Idrisi and Judge Baha' al-Khalayila, may Allah reward them well for bringing out this great book in a manner befitting it. 3 – 'Talkhis al-Tajrid li-'Umdat al-Murid' which is his medium commentary on al-Jawhara in size and date. It is said he wrote it for the scholar known as Qadi Zada, and it is said he did not finalize it. It has complete manuscript copies in al-Azhariyya. 4 – 'Hidayat al-Murid li-Jawharat al-Tawhid': it is his small commentary on al-Jawhara, small relative to the author's large and medium commentaries, but relative to others' commentaries on al-Jawhara with their glosses it is considered large. He finished its composition in the year 1029 AH. It has been printed and entered the world of publications by Dar al-Basa'ir in two large volumes, edited by the virtuous shaykh Marwan al-Bajawi, may Allah preserve him, and it is a sound scholarly edition; the editor adorned it by placing various glosses from manuscript copies. I ask Allah to reward Shaykh Marwan al-Bajawi well for this precise beneficial work. The book also has another edition by Dar al-Ma'arif al-Lubnaniyya in one volume. 5 – 'Qada' al-Watar min Nuzhat al-Nazar fi Tawdih Nukhbat al-Fikr: a gloss on the commentary of al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar on his Nukhba, in which he combined the gloss of Ibn Qutlubugha, student of Ibn Hajar, and the gloss of Ibn Abi Sharif. He finished it in Ramadan of the year 1023 AH. From him: 'Ijmal al-Wasa'il wa Bahjat al-Mahafil bi-l-Ta'rif bi-Ruwat al-Shama'il.' 'Manar Usul al-Fatwa wa Qawa'id al-Ifta' bi-l-Aqwa.' 8 – 'Iqd al-Juman fi Masa'il al-Daman.' 9 – 'Nasihah al-Ikhwan bi-Ijtinab Shurb al-Dukhan,' and his contemporary Shaykh Ali ibn Muhammad al-Ujhuri al-Maliki opposed it with a first and second treatise affirming the opinion about its permissibility as long as it does not cause harm. 10 – 'Tuhfat Dhurriyyat Sayyidi Ali Abhilul bi-Asanid Jawami' Ahadith al-Rasul,' which is a treatise on hadith license (ijaza). Printed in Dar al-Tawfiqiyya al-Masila, Algeria, with other collections of licenses edited by Mustafa Dayf in the year 1433 AH. 11 – 'Kashf al-Kurub li-Mulaqat al-Habib wa al-Tawassul bi-l-Mahbub': a poem on seeking intercession through the Prophet.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage begins the biography of the author, Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani. It opens with thanks to those who contributed to the edition of the book. Then it enumerates his completed works. The first work listed is 'Talkhis al-Tajrid li-'Umdat al-Murid', described as his medium commentary on his own poem al-Jawhara. It mentions uncertainty about its authorship and the existence of manuscripts. The second is 'Hidayat al-Murid li-Jawharat al-Tawhid', his small commentary on the same poem, noting its size relative to his other commentaries and to others' works, its completion date, and its printed editions with scholarly editing. The third is 'Qada' al-Watar min Nuzhat al-Nazar', a gloss on Ibn Hajar's commentary on his Nukhba, combining two earlier glosses. Two additional works without numbers follow: 'Ijmal al-Wasa'il' and 'Manar Usul al-Fatwa'. Then numbered works resume: 'Iqd al-Juman' on guaranty issues, 'Nasihah al-Ikhwan' defending the prohibition of smoking along with a rebuttal by al-Ujhuri, 'Tuhfat Dhurriyyat Sayyidi Ali Abhilul' a hadith license treatise, and 'Kashf al-Kurub' a poem on seeking intercession through the Prophet. The passage thus provides a comprehensive list with brief descriptions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The missing numbers 1,2,6,7 mean those works are lost.
Correction: The list is selective; only some of his works are enumerated here, not all.

Al-Laqqani's Four Incomplete Works
Lists al-Laqqani's four incomplete works with descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four incomplete works of al-Laqqani and understand their scope from the brief descriptions provided.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani left four major works unfinished, each a commentary or gloss on key texts.

In addition to his completed works, al-Laqqani authored several projects that remained incomplete. This passage from the biographical note lists four such works, giving a glimpse into his scholarly interests and the scope of his unfinished labor. Studying these titles helps us appreciate the breadth of his ambition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic list carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, noting each numbered work. Pay attention to the titles and the descriptive phrases following each.
The list uses hyphens and numbers; it is straightforward.
2
Identify the pattern among the works
Notice that three of the four works are commentaries or glosses (حاشية) on other texts. Consider what this suggests about al-Laqqani's scholarly method.
The fourth work, 'Nathr al-Ma'athir', is a biographical compilation.
3
Recognize the special mention of al-Sa'd
The second work includes a remark about al-Laqqani's great interest in al-Sa'd. Understand that this shows his admiration and frequent citation of al-Sa'd's works.
Al-Sa'd is likely Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani.
4
Reflect on the significance of incomplete works
Consider what the existence of these incomplete manuscripts tells us about al-Laqqani's scholarly output and the state of his legacy.
Incomplete works are often valuable for understanding an author's unfinished projects.

And from his works that were not completed: 1 – 'Ta'liq al-Fara'id 'ala Sharh al-'Aqa'id li-l-Sa'd': he commented on a large portion of it amounting to 237 folios, manuscript in Dar al-Kutub (1272) Ilm Kalam. 2 – 'Khulasat al-Ta'rif bi-Daqa'iq Sharh al-Tasrif': it is a gloss on Sharh al-Tasrif al-'Izzi li-l-Sa'd, and it is clear that al-Shaykh al-Laqqani had great interest in al-'Allama al-Sa'd and his books, and he was worthy of this, so that you find him frequently quoting from him in his books, describing him with attributes of veneration and deference, saying 'al-Sa'd, may Allah make him happy, etc.' 3 – 'Al-Budur al-Lawami' min Khudur Jam' al-Jawami': a gloss on al-Mahalli's commentary on Jam' al-Jawami'. 4 – 'Nathr al-Ma'athir fi-man Adraka min al-Qarn al-'Ashir': it is a part he compiled about...

Commentary
This passage lists the works of al-Laqqani that remained incomplete. Four works are mentioned. The first is 'Ta'liq al-Fara'id', a commentary on al-Sa'd's Sharh al-'Aqa'id, of which a large portion (237 folios) is extant in manuscript. The second is 'Khulasat al-Ta'rif', a gloss on al-Sa'd's Sharh al-Tasrif al-'Izzi, and the author notes al-Laqqani's particular fondness for studying al-Sa'd's works. The third is 'Al-Budur al-Lawami', a gloss on al-Mahalli's commentary on Jam' al-Jawami'. The fourth is 'Nathr al-Ma'athir', a biographical work about scholars of the tenth century. The list ends with the indication that these were not completed.

Biography of Al-Laqqani: His Works and Death
Biographical entry listing the author's works and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly works of Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani and the circumstances of his death.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani's legacy includes many works on fiqh, hadith, and theology, both completed and unfinished.

This biographical passage introduces the author of the matn, listing his key writings and his death. Understanding the author's scholarly output gives context to his theological poem. The passage also notes his admiration for al-Sa'd, a prominent scholar, helping situate al-Laqqani within the intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation. Notice that the passage is divided into completed works, unfinished works, and death.
The passage uses numbered lists for works.
2
Identify the two categories of works
The passage first lists completed works (numbers 8-11) and then works that were not completed (numbers 1-4). Note the titles and subjects.
The unfinished works include a large gloss on al-Sa'd's commentary.
3
Reflect on al-Laqqani's scholarly interests
The passage remarks on his great interest in the scholar al-Sa'd. Find where this is mentioned and consider why this matters.
4
Read the account of his death
The final part tells how and when he died, and includes a poetic elegy. Note the details of his burial place.
His death year is 1041 AH, the same year as al-Maqqari.

١٠ - تحفة ذُريَّة سيدي علي أبهلول بأسانيد جوامع أحاديث الرسول» وهي رسالة في إجازة حديثية. طبع في دار التوفيقية المسيلة الجزائر، مع مجموعة رسائل أخرى في الإجازات بتحقيق مصطفى ضيف في سنة : ١٤٣٣هـ .

۱ - تعليق الفرائد على شرح العقائد للسعد»: وقد شرح منها قطعة كبيرة تبلغ ٢٣٧ لوحة ، مخطوط بدار الكتب (۱۲۷۲) علم كلام . ٢ - خلاصة التعريف بدقائق شرح التصريف»: وهو حاشية على شرح التصريف العزي للسعد ومن الواضح أن للشيخ اللقاني مزيد اهتمام بالعلامة السعد وكتبه، وهو حري بهذا، حتى أنك تجده في كتبه يكثر من النقل عنه واصفا إياه بصفات التبجيل والتدليل ، فقال السعد أسعده الله إلخ.

وفاته

توفي - ـ وهو راجع من الحج سنة إحدى وأربعين وألف ، ودفن بالقُرب من عقبة أيلة بطريق الركب المصري ، وفي هذه السنة توفي الحافظ الكبير أبي العباس أحمد المقري المالكي صاحب (النفح الطيب) و(نسيم الرياض) و (إضاءة الدَّجُنَّة) ، وقال فيهما ابن محب الدين الدمشقي يرثيهما: مَضى المَقْرِيُّ إبراهيم اللقاني لاحقا إمامان ما للدَّهرِ بعدهُمَا خَلف فبدرُ الدُّجى أجرى على الخَدِّ دمعَهُ فأثَرَ ذاكَ الدَّمعُ ما فيه من كلف
Translation of the author of the text, Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani.

8 - 'Iqd al-Juman fi Masa'il al-Daman' .

9 - 'Nasiha al-Ikhwan fi Ijtinab Shurb al-Dukhan' , and his contemporary Sheikh Ali ibn Muhammad al-Ujhuri al-Maliki opposed it with a first and second treatise in which he affirmed the opinion of its permissibility as long as it does not cause harm.

10 - 'Tuhfa Dhurriyya Sayyidi Ali Abahlul bi-Asanid Jawami' Ahadith al-Rasul' , and it is a treatise in hadith license. Printed in Dar al-Tawfiqiyya al-Masila, Algeria, with another collection of works on licenses edited by Mustafa Diyab in the year 1433 AH.

11 - 'Kashf al-Kurub li-Mulaqat al-Habib wa al-Tawassul bi-al-Mahbub' : a poem on seeking intercession through the Prophet.

And from his works that were not completed:

1 - 'Ta'liq al-Fara'id 'ala Sharh al-'Aqa'id li-al-Sa'd' : and he explained from it a large portion amounting to 237 folios, manuscript in Dar al-Kutub (1272) 'ilm kalam. 2 - 'Khulasa al-Ta'rif bi-Daqa'iq Sharh al-Tasrif' : and it is a gloss on the commentary 'Sharh al-Tasrif al-'Izzi' by al-Sa'd, and it is clear that Sheikh al-Laqqani had great interest in the scholar al-Sa'd and his books, and he was worthy of this, so that you find him frequently quoting him and describing him with attributes of veneration and deference, saying 'al-Sa'd, may God make him successful, etc.'

- 3 - 'al-Budur al-Lawami' min Khudur Jam' al-Jawami' : a gloss on al-Mahalli's commentary on 'Jam' al-Jawami' .

4 - 'Nathr al-Ma'athir fi-man Adrak min al-Qarn al-'Ashir' : and it is a part in which he collected his teachers whom he encountered among the notable figures of the tenth century.

His death.

He died - while returning from Hajj in the year one thousand and forty-one, and was buried near the 'Aqaba of Aylah on the route of the Egyptian caravan. In this year died the great memorizer Abi al-'Abbas Ahmad al-Maqqari al-Maliki, author of (al-Nafh al-Tayyib) and (Nasim al-Riyad) and (Ida'at al-Dujunna). Ibn Muhibb al-Din al-Dimashqi said in elegy for them both: 'Al-Maqqari passed, Ibrahim al-Laqqani followed, two imams, after whom time has no replacement. So the full moon shed upon the cheek its tear, and the trace of that tear remains as a blemish.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on the author, Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqqani. It begins by naming him and then lists his completed works numbered 8 through 11: 'Iqd al-Juman fi Masa'il al-Daman' on guaranty issues; 'Nasiha al-Ikhwan fi Ijtinab Shurb al-Dukhan' on smoking, noting that a contemporary scholar opposed it; 'Tuhfa Dhurriyya Sayyidi Ali Abahlul bi-Asanid Jawami' Ahadith al-Rasul' on hadith licenses, with publication details; and 'Kashf al-Kurub li-Mulaqat al-Habib wa al-Tawassul bi-al-Mahbub', a poem on seeking intercession. Then it lists his unfinished works: a gloss on al-Sa'd's commentary on al-'Aqa'id, a gloss on al-Sa'd's commentary on al-Tasrif al-'Izzi (noting his admiration for al-Sa'd), a gloss on al-Mahalli's commentary on Jam' al-Jawami', and a collection of biographies of his teachers from the 10th century. Finally, it records his death in 1041 AH on return from Hajj, burial near Aqaba of Aylah, and mentions that the famous scholar al-Maqqari died the same year, along with a poetic elegy by Ibn Muhibb al-Din al-Dimashqi.

Biography of the Commentator Abd al-Salam al-Laqani
Biography of the commentator, his birth, education, and teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly journey of Abd al-Salam al-Laqani, the commentator of Jawharat al-Tawhid, and his relationship with his father.

Core Idea
A son's reform after his father's death: from youthful folly to scholarly legacy.

The success of a scholarly text often rests on the shoulders of its commentators. Abd al-Salam al-Laqani, the son of the original author, not only inherited his father's knowledge but also his teaching position at al-Azhar. This lesson traces his early years, his father's deep affection, and the transformative power of a parent's prayers.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully to get an overview of al-Laqani's life.
Notice the father's role in his education.
2
Identify key events
Identify his birth year, his teachers, his father's reaction to complaints, and his taking over the teaching position.
3
Reflect on the father's approach
Consider how the father's prayers and lack of rebuke shaped al-Laqani's eventual transformation.
This shows the importance of patience and dua.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمةُ صاحب الشرح ابن النَّاظم الشيخ عبد السلام اللقاني اسمه ونسبه: هو الشيخ عبد السلام بن إبراهيم اللقاني بن إبراهيم بن حسن بن علي بن علي اللقاني المصري، شيخ المالكية في وقته، حيث خلف والده في مجلس الدرس في الجامع الأزهر. مولده، وطلبه للعلم، وتصدره للتدريس ولد سنة (٩٧١ هـ) ولازم والده في العلوم الشرعية والعقلية، وقرأ بالرّوايات على مقرئ مصر في عصره الشيخ عبد الرحمن اليمني . ورِثَ مِن علوم والده طريفَه ،وتالِدَه ، وكان والده كثير الشغف به، والشفقة عليه، والمحبّة له ، والإشارة إليه ، وكانَ مُقرئ درس والده، ولا يُمكِّنُ أحدًا مِن القراءة بدله ، وإذا شَكاه أحدٌ إلى والده العلامة مما كان يصدر في عُنفوان شبابه .. يُكثر والده الدُّعاء له، ولا يُعنفه في خروجه عن الطاعة ، واستجاب الله لدعوات والده الصالح فظهر أثر دعائه له، خصوصا بعد موت والده، فترك كل شيء وسار بسيرته، وتصدر للتدريس بالجامع الأزهر مكان والده ، وحضر مجلسه غالب تلامذة والده ، وانتفع به خلقٌ كثير منه
Translation of the commentator, the son of the author, Shaykh Abd al-Salam al-Laqani. His name and lineage: He is Shaykh Abd al-Salam ibn Ibrahim al-Laqani ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ali al-Laqani al-Misri, the shaykh of the Malikis in his time, as he succeeded his father in the teaching circle at al-Azhar Mosque. His birth, his pursuit of knowledge, and his assuming the position of teaching: He was born in the year 971 AH. He closely accompanied his father in the religious and rational sciences, and recited with the various recitations under the reciter of Egypt in his time, Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Yamani. He inherited from his father's sciences both the novel and the ancient. His father was very fond of him, compassionate toward him, loved him, and pointed to him (as his successor). He was the reader of his father's lesson and did not allow anyone else to read in his place. If someone complained to his father, the scholar, about what he did in the rashness of his youth, his father would pray much for him and not rebuke him for his disobedience. Allah answered the prayers of his righteous father, so the effect of his prayers appeared for him, especially after his father's death. He left everything and followed his conduct, and assumed the teaching position at al-Azhar Mosque in place of his father. Most of his father's students attended his circle, and many people benefited from him.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the commentator, Abd al-Salam al-Laqani, son of the author. It begins with his full name and lineage, emphasizing that he was the leading Maliki scholar of his time and succeeded his father as teacher at al-Azhar. Then it details his birth (971 AH), his close study with his father in both religious and rational sciences, and his study of Quranic recitations under Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Yamani. It highlights his father's special affection for him, making him the reader of his lessons and not allowing anyone else. Despite any youthful indiscretions, his father only prayed for him rather than rebuking. After his father's death, he reformed himself, followed his father's path, and took over teaching at al-Azhar. Most of his father's students attended his lessons, and many benefited from him.

ابن الناظم
الجامع الأزهر

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

The Life and Legacy of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani
Biography of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani with name, birth, education, qualities, and praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key stages of Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani's life, his scholarly lineage, and the qualities that made him a respected Maliki scholar and commentator.

Core Idea
A scholar's life reflects the legacy of his father and the grace of answered prayers.

This passage introduces us to Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, the son and commentator of the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid. Understanding his biography helps us appreciate the context of the commentary and the scholarly tradition from which it emerged. As we read, we will see how his father's prayers shaped his transformation and how he became a leading figure in his own right.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three main sections: name and lineage, birth and education, qualities and praise.
The passage is detailed; don't worry about memorizing every name.
2
Trace his inheritance from his father
Identify how al-Laqqani inherited both knowledge and position from his father, and how his father's prayers affected his life.
This is a key theme: the power of a righteous parent's supplication.
3
Examine his teaching style and qualities
Reflect on the descriptions of his demeanor in class and his limited teaching schedule. Why might he have chosen to teach only three months?
Consider the two interpretations mentioned: asceticism vs. idleness.
4
Review the scholars' praise
Look at what his student al-Hamawi and others said about him. What fields of knowledge did they highlight?
This confirms his expertise in hadith, fiqh, kalam, and Arabic sciences.

ترجمة صاحب الشرح ابن الناظم الشيخ عبد السلام اللقاني
اسمه ونسبه:
هو الشيخ عبد السلام بن إبراهيم اللقاني بن إبراهيم بن حسن بن علي بن علي اللقاني المصري، شيخ المالكية في وقته، حيث خلف والده في مجلس الدرس في الجامع الأزهر.
مولده، وطلبه للعلم، وتصدره للتدريس
ولد سنة (٩٧١ هـ) ولازم والده في العلوم الشرعية والعقلية، وقرأ بالرّوايات على مقرئ مصر في عصره الشيخ عبد الرحمن اليمني .
ورِثَ مِن علوم والده طريفَه ،وتالِدَه ، وكان والده كثير الشغف به، والشفقة عليه، والمحبّة له ، والإشارة إليه ، وكانَ مُقرئ درس والده، ولا يُمكِّنُ أحدًا مِن القراءة بدله ، وإذا شَكاه أحدٌ إلى والده العلامة مما كان يصدر في عُنفوان شبابه .. يُكثر والده الدُّعاء له، ولا يُعنفه في خروجه عن الطاعة ، واستجاب الله لدعوات والده الصالح فظهر أثر دعائه له، خصوصا بعد موت والده، فترك كل شيء وسار بسيرته، وتصدر للتدريس بالجامع الأزهر مكان والده ، وحضر مجلسه غالب تلامذة والده ، وانتفع به خلقٌ كثير .
من أوصافه
كان ذا شهامة وله شدة وهيبة ، وكان كبار المشايخ من أهل وقته يحترمون ساحته ويُقدِّرونَ رأيه ، وكان مجللاً مُهابا عند العلماء فمَن دونهم، مع حُسن عشرته ورقيق طبعه والناس في درسه كأن على رؤوسهم الطير، فلا يقدر أحدٌ مِن الحاضرين أن يسأله أو يرُدَّ عليه ؛ هيبةً له ، وإذا تكلم في مسألةٍ يُملي عليها جميع ما ذكر من الكلام عليها ، وإذا أورد بحثا لا يُبقي فيها ولا يذر . الشيخ العياشي واصفا له غلب عليه حبُّ الانفراد، والتفور من العباد، فمن قائل: إنّ ذلك تَنَسُّكُ وزهادةٌ ، ومن قائل: بطالة ومَلالةٌ : والصحيح - إن شاء الله - الأول ، فكان لا يُدَرِّسُ إِلَّا في الشهور الثلاثة: رجب ، وتَالِيَيْه ، وغالب تدريسه فيها الحديث وما يشبهه .
مدح العلماء له:
قال عنه تلميذه العلامة مصطفى بن فتح الله الحموي في ترجمته له: شيخنا الإمام، شيخ المحدثين بالديار المصرية، كان ماهرا في الحديث، ومعرفة علله ورجاله فقيها في مذهبه، إماما في علم الكلام والفنون العربية ، دَمِثَ الأخلاق ، حَسنَ المُذاكرة بديع المُحاضرة .
وذكره الشيخ عبد الله العياشي في رحلته فقال: هو وارث علوم أبيه، والفذُ مِن أصحابه، الذي ليس له شبيه.
وقال عنه المُحبي الحافظ المتقن الفهامة ، شيخ المالكية في وقته بالقاهرة.
وقال عنه العلامة شهاب الدين أحمد الملوي: الرّحلة الإمام والعمدة
Biography of the author of the commentary, Ibn al-Nazim, Sheikh Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani:
His name and lineage:
He is Sheikh Abd al-Salam ibn Ibrahim al-Laqqani ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ali al-Laqqani al-Misri, the foremost Malikite scholar of his time, as he succeeded his father in the teaching circle (majlis) at al-Azhar Mosque.
His birth, his pursuit of knowledge, and his assumption of teaching:
He was born in the year (971 AH) and adhered to his father in the religious and rational sciences, and he recited (qara'a) with the recitations (riwayat) under the reciter (muqri') of Egypt in his time, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Yamani.
He inherited from his father's sciences both the novel and the ancient, and his father was very fond of him, compassionate toward him, loving him, and pointing to him (as his successor). He was the reciter (muqri') of his father's lesson, and he would not allow anyone else to read in his place. If someone complained to his father the scholar about something he did in the recklessness of his youth, his father would pray much for him and not reprimand him for leaving obedience. Allah answered the prayers of his righteous father, and the effect of his father's supplication appeared, especially after his father's death. He left everything and followed his path, and he sat for teaching at al-Azhar Mosque in his father's place. Most of his father's students attended his circle, and many people benefited from him.
Of his qualities:
He was possessed of honor and had strength and awe. The great scholars of his time respected his standing and valued his opinion. He was majestic and awe-inspiring among the scholars and those below them, with good companionship and delicate nature. The people in his lesson were as if birds were on their heads (in stillness); no one among the attendees could ask him or respond to him out of awe. When he spoke on a matter, he would dictate all that was said about it, and when he raised a research topic, he left nothing undiscussed. Sheikh al-Ayyashi described him as having been overcome by love of seclusion and aversion to people. Some said that was devotion and asceticism, and others said it was idleness and boredom. The correct view - Allah willing - is the first. He would only teach in the three months: Rajab and its two successors, and most of his teaching in them was hadith and similar subjects.
Praise of the scholars for him:
His student, the scholar Mustafa ibn Fathallah al-Hamawi, said in his biography of him: 'Our teacher the imam, the foremost of hadith scholars in the Egyptian lands. He was skilled in hadith, knowledge of its defects and transmitters, a jurist in his school, a leader in the science of kalam and the Arabic arts, gentle in character, excellent in discussion, splendid in lecture.'
And Sheikh Abd Allah al-Ayyashi mentioned him in his journey (rihla) and said: 'He is the inheritor of his father's sciences, and the unique one among his companions, who has no peer.'
And al-Muhibbi said about him: 'The exacting, discerning memorizer, the foremost Malikite scholar of his time in Cairo.'
And the scholar Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Mallawi said about him: 'The journey (al-rihla), the imam, the pillar.'
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a biography (tarjama) of Sheikh Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, the son of the author of the original text (Ibn al-Nazim), who wrote the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid. It is divided into three parts: his name and lineage, his birth and education, and his qualities along with praise from scholars.

First, his name and lineage: His full name is Abd al-Salam ibn Ibrahim al-Laqqani, tracing back to al-Laqqani, of Egyptian origin. He was the leading Maliki scholar of his time, succeeding his father in the teaching chair at al-Azhar Mosque.

Second, his birth and education: He was born in 971 AH. He studied both religious and rational sciences under his father, and also learned the various Quranic recitations from Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Yamani, the chief reciter of Egypt. His father was extremely fond of him and showed him special favor: he was the only one allowed to recite in his father's lessons. Even when others complained about the son's youthful indiscretions, the father did not rebuke him but prayed for him. After his father's death, those prayers bore fruit: Abd al-Salam reformed completely, adopted his father's path, and took over his teaching position at al-Azhar, benefiting many students, including most of his father's former students.

Third, his qualities and scholarly praise: The biography describes him as honorable, stern, and awe-inspiring, yet good-natured and gentle. In his lessons, students were so still and silent that they seemed like birds with their heads motionless. He spoke with authority, covering every aspect of a topic. He preferred seclusion and only taught during three specific months: Rajab, Sha'ban, and Ramadan. Some interpreted this as asceticism, others as laziness; the author considers the first view correct, as his teaching in those months focused on hadith.

Finally, several scholars praise him: His student Mustafa al-Hamawi calls him a master of hadith, a jurist, and an expert in kalam and Arabic sciences. Al-Ayyashi calls him the inheritor of his father's knowledge with no peer. Al-Muhibbi and al-Mallawi also praise his excellence and leadership.

Key Terms
اللقاني
ابن الناظم
الجامع الأزهر
شيخ المالكية
ترجمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think his limited teaching schedule (only three months) indicates laziness or boredom.
Correction: The author clarifies that the correct view is that it was due to devotion and asceticism (tanasuk wa zahada), as supported by his focus on hadith and his overall character.

Checkpoint
What position did Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani inherit from his father?
A) The position of chief judge of Egypt
B) The teaching chair at al-Azhar Mosque
C) The office of mufti of the Maliki school
D) The leadership of the Sufi orders

Key Takeaway
Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani was a distinguished Maliki scholar who inherited his father's knowledge and position at al-Azhar, reformed by his father's prayers, and was praised for his expertise in hadith, fiqh, kalam, and Arabic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone you love makes mistakes, do you resort to reprimand or to prayer? Abd al-Salam's father prayed for him instead of scolding. Who in your life needs your prayers more than your criticism? Will you commit to praying for them daily for one week?
?
The scholars debated whether al-Laqqani's seclusion was asceticism or idleness, and the author affirms it was devotion. Is there an area in your life where you avoid people or work, and if so, is it for God or for yourself? What one step can you take this week to turn your solitude into sincere worship?
?
Al-Laqqani transformed completely after his father's death, leaving his former ways to follow his father's path. If you were told you had only a year to live, what habits and priorities would you immediately change? Why wait? What is the first concrete change you will make today?
