D) Monday, 10th Dhu al-Qa'dah 1231 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Amir al-Kabir was a gentle and sensitive scholar who passed away in 1232 AH, leaving behind a son who continued his scholarly legacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that al-Amir al-Kabir was 'tender-hearted' and 'gentle in temperament', and that imagination almost pained him. When was the last time you allowed your heart to be truly affected by something that did not directly trouble you? Is your soul sensitive enough to feel for others, or have you hardened it for comfort? What small step today could revive that sensitivity?
?
The passage describes a gradual decline: his strength weakened, his limbs became lax, his complaint increased, and illnesses followed in succession until death. Is there a legacy—a child, a student, a written work—that you are deliberately building now to serve the deen after you are gone?
?
Al-Amir left behind a son who became a scholar 'like his father'. Who will carry your knowledge, your character, and your service to Allah after you? If you have not intentionally invested in someone, why not? What would it take to begin that investment today, even in a small way?

Biography of the Great Amir (al-Amir al-Kabir), author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. 10 - He has a beneficial gloss on Mughni al-Labib. 11 - Sadd al-Arab min 'Ulw al-Isnad wa al-Adab, which is his thabat (list of teachers and works). 12 - A gloss on Sharh Shudhur al-Dhahab, and other beneficial books, glosses, and investigations, as we did not intend to list all his works in this brief and hasty biography. His Death: He was tender-hearted, of gentle temperament, his nature was disturbed without disturbance, imagination almost pained him, and hearing what is repugnant weakened and sickened him. In his later years, his strength weakened, his limbs became lax, his complaints increased, and he continued to ail while diseases followed him, and the caller of death did not cease until he died on Monday, the 10th of Dhu al-Qi'dah al-Haram of the year 1232 AH. He had a crowded funeral, and was buried in the desert near the burial of Shaykh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-'Afifi, near the building of Sultan Qaytbay. Grief and sorrow for him was great. He left behind his son, the erudite scholar Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Saghir, who was like his father, one of the prominent figures who gave lessons, benefited students, and attended high councils and assemblies. (1) Sources for the biography: Tarikh 'Aja'ib al-Athar by al-Jabarti, Sadd al-Arab min 'Ulw al-Isnad wa al-Adab which is the thabat of al-Allamah al-Amir, Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin, Fihris al-Faharis.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of al-Amir al-Kabir, the author of a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins by listing three of his works: a gloss on Mughni al-Labib, his thabat (a work listing his chains of transmission and readings) titled Sadd al-Arab, and a gloss on Sharh Shudhur al-Dhahab. The author notes that this list is not exhaustive. Then it describes his character: he was tender-hearted, with a delicate temperament, easily affected by imagination and repugnant sounds. Then it details his final illness, his death on Monday, 10 Dhu al-Qi'dah 1232 AH, his funeral, and burial near Shaykh 'Abd al-Wahhab al-'Afifi and Sultan Qaytbay's building. It mentions the widespread sorrow at his death and that he was survived by his son Muhammad al-Amir al-Saghir, who also became a scholar. Finally, a footnote gives sources for the biography.

Biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. Biography of the scholar Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Shanwani al-Shafi'i, the thirteenth Shaykh of al-Azhar al-Sharif, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. His name: Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Mansur al-Shanwani al-Shafi'i. Birth and lineage: Shaykh Muhammad al-Shanwani was born in the village of Shanwan al-Ghurf, Monufia Governorate, to which he is attributed. His upbringing and stages of education: He studied under many of the notable scholars of his time, including the shaykhs Faris, al-Sa'idi, al-Dardir, and al-Farmawi. He specialized in fiqh under Shaykh 'Isa al-Barawi, attended his lessons closely, and read under him. The shaykh gave him ijaza after giving him most of what he had, and was reassured of his knowledge, because Shaykh al-Shanwani - may God have mercy on him - was intelligent, astute, and had a good memory. So his teacher gave him special attention and distinguished him with himself due to his diligence and good manners. His ethics: Shaykh al-Shanwani was known for generosity, extreme modesty, and humility. Among his humility...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, the 13th Shaykh of al-Azhar and author of a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins by stating his full name: Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Mansur al-Shanwani al-Shafi'i. He was born in the village of Shanwan al-Ghurf in Monufia, Egypt. His education: he studied under several shaykhs including Faris, al-Sa'idi, al-Dardir, al-Farmawi, and specialized in fiqh under Shaykh 'Isa al-Barawi. He was given ijaza by his teacher after mastering much of his knowledge. Al-Shanwani is described as intelligent and with a good memory, which made his teacher give him special attention. The passage then begins to describe his ethics, noting his generosity, modesty, and humility, but cuts off mid-sentence after 'Among his humility...'.

Core Idea
Muhammad al-Shanwani was a humble scholar who led through both knowledge and action.

This lesson presents the biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, a prominent Azhari scholar and commentator. The passage details his origins, his rigorous traditional education, his admirable character, and his courageous stance against unjust rulers. Reading this biography helps us appreciate the human dimension behind classical scholarly works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to get a clear sense of the narrative.
The passage is a continuous biography, not a structured argument.

5

ويحدثنا الجبرتي عن أخلاقه ، فيقول : كان مُهذَّبَ النفس مع التواضع ، والانكسار والبشاشة لكل أحد من الناس ، ويُشمِّرُ ثيابه ويخدم بنفسه، ويكنس الجامع ويسرج القناديل

كان الشيخ الشنواني - - مع تواضعه وزهده وعزوفه عن الاتصال بالحُكّام لا يتردد في إبداء النصيحة لهم، وفي الشفاعة عندهم، وكان الشيخ - من قادة الشعب، وشارك - ه - في مقاومة الحملة الفرنسية، وقد حاول الوالي أن يستولي على كل أراضي الدولة، وأن يتخذ العلماء مَطيَّة ، حيث أفهمهم أنه سيترك أراضيهم لهم يزرعونها بمعرفتهم ويستغلونها، فتصدَّى له الإمام الشنواني وطالبه بالإفراج عن الأوقاف المحبوسة للطلبة فوافقه ، ثم طالبه بإلغاء أمر الاستيلاء على بقية الأراضي فرفض
قال الجبرتي عن منزلته العلمية، فيقول عنه : شيخ الإسلام، وعمدة الأنام، الفقيه العلامة ، والتحرير الفهامة... من أهل الطبقة الثانية ، الفقيه، النحوي ، المعقولي» (۱).
(۱) عجائب الآثار ۱۹۷/۷ ، ويقصد بقوله المعقولي: أنه درس علوم المنطق والجدل والفلسفة والميقات والحساب وما إليها من العلوم التي يطلقون عليها علوم المعقول ، أما علوم المنقول=
Translation of Muhammad al-Shanwani, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. Translation of the scholar Muhammad ibn Ali al-Shanwani al-Shafi‘i, the thirteenth Shaykh of al-Azhar al-Sharif, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. His name: Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Mansur al-Shanwani al-Shafi‘i. Birth and lineage: Shaykh Muhammad al-Shanwani was born in the village of Shanwan al-Ghuraf, Menoufia Governorate, and to it he was attributed. His upbringing and stages of education: He studied under many of the scholars of his time, namely the shaykhs Faris, al-Sa‘idi, al-Dardir, and al-Farmawi, and he specialized in jurisprudence under Shaykh ‘Isa al-Barawi, and he attended his lessons and read under him. The shaykh gave him permission after giving him most of his knowledge and felt confident in his learning because Shaykh al-Shanwani was intelligent, perceptive, and had a good memory. So his teacher gave him special attention and singled him out for his diligence and manners. His character: The shaykh was known for generosity, extreme modesty, and humility. Among his humility was that he did not like crowding for worldly appearances, so he did not compete with others in teaching at al-Azhar, but was content to give his lessons at the mosque known as al-Fakahani in al-‘Aqqadin, near his home in (Khusqadam). Students flocked to him and benefited from his views and instructions, as they also benefited from his manners and etiquettes. Al-Jabarti tells us about his character, saying: He was well-bred with humility, self-effacement, and cheerfulness towards everyone. He would roll up his sleeves, serve with his own hands, sweep the mosque, and light the lanterns. His status: Shaykh al-Shanwani, despite his humility, asceticism, and disinterest in connecting with rulers, did not hesitate to give them advice and intercede with them. The shaykh was a leader of the people and participated in resisting the French campaign. The governor tried to seize all state lands and to use the scholars as a means, making them understand that he would leave their lands for them to cultivate and exploit themselves. So Imam al-Shanwani confronted him and demanded the release of the endowments frozen for the students, and he agreed. Then he demanded the cancellation of the order to seize the remaining lands, but he refused. Al-Jabarti said about his scholarly status: He said about him: Shaykh al-Islam, the pillar of mankind, the jurist, the scholar, the profound editor... from the second rank, the jurist, the grammarian, the rationalist. (1) (1) 'Aja'ib al-Athar 7/197. By 'rationalist' he means that he studied the sciences of logic, dialectic, philosophy, timekeeping, arithmetic, and similar sciences that they call the rational sciences. As for the transmitted sciences=
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Muhammad al-Shanwani, the author of a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins with his full name and title: Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Mansur al-Shanwani al-Shafi‘i, noting he was the thirteenth shaykh of al-Azhar. It then gives his birthplace: the village of Shanwan in Menoufia, from which his nisba derives. His education is described: he studied under multiple scholars, particularly in fiqh under Shaykh ‘Isa al-Barawi, and was granted ijaza after demonstrating intelligence and diligence. The passage then details his character: generosity, modesty, and humility. A specific example is that he avoided competing for teaching positions at al-Azhar, instead teaching at a local mosque, where students gathered. Al-Jabarti is quoted as testimony to his humility and service. Finally, his status is discussed: though humble and avoiding rulers, he advised them and interceded; he was a popular leader who resisted the French campaign and confronted the governor over land seizures. Al-Jabarti praises his scholarly rank, calling him Shaykh al-Islam and noting his expertise in both transmitted and rational sciences, with a footnote clarifying that 'rationalist' refers to his study of logic, dialectic, philosophy, etc.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad al-Shanwani was a humble Azhari scholar, a leader in both knowledge and social action, whose biography exemplifies the integration of learning, character, and courage.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
He served by sweeping the mosque and lighting lanterns. Imagine doing chores your community needs without expecting thanks. What would that reveal about your heart?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

The Life and Character of Muhammad al-Shanawani
Biography of al-Shanawani: teaching, character, status, works, and appointment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, character, and scholarly contributions of Muhammad al-Shanawani, the commentator on Ithaaf al-Mureed.

Core Idea
A humble scholar who taught in a small mosque yet led the people and defended religious endowments.

This lesson introduces you to Muhammad al-Shanawani, the author of the gloss on the Ithaaf. His biography is not just a list of dates; it reveals a scholar of profound humility who was deeply engaged in both teaching and public life. Through al-Jabarti's testimony, we glimpse his character and his fearless confrontation with injustice.

Guided Path
1
Read about his teaching style
The passage opens with al-Shanawani’s approach to teaching: he avoided worldly competition and chose a small mosque near his home. Notice the impact this had on students.
His humility attracted students.
2
Learn about his character from al-Jabarti
Al-Jabarti’s description reveals a man who was humble, cheerful, and served himself. How does this contrast with typical scholarly images?
3
Understand his role in society
Despite his humility, he boldly advised rulers and led the people in resisting injustice. The confrontation with the governor over land endowments is a key event.
This shows the scholar's responsibility toward society.
4
Review his scholarly status and works
Al-Jabarti classifies him as a second-tier scholar expert in both rational and transmitted sciences. The list of his works shows his breadth.
Note the gloss on al-Jawhara is this very book.
5
Reflect on his appointment as Shaykh
The passage ends with his appointment as Shaykh of al-Azhar after initially hiding. What does his reaction tell about his character?

(۱) عجائب الآثار ۱۹۷/۷ ، ويقصد بقوله المعقولي: أنه درس علوم المنطق والجدل والفلسفة والميقات والحساب وما إليها من العلوم التي يطلقون عليها علوم المعقول ، أما علوم المنقول= فهي : الفقه والتفسير ، والحديث ... وعلوم اللغة . مؤلفاته: حاشية على شرح الشيخ عبد السلام اللقاني على الجوهرة، وهو كتابنا هذا . الجواهر السَنيَّة بمولد خير البرية، وهي تقييدات جمعها المؤلف من بعض كتب مشايخه وغيرهم على مولد المدابغي ، توجد منه نسخة خطية بدار الكتب المصرية. حاشية الشنواني على مختصر البخاري لابن أبي جمرة، توجد منه نسخة خطية بدار الكتب المصرية . ثبت الشنواني (إجازة أجاز بها تلميذه المبلط ، قال فيها: «لازمني مُدَّة مَديدَة ، وسنين عديدة حضورًا وسماعا وبحثًا ... حتى غَزُرَ علمه ... ثم التمس مني الإجازة وكتابة السند، فأجبته بذلك بشرط ألا يترك الإفادة»، توجد منه نسخة خطية بدار الكتب المصرية. حاشية على السمرقندية (في علوم البلاغة). حاشية على العضدية (في آداب البحث ) . وغيرها من الكتب النافعة. ولايته المشيخة جامع الأزهر الشريف لما توفي شيخ الأزهر العلامة الشرقاوي - ه - توجهت الأنظار إلى الشيخ الشنواني ، فتغيَّب عن بيته واختفى عن العيون ، ولكن الباشا أمر القاضي
Translation of Muhammad al-Shanawani, author of the gloss on Ithaaf. He did not love crowding after worldly appearances, so he did not compete with others in al-Azhar, but contented himself with giving his lessons in the mosque known as al-Fakahani in al-Aqqadin, near his house in Khushqadam. So students flocked to him and benefited from his opinions and directions, just as they benefited from his character and etiquette. Al-Jabarti narrates to us about his character, saying: He was refined in soul with humility, brokenness, and cheerfulness to every one of the people, and he would roll up his clothes and serve himself, sweep the mosque and light the lamps. His status: The Sheikh al-Shanawani – with his humility, asceticism, and disinclination to connect with rulers – did not hesitate to give them advice and to intercede with them. The Sheikh was one of the leaders of the people, and participated in resisting the French campaign. The governor tried to seize all the state's lands and to make the scholars a mount, making them understand that he would leave their lands for them to cultivate by their knowledge and exploit. So Imam al-Shanawani confronted him and demanded the release of the endowments held for the students, and he agreed. Then he demanded the cancellation of the order to seize the rest of the lands, but he refused. Al-Jabarti said about his scholarly status, saying about him: 'Sheikh of Islam, support of mankind, the jurist, the scholar, the painstakingly accurate, the insightful... from the second class, the jurist, the grammarian, the rationalist.' (1) (1) Wondrous Relics 197/7. By his saying 'rationalist', he means that he studied the sciences of logic, disputation, philosophy, timekeeping, arithmetic, and other sciences that they call rational sciences. As for the transmitted sciences, they are: jurisprudence, exegesis, hadith, and linguistic sciences. His works: A gloss on the commentary of Sheikh Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani on al-Jawhara – this is our book. Al-Jawahir al-Saniyya bi-Mawlid Khayr al-Bariyya, which are notes collected by the author from some of the books of his shaykhs and others on the mawlid of al-Madabighi; a manuscript copy exists in the Egyptian National Library. Al-Shanawani's gloss on Mukhtasar al-Bukhari by Ibn Abi Jamra; a manuscript copy exists in the Egyptian National Library. Thabit al-Shanawani (a license he granted to his student al-Muballat), in which he said: 'He accompanied me for a long time and many years in attendance, listening, and research... until his knowledge became abundant... then he asked me for a license and writing of the chain, so I answered him with that on condition that he not abandon instruction'; a manuscript copy exists in the Egyptian National Library. A gloss on al-Samarqandiyya (on the sciences of eloquence). A gloss on al-Adudiyya (on the etiquette of research). And other beneficial books. His appointment as shaykh of the Azhar Mosque: When the shaykh of al-Azhar, the scholar al-Sharqawi – – died, eyes turned to Sheikh al-Shanawani, so he absented himself from his house and hid from view, but the Pasha ordered the judge...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Muhammad al-Shanawani, the commentator on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins by describing his teaching method: he avoided worldly competition and taught at a small mosque near his home, yet students flocked to him. Al-Jabarti then testifies to his character, emphasizing his humility, self-service, and care for the mosque. The text then describes his status: despite his humility, he was bold in advising rulers and interceding, and he was a popular leader who resisted the French occupation. A confrontation with the governor over land confiscation is narrated, showing his defense of students' endowments. Al-Jabarti's appraisal of his scholarly rank follows, classifying him as a second-tier scholar excelling in both transmitted and rational sciences. A footnote explains the term 'rationalist' (al-ma'quli). The passage then lists his major works, including his gloss on al-Laqqani's commentary on al-Jawhara (which is the present book), works on the Prophet's birth, hadith, and licenses. Finally, it recounts his appointment as Shaykh of al-Azhar after al-Sharqawi's death, noting that he initially hid but was sought out by the Pasha. The narrative is chronological and integrates personal, scholarly, and political dimensions.

ولاية المشيخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Shanawani was only interested in rational sciences (e.g., logic, philosophy) to the neglect of transmitted sciences.
Correction: The footnote explicitly states that he studied both rational and transmitted sciences, and al-Jabarti's description includes 'jurist' and 'grammarian', confirming his comprehensive scholarship.

Checkpoint

A) He fled and hid from the governor.
B) He confronted the governor and demanded the release of the endowments.
C) He wrote a letter to the French authorities for help.
D) He resigned from teaching.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad al-Shanawani exemplified the ideal scholar: humble, learned, and courageous in defending truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Shanawani did not love crowded displays of worldly things and taught in a small mosque near his home. In your own pursuit of knowledge or practice, are you more driven by visible status or by sincere service? What is one step you can take today to shift your focus from recognition to humility?
?
He cleaned the mosque and lit the lamps himself, serving with his own hands. What is a task in your life that you consider lowly or beneath you? Will you commit to doing it this week with the same spirit of humility and service?
?
Despite his humility, al-Shanawani boldly confronted the governor to defend the rights of students. When you see an injustice, do you speak up, or do you remain silent out of fear of consequences? Which relationship or situation in your life is calling for your courageous voice right now?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

Al-Shanwani's Humility and the Azhar Succession
Biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani's works and his withdrawal from the Azhar shaykhdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly works of Muhammad al-Shanwani and his humble withdrawal from the shaykhdom election, revealing the interplay of piety and politics.

Core Idea
Humility wins respect: al-Shanwani's withdrawal from the shaykhdom exemplifies true scholarly character.

Muhammad al-Shanwani is known for his valuable glosses on key texts, but even more for his remarkable humility. When the shaykhdom of al-Azhar was offered, he hid and sent a letter renouncing it. This lesson tells his story, from his scholarly output to the dramatic election and its political aftermath.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Shanwani's works
Go through the list of his writings to appreciate his scholarly range in fiqh, hadith, rhetoric, and debate.
2
Understand his withdrawal
Notice how he deliberately hid and left a letter withdrawing in favor of al-Haythami. This shows his humility.
This is the central event.
3
Analyze the scholars' debate
Some questioned the validity of his renunciation. Think about whether one can renounce a position not yet held.
4
Reflect on the political dimension
The governor rejected the chosen candidate due to political history. Consider how external authority influenced the religious institution.
This connects to the broader context.

; Thabt al-Shanwānī (an ijāza he gave to his student al-Muballīṭ, in which he said: 'He stayed with me for a long period and many years, attending, listening, and researching ... until his knowledge became abundant ... then he asked me for the ijāza and the writing of the chain, so I responded to that with the condition that he not abandon teaching'); a manuscript copy exists in the Egyptian National Library.
A gloss on al-Samarqandiyya (on the sciences of rhetoric).
A gloss on al-ʿAḍudiyya (on the etiquette of debate). And other beneficial books.
His refusal of the shaykhdom of the Jāmiʿ al-Azhar al-Sharīf
When the shaykh of al-Azhar, the ʿallāma al-Sharqāwī (d. 1227 AH) died, eyes turned to al-Shanwānī, so he absented himself from his house and hid from sight, but the Pasha ordered the judge
(categories of his knowledge): fiqh, tafsīr, hadīth ... and language sciences.
[Page 46]
(Translation of Muhammad al-Shanwānī, author of the gloss on Ithāf al-Murīd)
to gather the shaykhs with him and they should agree upon a person free of ulterior motives.
So the judge sent to them, and their multitude attended. The judge asked: 'Is there anyone left who has not attended?' They said: 'None has stayed away except Ibn al-ʿArūsī, al-Haythamī, and al-Shanwānī.' So he sent for them, and Ibn al-ʿArūsī and al-Haythamī attended. The judge said: 'Where is al-Shanwānī? He must attend.' So he sent a messenger to him; he went to his house and returned, saying: 'He has been absent from his home for three days, and he has left you a letter which I have brought to you.'
So the judge opened the letter and read it aloud before the multitude of scholars. It was:
'In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. May God bless our master Muḥammad and his family and Companions and grant them peace. We have renounced the shaykhdom in favor of Shaykh Badawī al-Haythamī.' Thereupon those present stood up and the shaykhs clamored. Some said: 'He has not been confirmed in the shaykhdom such that he could renounce it in favor of another.' Others said: 'No one is shaykh except one who teaches the sciences in al-Azhar and benefits the students.'
So the judge intervened to end this quarrel, calming them down. He asked them: 'Whom are you satisfied with?' They said: 'We are satisfied with Shaykh al-Mahdī.' Everyone agreed, and they stood up, shook hands with him, and recited al-Fātiḥa. The judge wrote a decision to that effect and sent it to the governor of Egypt (Muḥammad ʿAlī Pasha). Then the gathering dispersed, and Shaykh al-Mahdī rode to his home in a great procession with the shaykhs and groups of students around and behind him. People flocked to his house to congratulate him, and everyone awaited the governor's approval of this decision.
But the governor Muḥammad ʿAlī Pasha refused to appoint Shaykh al-Mahdī, because he had a history of leadership and refusal of injustice, and Muḥammad ʿAlī does not accept a shaykh who interferes (in politics).
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Muḥammad al-Shanwānī, the author of the gloss on Ithāf al-Murīd, focusing on his scholarly works and his conduct during the selection of the Shaykh al-Azhar after the death of Shaykh al-Sharqāwī. It begins by listing his major writings: a gloss on al-Laqānī's commentary on al-Jawhara, a work on the Prophet's birth, a gloss on Ibn Abī Jamra's Mukhtaṣar al-Bukhārī, an ijāza he gave to his student, and glosses on rhetorical and dialectical texts. This establishes his scholarly authority. The narrative then turns to the succession crisis at al-Azhar. When al-Shanwānī's name came up, he deliberately hid to avoid the position, sending a letter renouncing the shaykhdom in favor of al-Haythamī. This action reveals his humility and desire to avoid worldly prestige. The scholars at the gathering, however, debated the validity of his renunciation, with some arguing that he could not renounce a position he had never formally held. Ultimately, they agreed on Shaykh al-Mahdī. The judge formalized this choice, but the governor Muḥammad ʿAlī Pasha rejected it due to al-Mahdī's independent political history, indicating the governor's desire for a non-interfering shaykh. The passage thus illustrates the interplay of scholarly authority, personal piety, and political power in early 19th-century Cairo.

الشنواني
المشيخة
الإجازة
جامع الأزهر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Shanwani was appointed shaykh, but he actively avoided it.
Correction: Al-Shanwani deliberately hid and left a letter of withdrawal, never accepting the position.

Checkpoint
What did al-Shanwani do when his name was proposed for the shaykhdom of al-Azhar?
A) He accepted immediately
B) He hid and left a letter of withdrawal
C) He campaigned for the position
D) He nominated himself

Key Takeaway
Al-Shanwani's life exemplifies scholarly humility: despite being a prime candidate for shaykh, he withdrew and left the decision to others, though political forces ultimately intervened.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are recognized for your achievements by influential people, do you find it hard to step back and let others take the spotlight? Al-Shanwani hid to avoid a position that everyone thought he deserved. What would it take for you to emulate that level of detachment from worldly honor?
?
The scholars in the story argued about who should lead based on qualifications and teaching, but Muhammad Ali Pasha rejected their choice because of political reasons. Have you ever seen religious leadership compromised by worldly politics? How does that challenge your trust in such institutions?
?
Al-Shanwani's ijaza to his student required that he not abandon teaching. What does that say about the responsibility of passing on knowledge? Are you currently using whatever knowledge you have to benefit others, or are you holding it back?

The Appointment of Muhammad al-Shanawani as Shaykh al-Azhar
Narrates the biography and political appointment of Muhammad al-Shanawani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the political and historical context surrounding the appointment of Muhammad al-Shanawani as Shaykh al-Azhar in 1812.

Core Idea
The selection of a Shaykh al-Azhar was a strategic political move, not merely a religious appointment.

This passage narrates a dramatic series of events that led to Muhammad al-Shanawani becoming Shaykh al-Azhar. It reveals how Muhammad Ali Pasha manipulated the appointment to avoid a powerful scholar who might challenge his authority. The story illustrates the delicate balance between religious leadership and political power in 19th-century Egypt.

Guided Path
1
Read the full narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Follow the sequence of events from the scholars' gathering to al-Shanawani's eventual appointment.
Pay attention to the reactions of the scholars and the governor.
2
Identify the key figures
Note the roles of: the judge, Ibn al-Arusi, al-Haythami, Shaykh al-Mahdi, Muhammad Ali Pasha, and al-Shanawani. Understand their positions and motivations.
3
Analyze the political motives
Why did Muhammad Ali reject Shaykh al-Mahdi? What was his concern about a powerful shaykh? How did al-Shanawani fit the criterion of being 'free of personal motives'?
The passage explicitly states that al-Mahdi had a history of leadership and resistance.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this event shows the influence of political authority over religious institutions. How did the role of Shaykh al-Azhar change under Muhammad Ali?

ترجمة محمد الشنواني صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف المريد يجمع المشايخ عنده ويتفقوا على شخص يكون خاليا مِن الأغراض، أحد لم فأرسل القاضي إليهم فحضرتْ جَمهرتُهم، فسأل القاضي: هل بقي يحضر؟ فقالوا: لم يتأخر عن الحضور إلا ابن العروسي، والهيثمي، والشنواني، فأرسل إليهم فحضر ابن العروسي، والهيثمي، فقال القاضي: وأين الشنواني؟ لا بد من حضوره، وأرسل إليه رسولا فذهب إلى بيته وعاد، فقال: إنه غائب عن داره منذ ثلاثة أيام، وقد ترك لكم رسالة جئت بها إليكم، ففتح القاضي الرسالة وقرأها جهرا على جمهرة العلماء وهي: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم، إننا نزلنا عن المشيخة للشيخ بدوي الهيثمي، فعند ذلك قام الحاضرون وضجّ المشايخ، فقال بعضهم: إنه لم تثبت له المشيخة حتى ينزل عنها لغيره، وقال بعضهم: لا يكون شيخًا إلا من يدرس العلوم في الأزهر ويفيد الطلبة. فتدخل القاضي لينهي هذه المعركة، فهدأ من روعهم، وسألهم القاضي: من الذي ترضونه؟ قالوا: نرضى الشيخ المهدي، ووافق الجميع، وقاموا وصافحوه وقرأوا الفاتحة، وكتب القاضي بهذا الأمر قرارًا أرسله إلى والي مصر (محمد علي باشا)، وانفض الجميع، وركب الشيخ المهدي إلى بيته في موكب كبير وحوله وخلفه المشايخ وطوائف الطلبة، وأقبل الناس على بيته للتهنئة، وانتظر الجميع موافقة الوالي على هذا القرار. ولكن الوالي محمد علي باشا رفض تعيين الشيخ المهدي؛ لأنه صاحب تاريخ حافل في الزعامة ورفض الضيم فمحمد علي لا يقبل شيخا يتدخل في شؤون الحكم ويقود العلماء والطلبة في مقاومة المظالم كما كان كبار مشايخ الأزهر يفعلون، ولهذا اشترط في شيخ الأزهر - كما قلنا - أن يكون خاليا عن الأغراض، وهو لم ينس أن مشایخ الأزهر هم الذين عزلوا الوالي السابق، وهم الذين عيَّنوه، فاضطر الباب العالي إلى النزول إلى مشيئتهم، ومَن يملك العزل والولاية يكون خطرًا على باب دولته التي بدأ في تكوينها. لذا فقد أرسل محمد علي باشا جنوده في طلب الشيخ الشنواني، فجدوا في البحث عنه حتى عُثِر عليه في المكان الذي اختفى فيه بمصر القديمة، فأخبروه بطلب الوالي له، فذهب معهم. ثم أرسل محمد علي إلى المشايخ بالحضور إلى مقره بالقلعة، فلما حضروا وجدوا الوالي وعنده الشيخ الشنواني، فأعلن محمد علي الشيخ الشنواني شيخا للجامع الأزهر، ولم يعترض الشيوخ على جعل الشيخ الشنواني شيخًا على الأزهر. ثم عاد الشيخ الشنواني إلى بيته في جَمْع كبير وموكب رسمي عظيم، وكانت دار الشيخ صغيرة متواضعة لا تتسع لهذا الموكب ولوفود المهنئين. فأنزله السيد المحروقي في دار (بان الزليجي) بحارة (خوشقدم) وأرسل إليه الطباخين والفراشين والأغنام والأرز والحطب والسمن والعسل والسكر والقهوة وأوقف عبيده وخدمه لخدمة القادمين، وازدحم الناس على الشيخ الشنواني مهنئين وأتوا أفواجا، وكان ذلك في يوم الثلاثاء، الرابع عشر من شهر شوال سنة ١٢٢٧هـ ٢٠ من أكتوبر سنة ١٨١٢م، ولما كان يوم الجمعة ذهب الشيخ الإمام إلى الجامع الأزهر، فصلى الجمعة، وازدحمت
Biography of Muhammad al-Shanawani, author of the gloss on Ithaf al-Murid. The shaykhs gathered with him and agreed upon a person free of personal motives. One [fragment]. Then the judge sent to them, and their multitude attended. The judge asked: 'Has anyone remained absent?' They said: 'Only Ibn al-Arusi, al-Haythami, and al-Shanawani have not failed to attend.' So he sent to them, and Ibn al-Arusi and al-Haythami attended. The judge said: 'Where is al-Shanawani? He must attend.' He sent a messenger to him, who went to his house and returned, saying: 'He has been absent from his home for three days, and he left a letter for you which I have brought.' The judge opened the letter and read it aloud to the multitude of scholars. It was: 'In the name of God, the Merciful, the Compassionate. May God bless our Master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. We have relinquished the shaykhate to Shaykh Badawi al-Haythami.' At that, those present stood up and the shaykhs clamored. Some said: 'The shaykhate has not been established for him so that he can relinquish it to another.' Others said: 'No one is a shaykh except one who teaches the sciences in al-Azhar and benefits the students.' The judge intervened to end this conflict. He calmed them and asked them: 'Whom do you accept?' They said: 'We accept Shaykh al-Mahdi.' All agreed, and they stood, shook hands with him, and recited the Fatiha. The judge wrote a decision on this matter and sent it to the governor of Egypt (Muhammad Ali Pasha). The assembly dispersed, and Shaykh al-Mahdi rode to his house in a great procession, with shaykhs and groups of students around and behind him. People flocked to his house to congratulate him, and everyone awaited the governor's approval of this decision. But the governor Muhammad Ali Pasha refused to appoint Shaykh al-Mahdi, because he had a history full of leadership and refusal of injustice. Muhammad Ali does not accept a shaykh who interferes in matters of governance and leads scholars and students in resisting oppression, as the senior shaykhs of al-Azhar used to do. Therefore, he stipulated for the Shaykh of al-Azhar—as we said—that he be free of personal motives. And he had not forgotten that the shaykhs of al-Azhar were the ones who had deposed the previous governor and appointed him. Thus, the Sublime Porte was compelled to submit to their will. Whoever has the power to depose and appoint is a danger to the empire that he had begun to establish. So Muhammad Ali Pasha sent his soldiers to seek al-Shanawani. They searched diligently until he was found in the place where he had hidden in Old Cairo. They informed him of the governor's request, and he went with them. Then Muhammad Ali sent for the shaykhs to attend at his headquarters in the Citadel. When they arrived, they found the governor with al-Shanawani present. Muhammad Ali announced al-Shanawani as Shaykh of al-Azhar Mosque. The shaykhs did not object to making al-Shanawani shaykh of al-Azhar. Then al-Shanawani returned to his house in a large group and a great official procession. His house was small and modest, not spacious enough for this procession and the crowds of well-wishers. So al-Sayyid al-Mahruqi lodged him in the house of (Ban al-Zaliji) in the alley of (Khushqadam) and sent him cooks, servants, sheep, rice, firewood, ghee, honey, sugar, coffee, and assigned his slaves and servants to serve the visitors. People crowded upon al-Shanawani, congratulating him, and they came in waves. That was on Tuesday, the fourteenth of Shawwal in the year 1227 AH (20 October 1812 CE). And when Friday came, the shaykh imam went to al-Azhar Mosque, prayed the Friday prayer, and [the crowd] crowded.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a historical biography of Muhammad al-Shanawani, the author of a gloss on Ithaf al-Murid. It narrates the circumstances surrounding his appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar. The story begins with the shaykhs gathering to agree on a candidate for the shaykhate who is free of personal motives. The judge summons the scholars, and only three are absent: Ibn al-Arusi, al-Haythami, and al-Shanawani. When the first two attend, al-Shanawani is still missing. The judge insists on his presence, but a messenger finds he has been absent for three days, leaving a letter. The judge reads the letter aloud, in which al-Shanawani relinquishes the shaykhate to Shaykh Badawi al-Haythami. This causes an uproar among the scholars, with objections that al-Haythami never held the shaykhate to relinquish it, and that only one who teaches at al-Azhar qualifies. The judge calms them and asks for an acceptable candidate. They choose Shaykh al-Mahdi, and all agree, reciting the Fatiha. The judge sends a report to the governor, Muhammad Ali Pasha. However, Muhammad Ali rejects al-Mahdi due to his history of leadership and resistance to injustice. The governor fears a shaykh who might interfere in governance and lead opposition, recalling that previous shaykhs had deposed and appointed governors. Therefore, he insists on a shaykh free of personal motives. He sends soldiers to find al-Shanawani, who had hidden in Old Cairo, and brings him to the Citadel. When the shaykhs are summoned, they find al-Shanawani with the governor, who announces his appointment. The shaykhs do not object. Al-Shanawani returns home in a grand procession, but his house is too small for the crowds. A benefactor, al-Sayyid al-Mahruqi, provides a larger house and supplies for the celebration. People flock to congratulate him on Tuesday, 14 Shawwal 1227 AH (20 October 1812). On Friday, al-Shanawani goes to al-Azhar to lead the Friday prayer, and the crowd is immense, though the text breaks off. This biography highlights the political dynamics behind the appointment of the Shaykh al-Azhar and the strategic role of al-Shanawani.

Key Terms
الشيخ الشنواني
الشيخ المهدي
محمد علي باشا
مشيخة الأزهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Shanawani's appointment was purely a religious decision based on his scholarship.
Correction: The passage shows that political motives were paramount: Muhammad Ali rejected al-Mahdi because he could challenge his authority, and chose al-Shanawani because he appeared neutral and avoidant of political involvement.

Checkpoint
Why did Muhammad Ali Pasha refuse to appoint Shaykh al-Mahdi as Shaykh al-Azhar?
A) Because Shaykh al-Mahdi was not qualified.
B) Because Shaykh al-Mahdi had a history of leadership and resistance, which could threaten the governor's authority.
C) Because the other scholars opposed him.
D) Because al-Shanawani was better qualified.

Key Takeaway
The appointment of the Shaykh al-Azhar was a politically motivated decision to ensure the candidate would not challenge the governor's authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Shanawani hid to avoid the position of Shaykh al-Azhar. When have you avoided a responsibility that would have required you to stand up for truth? What did your avoidance reveal about your priorities?
?
The scholars initially chose al-Mahdi because he had a history of resisting oppression. Are you known in your community for speaking out against wrong, or do you remain silent to protect your comfort? What is one injustice you have ignored or excused?
?
Muhammad Ali wanted a shaykh 'free of personal motives' but also one who would not challenge him. Examine your own heart: do you claim neutrality while actually serving your own interests? Where is the line between genuine disinterest and cowardly silence in your life?

The Appointment and Legacy of Muhammad al-Shanwani
Biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, his appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar, and his death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the political and scholarly significance of Muhammad al-Shanwani's appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar under Muhammad Ali Pasha.

Core Idea
Al-Shanwani's appointment was as much political as academic.

This lesson covers the biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, the commentator on Ithaf al-Murid. It reveals how his appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar was intertwined with the political power struggles of the time, and highlights his enduring commitment to teaching and scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for historical context
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the sequence of events.
Pay attention to the political dynamics described.
2
Identify the political motivations
Note why Muhammad Ali Pasha sought out al-Shanwani and how the Azhar shaykhs' power to depose governors played a role.
The passage explicitly states this threat.
3
Observe the appointment ceremony
Notice that the other shaykhs were summoned and did not object to al-Shanwani's appointment.
This shows the authority of the ruler.
4
Reflect on al-Shanwani's character
He continued teaching despite his new role and remained humble in his personal life.
His dedication to learning is highlighted.
5
Consider the legacy
Think about how his life story illustrates the intersection of scholarship and politics in Ottoman Egypt.

ترجمة محمد الشنواني صاحب الحاشية على إتحاف المريد
في شؤون الحكم ويقود العلماء والطلبة في مقاومة المظالم كما كان كبار مشايخ الأزهر يفعلون ، ولهذا اشترط في شيخ الأزهر - كما قلنا ـ أن يكون خاليا عن الأغراض، وهو لم ينس أن مشایخ الأزهر هم الذين عزلوا الوالي السابق، وهم الذين عيَّنوه ، فاضطر الباب العالي إلى النزول إلى مشيئتهم، ومَن يملك العزل والولاية يكون خطرًا على باب دولته التي بدأ في تكوينها.
لذا فقد أرسل محمد علي باشا جنوده في طلب الشيخ الشنواني ، فجدوا ، في البحث عنه حتى عُثِر عليه في المكان الذي اختفى فيه بمصر القديمة، فأخبروه بطلب الوالي له، فذهب معهم.
ثم أرسل محمد علي إلى المشايخ بالحضور إلى مقره بالقلعة، فلما حضروا وجدوا الوالي وعنده الشيخ الشنواني، فأعلن محمد علي الشيخ الشنواني شيخا للجامع الأزهر ، ولم يعترض الشيوخ على جعل الشيخ الشنواني شيخًا على الأزهر.
ثم عاد الشيخ الشنواني إلى بيته في جَمْع كبير وموكب رسمي عظيم، وكانت دار الشيخ صغيرة متواضعة لا تتسع لهذا الموكب ولوفود المهنئين . فأنزله السيد المحروقي في دار (بان) الزليجي) بحارة (خوشقدم) وأرسل إليه الطباخين والفراشين والأغنام والأرز والحطب والسمن والعسل والسكر والقهوة وأوقف عبيده وخدمه لخدمة القادمين، وازدحم الناس على الشيخ الشنواني - ه - مهنئين وأتوا أفواجا ، وكان ذلك في يوم الثلاثاء، الرابع عشر من شهر شوال سنة ١٢٢٧هـ ٢٠ من أكتوبر سنة ١٨١٢م ، ولما كان يوم ۱۸۱۲م. الجمعة ذهب الشيخ الإمام إلى الجامع الأزهر ، فصلى الجمعة، وازدحمت الجماهير عليه مهنئين له .
ولم يترك الشيخ - - مكانه في الدرس بعد تولي المشيخة، وكان متبحرًا في علوم اللغة ، كما كان مولعاً بعلم الكلام والرياضيات .
وفاته
كان الشيخ الإمام الشنواني - - متواضعاً في حياته وفي شؤون معاشه، وأقبلت عليه الدنيا فلم يهنأ بها، فقد اعترته الأمراض إلى أن توفي الأربعاء رابع عشر من المحرم سنة ١٢٣٣هـ = ٢٣ نوفمبر سنة ١٨١٧م، وصُلَّي عليه بالأزهر في مشهد عظيم، ودُفنَ بتربة المجاورين(١)
Translation of Muhammad al-Shanwani, author of the gloss on Ithaf al-Murid. He was involved in matters of governance and led scholars and students in resisting injustices as the senior shaykhs of al-Azhar used to do, and for this reason he stipulated in the Shaykh al-Azhar—as we said—that he be free from personal interests, and he did not forget that the shaykhs of al-Azhar were the ones who deposed the previous governor and the ones who appointed him, so the Sublime Porte was forced to submit to their will, and whoever holds the power of dismissal and appointment is a danger to the state that it began to form. So Muhammad Ali Pasha sent his soldiers to summon al-Shanwani, and they searched diligently until he was found in the place where he was hiding in Old Cairo, and they informed him of the governor's summons, so he went with them. Then Muhammad Ali sent for the shaykhs to come to his residence at the Citadel, and when they arrived, they found the governor with al-Shanwani present, and Muhammad Ali announced al-Shanwani as Shaykh of al-Azhar Mosque, and the shaykhs did not object to making al-Shanwani Shaykh of al-Azhar. Then al-Shanwani returned to his home in a large gathering and a great official procession, but his house was small and modest, not spacious enough for this procession and the crowds of well-wishers. So al-Sayyid al-Mahruqi housed him in a house (of al-Zalaji) in the alley of Khushqadam, and sent him cooks, servants, sheep, rice, firewood, ghee, honey, sugar, and coffee, and assigned his slaves and servants to serve the visitors, and the people crowded around al-Shanwani congratulating him, coming in droves. That was on Tuesday, the 14th of Shawwal 1227 AH (20 October 1812 CE). On Friday, the Shaykh Imam went to al-Azhar Mosque, prayed Friday prayer, and the masses crowded around him congratulating him. He did not leave his place in teaching after assuming the shaykhdom, and he was deeply learned in the linguistic sciences, and was fond of kalam and mathematics. His death: The Shaykh Imam al-Shanwani was humble in his life and in his livelihood, and worldly prosperity came to him but he did not enjoy it, as illnesses afflicted him until he died on Wednesday, the 14th of Muharram 1233 AH (23 November 1817 CE). The funeral prayer was performed over him at al-Azhar in a great gathering, and he was buried in the burial ground of the neighbors (1).
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Muhammad al-Shanwani, the commentator on Ithaf al-Murid. It begins by describing his involvement in governance and his leadership role in resisting injustices, similar to earlier Azhar shaykhs. The author explains that al-Shanwani insisted that the Shaykh al-Azhar be free from personal interests, and notes that the Azhar shaykhs had previously played a key role in deposing and appointing governors, which made them a threat to the state. Therefore, Muhammad Ali Pasha sought to control the situation by summoning al-Shanwani, who was found hiding in Old Cairo. The Pasha then brought the shaykhs together and appointed al-Shanwani as Shaykh al-Azhar, and no one objected. After the appointment, al-Shanwani returned home in a grand procession, but his house was too small, so a benefactor provided him with a larger house and provisions for entertaining guests. The people came in large numbers to congratulate him. On the following Friday, he went to al-Azhar and led the Friday prayer. Despite his new position, he continued his teaching and remained dedicated to learning, particularly in linguistics, kalam, and mathematics. The passage concludes with his death: he remained humble despite his worldly prosperity, suffered from illnesses, and died on a Wednesday in 1233 AH. His funeral was well-attended, and he was buried in the burial ground of the neighbors. A footnote marker indicates a source note, but the sources are not included in this passage.

Key Terms
شيخ الأزهر
محمد علي باشا
علم الكلام

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Shanwani's appointment was purely academic.
Correction: The passage shows it was politically motivated because the Azhar shaykhs had power to depose governors.

Checkpoint
Why did Muhammad Ali Pasha seek out al-Shanwani and appoint him as Shaykh al-Azhar?
A) Because al-Shanwani was the most learned scholar available.
B) Because the previous Shaykh had died and al-Shanwani was next in line.
C) Because the Azhar shaykhs had power to appoint and depose governors, and Muhammad Ali wanted to control that power.
D) Because the people demanded al-Shanwani's appointment.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad al-Shanwani's appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar was a political move by Muhammad Ali Pasha to control the influential shaykhs, yet al-Shanwani remained a dedicated scholar until his death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When al-Shanwani was suddenly elevated to power and given a grand procession, everyone celebrated. But his house was too small, and he couldn't enjoy the prosperity. If you were in his place, would your heart be captured by the honor and luxury, or would you remain humble like him? What practical step can you take today to detach your self-worth from worldly recognition?
?
The shaykhs of al-Azhar had the power to depose and appoint governors—they were a real threat to the ruler. If you held such influence, would you use it to resist injustice, or would you be tempted to serve your own interests? How can you ensure your leadership, even in small matters, is free from personal ambition?
?
Al-Shanwani faced illnesses when prosperity came. Are you prepared to remain steadfast in faith and humility when your circumstances improve, or do you fear that comfort will weaken your resolve? What attachments in your life right now might prevent you from staying close to Allah if prosperity increases?

The Life and Legacy of Muhammad al-Shanawani
Biography of al-Shanawani: his teaching, death, and sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly character, and death of Muhammad al-Shanawani, as well as the sources for his biography.

Core Idea
A humble scholar who remained devoted to teaching despite worldly prominence.

Before studying his gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed, it helps to know the man behind the work. Muhammad al-Shanawani was a scholar of language, kalam, and mathematics, who served as Shaykh al-Azhar yet never abandoned his teaching post. This brief biography from the Egyptian Dar al-Ifta' offers a glimpse into his humility, his expertise, and the circumstances of his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key facts: his expertise, his humility, his death date and burial.
2
Identify the two main sections
The passage has two clear parts: first, a description of his character and teaching; second, the account of his death and a list of sources. Note how each part contributes to the overall portrait.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why such a biography is included in a theological work. It establishes the authority and piety of the commentator, and reminds us of the human dimension of scholarship.

Biography of Muhammad al-Shanawani, author of the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. The masses congratulated him. And the Shaykh did not leave his place in teaching after assuming the shaykhdom, and he was well-versed in the linguistic sciences, and he was enamored with the science of kalam and mathematics. His death. The Imam Shaykh al-Shanawani was humble in his life and in the affairs of his livelihood, and the world turned to him but he did not enjoy it, for illnesses befell him until he died on Wednesday the fourteenth of Muharram in the year 1233 AH = 23 November 1817 CE, and the funeral prayer was performed for him in al-Azhar in a great gathering, and he was buried in the cemetery of al-Mujawirin (1). Day. (1) Sources of his biography: al-Azhar in Twelve Years, published by the Azhar Administration; al-Azhar over a Thousand Years by Muhammad Abd al-Mun'im Khafaji 2/355, 356; *Shuyukh al-Azhar by Ashraf Fawzi 2/21-24; Aja'ib al-Athar by al-Jabarti, published by the Arab Statement Committee; Kanz al-Jawhar fi Tarikh al-Azhar by Sulayman Rasad al-Hanafi al-Zayyati, pp. 135-173; Mashyakhat al-Azhar from its inception until now by Ali Abd al-Azim 1/189-193. And this translation with its sources is complete, taken from the website of the Egyptian Dar al-Ifta'.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Muhammad al-Shanawani, the author of a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed. It begins by noting that the masses congratulated him, likely upon his appointment as Shaykh al-Azhar. It then emphasizes that despite assuming leadership, he did not abandon teaching; he remained a teacher and was proficient in linguistic sciences, and had a passion for the science of kalam and mathematics. The passage then describes his death: he was humble and worldly success did not bring him comfort; he was afflicted by illnesses and died on Wednesday, 14 Muharram 1233 AH (23 November 1817 CE). His funeral prayer was held at al-Azhar with a large attendance, and he was buried in the cemetery of al-Mujawirin. The passage ends with a list of sources for his biography, collected from various works on the history of al-Azhar and prominent scholars, with a note that the biography is taken from the Egyptian Dar al-Ifta' website.

Biography of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid covering his birth, lineage, and early education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life and scholarly background of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, the commentator of Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Core Idea
A scholar's upbringing in a household of knowledge shaped his pursuit of religious sciences.

This lesson introduces the editor of al-Nizam al-Farid, whose gloss on Jawharat al-Tawhid is foundational. Understanding his biography helps us appreciate the context in which his commentary was produced. The passage covers his birth, family, and early education in al-Azhar.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the scholar's life. Note the structure: name, lineage, birth, upbringing, education.
The passage is from a biographical entry, so it follows a traditional format.

Pay attention to the year 1318 AH / 1900 CE and the institutes in Damietta and Cairo.

العلامة الجليل الشيخ محمد محي الدين عبد الحميد بن إبراهيم بن أحمد الشرقاوي الأزهري الحنفي، أبو رجاء.

ونشأ في كنف والده العالم الأزهري الشيخ عبد الحميد الذي كان من رجال القضاء والفتيا، فقد تربى في بيت علم وفقه ، وترعرع وهو يرى كبار رجال العلم والقضاء يجتمعون مع أبيه في البيت، ويتطارحون مسائل الفقه والحديث واللغة، فتاقت نفسه إلى أن يكون مثل هؤلاء، ودفع به والده إلى من يُحفظه القرآن ويعلمه مبادئ القراءة والكتابة.
طلبه للعلم في الأزهر وتخرجه متفوقا
حتى إذا انتهى من ذلك التحق بمعهد دمياط الأزهري ليرتشف مبادئ العلوم، حيث كان والده قاضيا في دمياط . ثم انتقل إلى معهد القاهرة الأزهري لما انتقل والده لتقلد منصف المفتي لوزارة الأوقاف ، وظل بالأزهر حتى حصل على شهادة العالمية النظامية مع أول فرقة دراسية نالت هذه الدرجة وفق طريقة
Biography of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid. Biography of the distinguished scholar Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, author of the gloss al-Nizam al-Farid on the critical edition of Jawharat al-Tawhid. His name, lineage, birth, and upbringing. He is the venerable distinguished scholar Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Sharqawi al-Azhari al-Hanafi, Abu Raja'. He was born in the village of Kafr al-Hammam in the Sharqiyya Governorate, in the year 1318 AH corresponding to 1900 CE. And he grew up under the care of his father, the Azhari scholar Shaykh Abd al-Hamid, who was among the men of judiciary and fatwa. So he was raised in a house of knowledge and jurisprudence, and he grew up seeing the great men of knowledge and judiciary gathering with his father in the house, discussing issues of jurisprudence, hadith, and language, so his soul yearned to be like them, and his father pushed him to one who would have him memorize the Quran and teach him the basics of reading and writing. His pursuit of knowledge in al-Azhar and his outstanding graduation. When he finished that, he enrolled in the Damietta Azhari institute to sip the principles of the sciences, as his father was a judge in Damietta. Then he moved to the Cairo Azhari institute when his father moved to assume the position of mufti in the Ministry of Awqaf, and he remained at al-Azhar until he obtained the regular alamiyya certificate with the first study group that attained this degree according to the method.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a biographical entry for Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, the scholar who wrote a gloss on al-Nizam al-Farid, which is a commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid. It first gives his full name and lineage: he is the son of Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Sharqawi, an Azhari Hanafi scholar, with the kunya Abu Raja'. His birth: in Kafr al-Hammam, Sharqiyya, in 1318 AH/1900 CE. His upbringing: he was raised under his father, an Azhari scholar who worked as a judge and mufti. The scholarly environment at home—with jurists, hadith scholars, and linguists gathering—inspired him to pursue knowledge. His father arranged for him to memorize the Quran and learn basic literacy. For his formal education, he first attended the Damietta Azhari institute (his father was a judge there), then moved to the Cairo Azhari institute when his father became mufti of the Ministry of Awqaf. He remained at al-Azhar until he obtained the 'regular alamiyya certificate' (shahada al-alamiyya al-nizamiyya) as part of the first group to receive this degree under the new system. The passage ends mid-sentence, describing the method of that system.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A scholar's foundation is built in the homes of scholars.

Before diving into the theological content of the book, it is valuable to know the person behind it. This lesson introduces the author of the commentary, Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, tracing his name, lineage, birthplace, and the scholarly environment that nurtured him. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the tradition from which he writes.

Azhari Education and Outstanding Graduation
The author's educational journey through Azhari institutes and his top-ranked graduation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the formal educational path that shaped the author, including his progression through Azhari institutes and his outstanding graduation with the first 'Alamiyya class in 1925.

Core Idea
Discipline, excellence, and scholarly mentorship yield extraordinary success.

This lesson traces the author's formal education at al-Azhar, from his early studies at the Damietta Institute to his transfer to Cairo and eventual graduation at the top of the first class to receive the regular 'Alamiyya degree. His achievement of first rank among elite peers highlights exceptional dedication and intelligence, setting the stage for his later contributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the education passage
Read the Arabic passage describing his educational journey once. Then read the translation. Notice the sequence of institutes and his father's role.
The passage flows chronologically from Damietta to Cairo.
2
Identify key institutions
Note the two Azhari institutes: Damietta and Cairo. Understand that his father's position as judge then mufti influenced his moves.
3
Understand the 'Alamiyya degree
The 'Alamiyya was a prestigious certificate. He obtained it in 1344 AH/1925 CE as part of the first regular class. His first rank among peers was remarkable.
This degree marked a milestone in modern Azhari education.
4
Reflect on his teachers and success
He studied under 'great God-fearing scholars.' His success astonished many. Consider how environment and effort combined.

طلبه للعلم في الأزهر وتخرجه متفوقا. حتى إذا انتهى من ذلك التحق بمعهد دمياط الأزهري ليرتشف مبادئ العلوم، حيث كان والده قاضيا في دمياط. ثم انتقل إلى معهد القاهرة الأزهري لما انتقل والده لتقلد من[؟]صف المفتي لوزارة الأوقاف، وظل بالأزهر حتى حصل على شهادة العالمية النظامية مع أول فرقة دراسية نالت هذه الدرجة وفق طريقة دراسية منتظمة، وذلك في سنة (١٣٤٤هـ) الموافق (١٩٢٥م) وتتلمذ في تلك الفترة على جيل الكبار من العلماء الربانيين، وكان نجاحه مثار الدهشة، فقد فاق الجميع وحصل على المرتبة الأولى بين فحول أقرانه من العلماء. من أول تأليفه حالة طلبه للعلم: ومن أكبر ما يدلّ على ألمعية الطالب وظهور هلاله مُبشرا بما سيعقبه من إبدار .. أن طمح في التأليف وهو لا يزال طالبا قبل التخرج، فقد كان ذا نفس مكبة على القراءة والمطالعة، وصاحب همة عالية، وكان من ثمرة ذلك قيامه بشرح مقامات بديع الزمان الهمذاني شرحاً مسهبا مستفيضا مشحونا بدرر الفوائد العلمية وتفسير الإشارات الأدبية والتاريخية، مما يدلّ على أنه قد وعى مسائل اللغة والأدب والتاريخ العربي مما سمح له بالإتقان في هذا الشرح، ونشر ذلك العمل وهو لا يزال طالبا لم يظفر بعد بدرجة العالمية، وصدّر هذا الشرح بإهداء لوالده اعترافا بفضله عليه وقياما بواجب البرّ، فلولا توجيهات والده المتواصلة وحثه له لما بلغ ما بلغ. ومما قاله في ذلك الإهداء لوالده: «إلى نفسك الطاهرة، وحكمتك العالية، وأدبك الجم، وفضلك الغزير .. أقدم كتابي هذا، لقد ربيتني على الفضيلة، وزهدتني في الدَّعة والوَنْي، وعند الله في ذلك جزاؤك، فليس بيدي ء منه، ولا في استطاعتي أنْ أناله ولو رقيت أسباب السماء، ولكني أتقدَّمُ إليك بكتابي هذا، بُرهانا على أنكَ غرست فأثمرتَ، وبذرت فأنميتَ، ودليلاً على أنَّ غِراسك سيزدَادُ نموًا بمَرَّ الأيام إلى أن يؤتي أكله مرتين بإذن الله». والحقُّ أنَّ الغِراس قد أتى أُكله مرّات عدة، فإنّ ما أخرجه الأستاذ الشيخ
His pursuit of knowledge at al-Azhar and his outstanding graduation. When he completed that, he joined the Damietta Azhari Institute to drink in the principles of the sciences, as his father was a judge in Damietta. Then he transferred to the Cairo Azhari Institute when his father moved to hold the position of mufti of the Ministry of Awqaf, and he remained at al-Azhar until he obtained the regular 'Alamiyya certificate with the first study group that attained this degree according to a regular study method, in the year (1344 AH) corresponding to (1925 CE). During that period he studied under a generation of great God-fearing scholars, and his success was a cause of astonishment, for he surpassed everyone and obtained the first rank among the elite of his peers among the scholars. [Section: On his first authorship while a student:] Among the greatest indications of the student's brilliance and the appearance of his crescent moon heralding what would follow of full moons .. is that he aspired to authorship while still a student before graduation, for he had a soul devoted to reading and study, and was highly motivated. The fruit of that was his undertaking a detailed, extensive commentary on the Maqamat of Badi' al-Zaman al-Hamadhani, filled with precious scientific benefits and interpretation of literary and historical references, indicating that he had mastered issues of language, literature, and Arab history, which allowed him to excel in this commentary. He published this work while still a student who had not yet obtained the 'Alamiyya degree, and he prefaced this commentary with a dedication to his father in recognition of his virtue and fulfillment of the duty of filial piety. For without his father's continuous guidance and encouragement, he would not have reached what he reached. Among what he said in that dedication to his father: 'To your pure soul, your lofty wisdom, your abundant refinement, and your overflowing virtue... I present this my book. You raised me in virtue, and you made me renounce ease and weakness. With God is your reward for that, for I have no part in it, nor is it in my power to attain it even if I ascended the causes of heaven. But I present to you this my book as a proof that you planted and bore fruit, and you sowed and caused growth, and as evidence that your planting will increase in growth over time until it yields its fruit twice by God's permission.' The truth is that the planting has yielded its fruit many times, for what the professor shaykh has produced...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage covers two main aspects of the author's life: his formal education and his early scholarly output. The first part describes his progression through Azhari institutes: after initial studies, he joined the Damietta Azhari Institute, then moved to Cairo when his father became mufti of the Ministry of Awqaf. He eventually obtained the regular 'Alamiyya degree in 1925 as part of the first class, achieving the highest rank. The second part highlights his first major work: while still a student, he authored a detailed commentary on the Maqamat of al-Hamadhani. The passage emphasizes his diligence and brilliance, noting that this commentary was published before he graduated. The dedication to his father is quoted at length, expressing profound gratitude and acknowledging his father's role. The passage concludes with a statement that the father's efforts indeed bore fruit many times over.

Key Terms
معهد دمياط الأزهري
معهد القاهرة الأزهري
العالمية النظامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author studied only at one institute.
Correction: He moved from Damietta to Cairo due to his father's job relocation.

Checkpoint
In what year did the author obtain the regular 'Alamiyya degree?
A) 1344 AH / 1925 CE
B) 1350 AH / 1931 CE
C) 1330 AH / 1912 CE
D) 1320 AH / 1902 CE

Key Takeaway
The author's formal education at al-Azhar culminated in his obtaining the 'Alamiyya degree with first rank in 1925, after studying under leading scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author's education required moving and adapting to his father's career changes. Are you willing to uproot your comfort and make sacrifices for knowledge? What is one sacrifice you can make this week for your learning?
?
He did not merely pass; he surpassed everyone and obtained the first rank. In your own studies, do you settle for 'good enough' or do you strive to be among the elite? What would change if you aimed for the first rank?
?
He studied under God-fearing scholars. Who are the people you learn from? Do you seek out teachers who not only have knowledge but also piety? How can you prioritize finding righteous teachers in your current situation?

First Authorship as a Student: The Maqamat Commentary
The author's first published work and the dedication to his father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author's first major work—a commentary on Maqamat al-Hamadhani—was produced while he was still a student, and appreciate the role of his father's guidance and his filial piety.

Core Idea
True scholarship can begin early, and filial piety is a foundation for academic excellence.

This lesson explores the author's remarkable achievement of authoring a detailed commentary on the Maqamat of Badi' al-Zaman al-Hamadhani while still a student before graduation. The passage highlights his brilliance and diligence, and includes a heartfelt dedication to his father. This dedication sheds light on his character and the nurturing environment that fostered his talents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on his first work
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'من أول تأليفه' carefully. Then read the translation. Notice the emphasis on his student status and the nature of the commentary.
The passage is a continuous narrative about his early authorship.
2
Understand the significance of the commentary
The commentary on Maqamat al-Hamadhani is described as detailed and extensive, filled with scientific benefits and literary/historical insights. It shows his mastery of language, literature, and history.
3
Examine the dedication
Read the dedication to his father. Note the language of gratitude and recognition. Reflect on how the author attributes his success to his father's guidance.
The dedication is a key part of the passage.
4
Reflect on the father's role
The author explicitly says that without his father's continuous guidance, he would not have achieved what he did. Consider the impact of a supportive family in scholarship.

Early Education and First Publication
Describes the author's student years and his first scholarly work on Maqamat al-Hamadhani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early academic journey of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din and the significance of his first scholarly work.

Core Idea
Brilliance emerges early; the first commentary marks the beginning of a scholarly legacy.

This lesson introduces us to the formative years of Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, a towering figure in Islamic scholarship. We will see how his exceptional ability, nurtured by his father's guidance, led him to produce a remarkable commentary while still a student.

ترجمة محمد محيي الدين عبد الحميد
دراسية منتظمة، وذلك في سنة (١٣٤٤هـ) الموافق (١٩٢٥م) وتتلمذ في تلك الفترة على جيل الكبار من العلماء الربانيين، وكان نجاحه مثار الدهشة ، فقد فاق الجميع وحصل على المرتبة الأولى بين فحول أقرانه من العلماء.
من أول تأليفه حالة طلبه للعلم:
ومن أكبر ما يدلّ على ألمعية الطالب وظهور هلاله مُبشرا بما سيعقبه من إبدار .. أن طمح في التأليف وهو لا يزال طالبا قبل التخرج، فقد كان ذا نفس مكبة على القراءة والمطالعة ، وصاحب همة عالية ، وكان من ثمرة ذلك قيامه بشرح مقامات بديع الزمان الهمذاني شرحاً مسهبا مستفيضا مشحونا بدرر الفوائد العلمية وتفسير الإشارات الأدبية والتاريخية ، مما يدلّ على أنه قد وعى مسائل اللغة والأدب والتاريخ العربي مما سمح له بالإتقان في هذا الشرح ، ونشر ذلك العمل وهو لا يزال طالبا لم يظفر بعد بدرجة العالمية، وصدّر هذا الشرح بإهداء لوالده اعترافا بفضله عليه وقياما بواجب البرّ، فلولا توجيهات والده المتواصلة وحثه له لما بلغ ما بلغ .
ومما قاله في ذلك الإهداء لوالده: «إلى نفسك الطاهرة، وحكمتك العالية ، وأدبك الجم، وفضلك الغزير .. أقدم كتابي هذا، لقد ربيتني على الفضيلة ، وزهدتني في الدَّعة والوَنْي ، وعند الله في ذلك جزاؤك ، فليس بيدي [؟] منه ، ولا في استطاعتي أنْ أناله ولو رقيت أسباب السماء ، ولكني أتقدَّمُ إليك بكتابي هذا ، بُرهانا على أنكَ غرست فأثمرتَ ، وبذرت فأنميتَ ، ودليلاً على أنَّ غِراسك سيزدَادُ نموًا بمَرَّ الأيام إلى أن يؤتي أكله مرتين بإذن الله». والحقُّ أنَّ الغِراس قد أتى أُكله مرّات عدة، فإنّ ما أخرجه الأستاذ الشيخ محمد محي الدين من الكتب العلمية تأليفا وتحقيقا ليدهش لها العلماء، ويعجز عنها القرناء.
Translation of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid. Regular study, and that in the year 1344 AH corresponding to 1925 CE, and he studied during that period under a generation of great spiritual scholars, and his success was astonishing, for he surpassed everyone and obtained the first rank among the elite of his peers among scholars. From his first authorship while a student: Among the greatest indications of the student's brilliance and the appearance of his crescent moon heralding what would follow of full moon... that he aspired to authorship while still a student before graduation, for he had a soul devoted to reading and study, and high ambition, and the fruit of that was his undertaking a detailed, comprehensive commentary on the Maqamat of Badi' al-Zaman al-Hamadhani, filled with pearls of scholarly benefits and explanation of literary and historical allusions, indicating that he had mastered the issues of language, literature, and Arab history which allowed him to excel in this commentary. And he published that work while still a student who had not yet obtained the degree of 'alimiyya, and he prefaced this commentary with a dedication to his father in recognition of his father's favor upon him and fulfillment of the duty of piety. For without his father's continuous guidance and urging, he would not have achieved what he achieved. And among what he said in that dedication to his father: 'To your pure soul, your high wisdom, your abundant refinement, and your vast merit... I present this book of mine. You raised me in virtue, and made me renounce ease and weakness, and with Allah is your reward for that. I have nothing in my hand from it, nor is it in my power to attain it even if I ascend the causes of the sky. But I advance to you with this book of mine, as proof that you planted and bore fruit, and sowed and made thrive, and as evidence that your planting will increase in growth with the passage of days until it yields its fruit twice by Allah's permission.' And the truth is that the planting has yielded its fruit many times; indeed, what the professor Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din has produced of scholarly books, authorship and editing, astonishes scholars and incapacitates peers.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative. It begins by describing the author's regular studies in 1925 under great scholars, and his exceptional success ranking first among his peers. It then focuses on his first authorship while still a student: a detailed commentary on the Maqamat of Badi' al-Zaman al-Hamadhani, which he published before graduating. The passage highlights his dedication, ambition, and mastery of language and literature. It includes the full text of his dedication to his father, acknowledging his father's role in his upbringing and encouragement. The passage concludes by noting that his scholarly output later exceeded all expectations, astonishing scholars and surpassing his contemporaries.

ألمعية
التأليف
شرح

Muhammad Muhyi al-Din's first publication, a commentary on the Maqamat, demonstrated his early brilliance and set the stage for a prolific scholarly career.

?
The author credited his father's continuous guidance for his success. Who in your life has been instrumental in your spiritual or intellectual growth, and when will you express genuine gratitude to them?
?
The passage describes a soul 'devoted to reading and study.' Is your soul similarly devoted to learning Islam? If not, what distraction do you need to renounce starting today to make room for that?

The Author's Teaching Career and High Positions
Lists the author's teaching career and various high academic positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the trajectory of the author's teaching career and the range of high academic positions he held, reflecting his scholarly prestige.

Core Idea
A distinguished scholar ascends through teaching and leadership roles.

This passage introduces us to the author's professional life—his early teaching, his selection for key academic posts, and his lasting influence. Reading it helps us appreciate how his knowledge was recognized and utilized in major Islamic institutions.

1
Read the Arabic passage aloud

The passage begins with his teaching career and then lists positions.

He became head of inspectors and a member of the Supreme Council for Islamic Affairs.

اشتغاله بالتدريس ومناصبه العليمة
اشتغل بالتدريس في المعاهد الأزهرية، وتولى التدريس بمعهد القاهرة الأزهري عقب تخرجه ، حتى إذا أُنشئت كليات الجامع الأزهر لأول مرة اختير للتدريس بكلية اللغة العربية سنة ( ١٣٥٠هـ) الموافق: (۱۹۳۱م) وكان أصغر أعضاء هيئة التدريس بالكلية سنا، ولكن مقامه العلمي دفعه إلى الصدارة، فاختير سنة ( ۱۹۳٥م) للتدريس بتخصص المادة لطلبة الدراسات العليا، وزامل الكبار من أساتذته واعترفوا بفضله.
شَغَلَه في هذه الحقبة الطويلة الكثير من المناصب العلمية الرفيعة: أستاذا بالأزهر، فأستاذا بكلية اللغة العربية، فمفتشا عاما بالمعاهد الدينية، فوكيلا لكلية اللغة العربية ، فأستاذا بكلية أصول الدين ، فرئيسا لمفتشي العلوم الدينية والعربية بالأزهر، وعضوا بالمجلس الأعلى للشؤون الإسلامية، واختير عام ( ١٩٤٠م) للمشاركة في إنشاء وتأسيس مدرسة الحقوق العليا في حكومة السودان الخرطوم، فشارك في وضع المناهج للعلوم الشرعية، وعمل هناك أستاذا للعلوم الشرعية.
His Engagement in Teaching and His High Positions: He engaged in teaching in the Azhar institutes, and undertook teaching at the Cairo Azhar Institute after his graduation, until when the colleges of al-Azhar University were established for the first time, he was selected to teach at the College of Arabic Language in the year 1350 AH corresponding to 1931 CE. He was the youngest member of the faculty in age, but his scholarly standing pushed him to the forefront, so he was selected in 1935 CE to teach the specialization subject for graduate students, and he associated with the great among his teachers and they acknowledged his merit. In this long period, he occupied many high academic positions: professor at al-Azhar, then professor at the College of Arabic Language, then general inspector of religious institutes, then vice-dean of the College of Arabic Language, then professor at the College of Usul al-Din, then head of inspectors of religious and Arabic sciences at al-Azhar, and member of the Supreme Council for Islamic Affairs. And in 1940 CE he was selected to participate in the establishment and founding of the High School of Law in the government of Sudan, Khartoum, so he participated in setting curricula for the Sharia sciences, and he worked there as a professor of Sharia sciences.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage lists the author's teaching career and academic positions. It begins with his teaching at Azhar institutes and later at the College of Arabic Language when it was first established, noting he was the youngest faculty member but his scholarly merit elevated him. It then enumerates a series of high positions he held over a long period: professor at al-Azhar, professor at the College of Arabic Language, general inspector of religious institutes, vice-dean, professor at the College of Usul al-Din, head of inspectors of religious and Arabic sciences, and member of the Supreme Council for Islamic Affairs. Finally, it mentions his involvement in founding a law school in Sudan where he taught Sharia sciences and helped develop curricula.

Biography of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din and His Scholarly Works
Biographical account of works and contributions of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of scholarly contributions of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, including his commentaries, editions of heritage works, and his efforts in writing for children.

Core Idea
A single scholar can revive whole fields: kalam, grammar, and children's education.

This passage introduces us to Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, the editor of the very book we are studying. It is important to know the person behind the text. By seeing his many works, we gain appreciation for his scholarly dedication and the tradition he represents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic text and its English translation once. Notice the numbered list of works and the later discussion of editorial projects and children's books.
2
Identify works related to kalam
The passage mentions two works directly connected to kalam: the commentary on al-Musayara and the gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed (which is this very book). Recognize their importance.
3
Observe the heritage editing effort
The passage lists many classical texts he edited. Note the variety of fields (theology, grammar, poetry, etc.) and his meticulous method.
4
Note the children's books and teacher's praise
He pioneered religious books for children. The praise from his teacher shows the high quality of his work.
5
Connect to the main text
Reflect on how his work on Ithaaf al-Mureed relates to the rest of his career—he was both a commentator and a publisher of heritage.
