والشيخ محمد محي الدين لم ينس أنْ يهتم بالنَّاشئة والجيل الجديد، وهو أول من فكر في تأليف كتب دينية مزدانة بما يناسب الأطفال، فألف خمسة كتب أجزاء اثنين للبنين ، واثنين للإناث، وكتابا مشتركا ، وقد ذاعت هذه الكتب آنذاك ، حتى كان المرحوم الدكتور عبد الوهاب عزام يذكر أنه شاهدها مترجمة بالفارسية والتركية.
نموذج من ثناء ومدح شيوخه له:
لما ألَّفَ الشيخ محمد محي الدين شرحه الماتع على «المسايرة» وكان في تلك الفترة مدرسا في القسم الثانوي في الأزهر الشريف، عرض شرحه على شيخه العلامة عبد المجيد اللبان، فكتب له بعد الديباجة: (ولدي العزيز الشيخ محمد الدين عبد الحميد! أهديك تحياتي ، وأُعلمك بأني قرير العين بما صنعت، قرأتُ كتابك: شرح المسايرة للكمال ابن الهمام» فأعجبني أسلوبه ، وسترني جزالته ، جمع من التوحيد ما جاء في كتاب الله فهو من الهدي وخير الهدي هداه خلا مِن التعقيد، وسما عن الابتذال، فكان سهلا ممتعا، بحر علم يُصحح عقيدة من قرأه، ومنهل تهذيب يثقف
Biography of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid. 2 - Among his important works related to the subject of this our book: his writing of a delightful, well-edited commentary on al-Musayara in the science of kalam, by Imam Kamal ibn al-Humam. 3 - A gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed, which he named al-Nizam al-Farid bi-Tahqiq Jawharat al-Tawhid, and it is included in this our book. 4 - And he also has: 'The Personal Status in Islamic Law'. 5 - And al-Tuhfa al-Saniyya bi-Sharh al-Muqaddima al-Ajurrumiyya. 6 - And a treatise on the etiquette of research and debate. - And 'Tasrif al-Af'al'. 8 - And he has a delightful gloss on Qatr al-Nada wa-Ball al-Sada. 9 - And a gloss on Sharh Shudhur al-Dhahab. 10 - And on Awḍah al-Masalik by Ibn Hisham in four volumes. 11 - And he has a commentary on the book al-Insaf fi Masa'il al-Khilaf bayn al-Basriyyin wa-al-Kufiyyin by Ibn al-Anbari. 12 - And he has an important gloss on Sharh al-Ushmuni in four volumes. 13 - And a commentary on al-Mufassal by al-Zamakhshari. 14 - And he has the book 'Tanqih al-Azhariyya'. This, and he has very great efforts in publishing heritage books, achieving them with superior, excellent editing, with great care in correcting the text, controlling the problematic, and explaining the obscure, in various arts and sciences, including, by way of example not limitation: Sharh Shafiyat Ibn al-Hajib, al-Mukhtar min al-Sihah, Adab al-Katib wa-al-Sha'ir by Ibn al-Athir, Nahj al-Balagha by al-Sharif al-Radi, al-Muwazana bayn Abi Tammam wa-al-Buhturi by al-Amidi, Wafa' al-Wafa bi-Akhbar Dar al-Mustafa by al-Samhudi, and from them Tawdih al-Afkar li-Ma'ani Tanqih al-Anzar by al-San'ani, al-Farq bayn al-Firaq by al-Baghdadi, Maqalat al-Islamiyyin by Imam al-Ash'ari, al-Targhib wa-al-Tarhib by al-Mundhiri, and other books of the treasures of heritage. And Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din did not forget to care for the youth and the new generation; he was the first to think of writing religious books adorned with what is suitable for children. So he wrote five books: two parts for boys, two for girls, and one joint book. These books became widespread at that time, so much so that the late Dr. Abd al-Wahhab Azzam mentioned that he saw them translated into Persian and Turkish. A sample of the praise and commendation of his teachers for him: When Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din wrote his delightful commentary on al-Musayara, and he was at that time a teacher in the secondary section of al-Azhar al-Sharif, he presented his commentary to his teacher, the scholar Abd al-Majid al-Laban, who wrote to him after the preamble: 'My dear son Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid! I send you my greetings, and I inform you that I am delighted with what you have done. I read your book: Sharh al-Musayara li-l-Kamal Ibn al-Humam, and I was impressed by its style, and its excellence covered me. It gathered from tawhid what came in the Book of Allah, so it is from guidance, and the best guidance is his guidance. It is free from complexity, and rises above triviality, so it is easy and delightful, a sea of knowledge that corrects the creed of whoever reads it, and a fountain of refinement that cultivates.'
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the scholar Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid, focusing on his scholarly output and achievements. It begins by listing his important works, many of which are commentaries and glosses on classical texts in various fields: kalam (theology), grammar, jurisprudence, and language. The list includes a commentary on al-Musayara in kalam, a gloss on Ithaaf al-Mureed (which is the very book we are studying), and works on Islamic personal status law, Arabic grammar (e.g., al-Ajurrumiyya, Qatr al-Nada), and research methodology. It then highlights his monumental efforts in editing and publishing heritage books, providing examples of key texts he worked on, such as commentaries on Ibn al-Hajib, al-Sihah, and classical works by Ibn al-Athir, al-Sharif al-Radi, al-Amidi, al-Samhudi, al-San'ani, al-Baghdadi, al-Ash'ari, and al-Mundhiri. The passage notes his pioneering role in writing simplified religious books for children, with five volumes for boys and girls. Finally, it presents a concrete example of recognition from his teacher, Abd al-Majid al-Laban, who praised his commentary on al-Musayara for its clarity, depth, and adherence to Quranic guidance, emphasizing that it avoids complexity and vulgarity while being intellectually stimulating and spiritually uplifting.

The Scholarly Legacy of Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid
Biography of the editor, his works, praise, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly credentials and contributions of the editor of this text, Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid.

Core Idea
A scholar who mastered multiple sciences and pioneered religious children's literature.

Before delving into the theological content of the book, it is important to know the man who edited it. This biography shows his vast knowledge, his innovation in writing for children, and the high praise he received from his teachers. Understanding his background helps us trust the quality of the edition.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation once. Note that this is a biography of the editor, not the author of the main text.
Pay attention to the list of works and the two pieces of praise.
2
Identify his scholarly works
The passage lists several books he published. These show his expertise in various fields: grammar, literature, history, theology, and more.
He also wrote children's books on religion, an innovation.
3
Analyze the praise from his teachers
Abd al-Majid al-Laban praises his commentary on 'al-Musayarah' for its clarity and doctrinal correctness. Muhammad Ali al-Najjar compares him to al-Tabari, saying he masters grammar, jurisprudence, hadith, and kalam.
Both teachers emphasize his breadth and depth.
4
Conclude with his character and death
The passage notes his intelligence, good conduct, and dedication to al-Azhar. His death date is given. This reinforces his reliability.
He died in 1972 at over seventy years of age.

And these books spread at that time, so much so that the late Dr. Abd al-Wahhab Azzam mentioned that he saw them translated into Persian and Turkish. A sample of the praise and commendation of his teachers for him: When Shaykh Muhammad Muhyi al-Din composed his delightful commentary on 'al-Musayarah' and was at that time a teacher in the secondary section at al-Azhar al-Sharif, he presented his commentary to his teacher the scholar Abd al-Majid al-Laban, who wrote to him after the preamble: 'My dear son, Shaykh Muhammad al-Din Abd al-Hamid! I send you my greetings, and inform you that I am delighted with what you have done. I read your book: Sharh al-Musayarah li al-Kamal Ibn al-Humann. I was impressed by its style, and its richness amazed me. It gathered from Tawhid what came in the Book of Allah, so it is from guidance, and the best guidance is its guidance, free from complexity and above commonness. It was easy and enjoyable, a sea of knowledge that corrects the creed of whoever reads it, and a fountain of refinement that cultivates the soul of whoever remembers it with a sound heart. May Allah benefit by you, accept your work, and reward you abundantly. Accept the praise of your affectionate father, admiring your talents: Abd al-Majid al-Laban. Muharram 1348 AH, corresponding to June 1929.' The statement of the scholar Muhammad Ali al-Najjar about him: And Shaykh Muhammad Ali al-Najjar, member of the Arabic Language Academy, said about him: 'It was said of al-Tabari: He was like a Qur'an reciter who knows only the Qur'an, and a hadith scholar who knows only hadith, and a jurist who knows only jurisprudence, and a grammarian who knows only grammar, and an arithmetician who knows only arithmetic. Likewise, it is said of Shaykh Muhyi al-Din: He is like a grammarian who knows only grammar, and a jurist who knows only jurisprudence, and a hadith scholar who knows only hadith, and a theologian who knows only kalam. And the proof of that is what he composed and published of books in these arts.' His death: In brief, he was a marvel in intelligence and cleverness, and good conduct, and zeal for al-Azhar, its history and its men. He was also known for moderation in speech, guarding himself, and controlling his behavior. He continued on that path until Allah the Exalted took his soul on (25) of Dhu al-Qa'dah of the year (1392 AH), corresponding to (30) December of the year (1972 CE), at over seventy years of age. May Allah have mercy on him, elevate his rank, honor his abode, and reward him well for Islam and the Muslims. (1) (1) Sources of the biography: The book 'al-Nahdah al-Islamiyyah fi Siyar A'lamiha al-Mu'asirin' by Dr. Ibrahim Rajab al-Bayyumi, and 'Madkhal ila Tarikh Nashr al-Turath al-Arabi' by the verifier professor Dr. Mahmud al-Tanahi, and the book 'Jumharat A'lam al-Azhar al-Sharif fi al-Qarnayn al-Rabi' Ashar wa al-Khamis Ashar al-Hijriyyayn' by Shaykh Dr. Usamah al-Sayyid al-Azhari.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the editor, Muhammad Muhyi al-Din Abd al-Hamid. It begins by listing some of his scholarly works across various disciplines, such as commentaries, literary works, and historical texts, establishing his expertise in multiple fields. It then highlights his unique contribution to writing religious books for children, an innovative idea that gained international recognition. The core of the passage presents two pieces of praise from his teachers. The first is a detailed letter from his teacher Abd al-Majid al-Laban, who commends his commentary on 'al-Musayarah' for its clarity, depth, and doctrinal correctness, calling it a sea of knowledge that corrects creed. The second praise is from Muhammad Ali al-Najjar, who compares him to al-Tabari in his mastery of multiple sciences, specifically stating that he excels in grammar, jurisprudence, hadith, and kalam (theology), as evidenced by his published works. The passage concludes with an account of his character and death, noting his intelligence, modesty, and dedication to al-Azhar, and provides the date of his death in both Hijri and Gregorian calendars, along with a prayer for mercy. A footnote lists the sources from which the biography is drawn. The overall purpose is to establish the editor's scholarly authority and virtuous character, lending credibility to his editorial work on the present book.

Eulogy of the Editor's Multiscience Expertise
A eulogy comparing the editor's scholarly breadth to al-Tabari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Muhammad Ali al-Najjar praised the editor by comparing his expertise to that of al-Tabari.

Core Idea
Muhammad Ali al-Najjar compares the editor's mastery to al-Tabari's legendary breadth.

This passage is a eulogy from the scholar Muhammad Ali al-Najjar, who lauds the editor's mastery across multiple Islamic sciences. He draws a parallel to the great scholar al-Tabari, about whom it was said he mastered each science so completely that one would think he only knew that science. This rhetorical device underscores the editor's exceptional versatility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the eulogy's flow and content.
Notice the repeated structure: 'like a ... who knows only ...'
2
Identify the key figure being praised
Recognize that the passage is about Shaykh Muhyi al-Din (the editor), and it compares him to al-Tabari, a renowned scholar of the past.
Al-Tabari is known for his tafsir and history, but here his multifield expertise is highlighted.
3
List the sciences mentioned
Make a list of the Islamic sciences: grammar (nahw), fiqh, hadith, kalam (theology). For al-Tabari, also qira'at and mathematics.
This illustrates the breadth of their knowledge.
4
Understand the rhetorical device
The phrase 'like a ... who knows only that science' is hyperbole to emphasize deep specialization. It does not mean they actually knew nothing else.
This is a common praise format in classical biographies.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why such a comparison elevates the editor: it places him among the most versatile scholars in Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلمة العلامة محمد علي النجار فيه
وقال عنه الشيخ محمد علي النجار عضو مجمع اللغة العربية: (لقد قيل في الطبري: إنه كان كالقارئ الذي لا يعرف إلا القرآن ، وكالمحدث الذي لا يعرف إلا الحديث، وكالفقيه الذي لا يعرف إلا الفقه، وكالنحوي الذي لا يعرف إلا النحو، وكالحاسب الذي لا يعرف إلا الحساب، وكذا يُقال في الشيخ محي الدين إنه كالنحوي الذي لا يعرف إلا النحو، وكالفقيه الذي لا يعرف إلا الفقه والمحدث الذي لا يعرف إلا الحديث ، وكالمتكلم الذي لا يعرف إلا الكلام، وآية ذلك ما ألّفه وأخرجه من الكتب في هذه الفنون).
The statement of the scholar Muhammad Ali al-Najjar about him: And the Shaykh Muhammad Ali al-Najjar, member of the Arabic Language Academy, said: 'It was said about al-Tabari: He was like a reciter who knows only the Quran, and like a muhaddith who knows only hadith, and like a faqih who knows only fiqh, and like a grammarian who knows only grammar, and like a mathematician who knows only mathematics. Likewise, it is said about Shaykh Muhyi al-Din: He is like a grammarian who knows only grammar, and like a faqih who knows only fiqh, and like a muhaddith who knows only hadith, and like a mutakallim who knows only kalam. And proof of that is what he authored and published of books in these arts.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a eulogy for the editor, Shaykh Muhyi al-Din, by the scholar Muhammad Ali al-Najjar. It begins by drawing a parallel to the famous scholar al-Tabari, about whom it was said he mastered each Islamic science to the point of being known only for that science. The eulogy then applies this to Shaykh Muhyi al-Din, listing his expertise in grammar, fiqh, hadith, and kalam, implying he is equally proficient in each. The passage concludes by pointing to his authored works as evidence of his breadth. The structure follows a parallelism: what was said about al-Tabari is said about the editor.

Correction: The phrase 'like a grammarian who knows only grammar' is a rhetorical hyperbole to emphasize deep specialization; it actually indicates mastery of multiple sciences, not limitation.

The Author's Humble Self-Introduction
Al-Laqani introduces himself with humble epithets and his full name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Laqani introduces himself with deep humility and why this style is significant in Islamic scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Humility is the first credential of a scholar.

Al-Laqani opens his work not with self-praise but with self-abasement, calling himself a poor, lowly, perishing slave. This sets the tone for the entire text: knowledge is a gift from Allah, not a personal achievement. Let's examine his words carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the self-introduction
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the sequence of epithets and the author's name.
2
Understand the epithets
Identify each adjective: 'al-ʿabd' (the slave), 'al-faqīr' (the poor), 'al-ḥaqīr' (the lowly), 'al-fānī' (the perishing). Reflect on what each emphasizes about human dependence on Allah.
These are not mere formalities; they carry deep theological meaning.
3
Reflect on scholarly humility
Consider why a scholar would begin a theological work with such humility. What does it teach about the proper attitude for seeking knowledge?
This connects to the broader Islamic emphasis on sincerity and reliance on Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد فيقول العبد الفقير الحقير (۲) الفاني (۳) ، عبد السلام بن إبراهيم المالكي (٤) اللقاني، ستر الله عيوبه ، وغفر ذنوبَهُ: قد كنتُ لخصت (٥) ما علقه أستاذنا (٦) من عُمْدَةِ المُرِيدِ» على عقيدته
And after: So says the slave, the poor, the lowly, the perishing, ʿAbd al-Salām ibn Ibrāhīm al-Mālikī al-Laqānī—may Allah cover his faults and forgive his sins—: I have indeed summarized what our teacher (ustādhunā) annotated from 'ʿUmdat al-Murīd' upon his creed.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is the author's self-introduction and statement of purpose. After the opening praises (implied by 'wa baʿd'), the author refers to himself using a series of humble epithets: 'al-ʿabd al-faqīr al-ḥaqīr al-fānī' (the slave, the poor, the lowly, the perishing). He then gives his full name: ʿAbd al-Salām ibn Ibrāhīm al-Mālikī al-Laqānī, followed by a prayer for forgiveness. Next he declares that he has made a summary (lakhkhaṣtu) of what 'our teacher' (ustādhunā) wrote as annotations (taʿlīq) from the work 'ʿUmdat al-Murīd' on his creed (ʿaqīdah). 'Ustādhunā' here refers to his father (as the footnote explains), so the author is presenting his work as a digest of his father's commentary on the original poem (Jawharat al-Tawḥīd). The phrase 'min ʿumdat al-murīd ʿalā ʿaqīdatihi' indicates the source: the book 'ʿUmdat al-Murīd' which is a commentary on the author's own creedal poem. This establishes the work as a filial and scholarly transmission.

Key Terms
العبد الفقير الحقير
اللقاني
ستر الله عيوبه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author is being overly self-deprecating or that it's just a routine formula.
Correction: The epithets are carefully chosen to express the Islamic teaching that humans are entirely dependent on Allah, especially when engaging in theology. It is a conscious act of worship and humility.

Checkpoint

A) The wise and learned
B) The poor and lowly slave
C) The honored master
D) The proud scholar

Key Takeaway
Al-Laqani's humble self-introduction grounds the entire work in a posture of dependence on Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to introduce yourself as Al-Laqani does—as a slave, poor, lowly, perishing—how would that change the way you see yourself right now? Would you still cling to your titles and achievements?
?
Think of a time you felt proud of your knowledge or status. How would Al-Laqani's prayer 'may Allah cover his faults' reshape that moment? What faults are you hiding that you haven't asked Allah to cover?
?
Al-Laqani could have listed his scholarly credentials first. Instead, he led with utter dependence. When you introduce yourself—at work, among friends, even in your own mind—what comes first: your accomplishments or your need for Allah? What would it cost you to reverse that order starting today?

Al-Laqani states he summarized his teacher's annotations from 'Umdat al-Murīd' on his creed.

Author's Purpose and the Student's Criticism
Author explains his purpose and a student's criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Laqqani wrote this commentary and how a student's criticism prompted him to expand his earlier summary.

Core Idea
A critic's words can motivate deeper scholarship.

This lesson introduces the author al-Laqqani and the story behind the writing of Ithaaf al-Mureed. A student's criticism of a shorter work led him to compose a fuller commentary, showing how even criticism can drive beneficial knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's self-identification
Notice the author's humble description of himself as 'the humble, lowly, and mortal servant' and his invocation for forgiveness. This sets a tone of humility and dependence on Allah.
The author, 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, is a Maliki scholar.
2
Understand the earlier summary work
The author explains that he had previously summarized his father's commentary ('Umdat al-Murid') on the creedal poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' into a short work called 'Irshad al-Murid'. This contained the chosen Sunni doctrines without addition.
The father, Ibrahim al-Laqqani, wrote the original poem and commentary.
3
Identify the student's criticism
A student from Takrur (a region in North Africa) obtained the summary and expressed something indicating weak resolve and distant aspiration. The author quotes a poetic line: 'Be a man whose foot is in the earth and the peak of his resolve is in the Pleiades.'
The criticism likely was that the summary was too brief or lacked depth.
4
Recognize the author's response
The author hastened to address the student's concern by writing a fuller commentary, citing the hadith: 'The one who guides to good is like the doer of it.' This explains his motivation for composing Ithaaf al-Mureed.
The hadith wisdom: guiding others to knowledge is rewarded like performing the good deed.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this passage shows the author's humility, responsiveness to criticism, and commitment to spreading sound creed. His intention is pedagogical and sincere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بجواهر الفرائد (۱) . وبعد مقدمة المصنف فيقول العبد الفقير الحقير (۲) الفاني (۳) ، عبد السلام بن إبراهيم المالكي (٤) اللقاني، ستر الله عيوبه ، وغفر ذنوبَهُ: قد كنتُ لخصت (٥) ما علقه أستاذنا (٦) من عُمْدَةِ المُرِيدِ» على عقيدته المُسمَّاة جَوْهَرة التَّوحِيد في أوراق قليلةٍ سمَّيْتُها إِرْشَادَ المُريد» ضمَّنتُها مُختارَ أهل السُّنَّة من غير مزيد، فحينَ أَخرجته وتناوله بعض طلبة التكْرُور (۱) ، ضاعف الله لي ولهم الخيرات والأجور، أفصَحَ بما يُنْبِيُّ عن قصور همَّتِه ، وتَنَائى رغبته ، ولَيْته (۲) نظر إلى قوله : فَكُنْ رَجُلًا رِجْلُهُ فِي الثَّرَى وَهَامَةُ هِمَّتِه فِي الثَّرَيَّا (۳) فبادرتُ إلى إسْعَافِه بصَرْفِ شاغِله ؛ لِما جاءَ (٤): «أَنَّ الدَّال على الخير
With the jewels of the unique pearls (1). After the introduction of the author, the humble, lowly, and mortal servant (2), 'Abd al-Salam ibn Ibrahim al-Maliki (4) al-Laqqani—may Allah cover his faults and forgive his sins—says: I had summarized (5) what our teacher (6) [my father] wrote from the 'Umdat al-Murid' on his creed named Jawharat al-Tawhid in a few folios, which I named 'Irshad al-Murid'. I included in it the chosen [doctrines] of Ahl al-Sunna without addition. Then, when I published it and some students from Takrur (1)—may Allah multiply blessings for me and them—took it up, he expressed something indicating deficiency of his resolve and distance of his desire. Would that he had (2) looked at his saying: 'So be a man whose foot is in the earth and the peak of his resolve is in the Pleiades' (3). So I hastened to aid him by diverting his distraction, because of what has come (4): 'Indeed, the one who guides to good
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the author's introduction. It begins with the title phrase 'With the jewels of the unique pearls' (which likely refers to the book's title or a dedicatory phrase, with the footnote explaining 'jewels' as necklaces and 'unique pearls' as precious independent gems). Then the author identifies himself humbly as 'Abd al-Salam ibn Ibrahim al-Maliki al-Laqqani, invoking Allah's forgiveness. He states his prior work: he had summarized his father's commentary (the 'Umdat al-Murid') on his father's creedal poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' into a short work called 'Irshad al-Murid', which contained the sound Sunni creed without excess. After publishing it, a student from the Takrur region (a place in North Africa) criticized it, showing weak resolve and distant aspiration. The author wishes the student had considered the poetic advice: 'Be a man whose foot is on the ground but whose ambition reaches the Pleiades' (i.e., have lofty aims despite humble beginnings). Consequently, the author hastened to address the student's concern by redirecting his attention, citing the hadith that 'the one who guides to good is like the doer of it.' The author thus explains his motivation for writing the present commentary: to provide a more thorough explanation to help the critic and others.

إرشاد المريد
مختار أهل السنة
التكرور

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author wrote this commentary solely for self-praise or to show off his knowledge.
Correction: Al-Laqqani explicitly states he wrote in response to a critic's deficiency and to guide him, citing the hadith about guiding to good.

Checkpoint
Why did the author write the present commentary (Ithaaf al-Mureed) according to the introduction?
A) To earn money from students
B) Because a student criticized his earlier summary and he wanted to help him
C) To oppose the doctrines of Ahl al-Sunna
D) To create a longer work than his father's

Key Takeaway
Al-Laqqani's commentary was born from a desire to help a student whose critique revealed a need for deeper explanation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone criticizes your efforts or knowledge, does your first reaction protect your ego or seek to understand the underlying need? How can you train yourself to respond like al-Laqqani—turning criticism into an opportunity to serve?
?
Al-Laqqani wrote an entire commentary for 'some students from Takrur'—not for fame, but to help a few. Is your pursuit of knowledge driven by a desire to be seen or to be useful? What concrete step can you take this week to share knowledge purely for Allah's sake?
?
The student expressed 'deficiency of resolve' and 'distance of desire.' When you feel your own spiritual or academic motivation flagging, do you seek external help or retreat? What would it mean for you to be a 'man whose foot is in the earth and the peak of his resolve in the Pleiades'? What one area of your life needs that renewal of high aim?

Early Life and Quest for Knowledge
Biographical account of Zakariya al-Ansari's early life and poverty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life challenges and determination of Sheikh al-Islam Zakariya al-Ansari in seeking knowledge.

Core Idea
Poverty and hardship can fuel the pursuit of knowledge.

Sheikh Zakariya al-Ansari's biography begins with his humble origins. Abandoned to poverty and orphaned, his early life was marked by severe deprivation. Yet, his unwavering commitment to learning even in the face of hunger shaped his character. This passage recounts his early struggles and the divine assistance that came to him.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview of his early life, then read the translation to grasp the details.
2
Identify key events
Notice the sequence: his birth, orphan status, memorization of Quran, travel to Azhar, and the extreme poverty he endured.
Focus on the watermelon rinds story as a sign of his patience.
3
Reflect on the moral
Consider how this story illustrates the value of perseverance in seeking knowledge despite worldly hardships.
This is a recurring theme in classical biographies.

هو الإمام زين الدين أبو يحيى زكريا بن محمد بن زكريا الأنصاري الخزرجي المصري مولدا، الشافعي الأشعري، شيخ مشايخ الإسلام، قاضي القضاة، ولد سنة (٨٢٤ هـ) في قرية «سنيكة) بمصر نشأ في قريته يتيما فقيرا ، وقامت على رعايته أم صالحة أسلمته إلى شيخ صالح تكفل به فحفظ القرآن وعمدة الأحكام ، ثم رحل إلى القاهرة والتحق بالأزهر سنة (٨٤١) هـ) وعانى الفقر والحرمان وقال كما في طبقات الشعراني»: جئت من البلاد وأنا شاب فلم أعكف على الاشتغال بشيء من أمور الدنيا ، ولم أعلق قلبي بأحد من الخلق ، وكنت أجوع في الجامع كثيرا ، فأخرج في الليل إلى الميضأة وغيرها; فأغسل ما أجده من قشيرات البطيخ واكلها ، وأقنع بها ، فأقمت على ذلك سنين، ثم إن الله تعالى قيض لي شخصاً مِن أولياء الله ، كان يعمل في الطواحين في غَرْبَلة القمح، فكان يتفقدني، ويشتري لي ما أحتاج إليه من الأكل والشرب والكسوة والكتب. من شيوخه الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني، وعلم الدين البلقيني، والكافيجي، وغيرهم الكثير ، وورد أنه بلغ عددهم مئة وخمسين شيخا . من تلامذته الشيخ الشعراني ، ولازمه عشرين سنة، والشيخ شهاب الدين عميرة البرلسي، والإمام شمس الدين الرملي ووالده الشهاب الرملي والإمام الشهاب أحمد بن حجر الهيتمي ، والعلامة الخطيب الشربيني ، وغيرهم خلق لا يحصون . من مؤلفاته: إحكام الدلالة على تحرير شرح الرسالة وهو شرح على «الرسالة القشيرية» في التصوف. وتحفة الباري بشرح صحيح البخاري» وله: «الحدود الأنيقة والتعريفات الدقيقة» وله: «حاشية على شرح المحلي على جمع الجوامع وله أيضا: «المطلع شرح إيساغوجي في المنطق، وله فتح الإله الماجد بإيضاح شرح العقائد» ومن مؤلفاته الفقهية العالية: أسنى المطالب في شرح روض الطالب وقد قاربت مؤلفاته المئة . وفاته لما بلغ من العمر (۱۰۲) سنة ، توفي شيخ الإسلام زكريا في عام (٩٢٦ هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه، ودفن في القاهرة بالقرب من قبر إمام الدنيا الإمام الشافعي.
He is Imam Zayn al-Din Abu Yahya Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn Zakariyya al-Ansari al-Khazraji al-Misri by birth, the Shafi'i Ash'ari, Shaykh of the Scholars of Islam, Judge of Judges. He was born in the year 824 AH in a village called 'Sanika' in Egypt, and grew up in his village as an orphan in poverty. His righteous mother took care of him and entrusted him to a righteous shaykh who sponsored him, so he memorized the Qur'an and 'Umdat al-Ahkam. Then he traveled to Cairo and joined al-Azhar in the year 841 AH, enduring poverty and deprivation. He said, as in Tabaqat al-Sha'rani: 'I came from the countryside as a youth, and I did not occupy myself with any worldly matter, nor did I attach my heart to anyone among creation. I often went hungry in the mosque, so at night I would go to the ablution place and elsewhere, and wash and eat the watermelon rinds I found, content with that. I remained thus for years. Then Allah appointed for me a person from among the saints of Allah, who worked in the mills sifting wheat, and he would check on me and buy for me what I needed of food, drink, clothing, and books.' Among his teachers: al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, 'Alam al-Din al-Bulqini, al-Kafiji, and many others. It is reported that they numbered one hundred and fifty shaykhs. Among his students: al-Sha'rani, who accompanied him for twenty years, Shihab al-Din 'Umaira al-Barlisi, Imam Shams al-Din al-Ramli and his father al-Shihab al-Ramli, Imam al-Shihab Ahmad ibn Hajar al-Haytami, al-Allama al-Khatib al-Shirbini, and countless others. Among his works: Ihkam al-Dilala 'ala Tahrir Sharh al-Risala, a commentary on al-Risala al-Qushayriyya in Sufism; Tuhfat al-Bari bi-Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari; al-Hudud al-Aniqa wa al-Ta'rifat al-Daqiqa; a gloss on the commentary of al-Mahalli on Jam' al-Jawami'; al-Muttala' Sharh Isaghuji in logic; Fath al-Ilah al-Majid bi-Idah Sharh al-'Aqa'id; and among his great juridical works: Asna al-Matalib fi Sharh Rawd al-Talib. His works nearly reached one hundred. His death: he lived to the age of 102 years; Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya died in the year 926 AH, may Allah have mercy on him and elevate his rank. He was buried in Cairo near the grave of the Imam of the world, Imam al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Sheikh al-Islam Zakariya al-Ansari, the commentator of the text. It provides his full name, lineage, birth, and early life, emphasizing his poverty and hardship in seeking knowledge. It then lists his teachers, notably Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, and his students, such as al-Sha'rani and Ibn Hajar al-Haytami. It enumerates his major works in various fields including Sufism, hadith, jurisprudence, logic, and creed. The biography concludes with his age at death (102 years), the year (926 AH), and his burial place near Imam al-Shafi'i.

He studied under eminent scholars like Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani and taught many who became leading figures. His nearly one hundred works span various Islamic sciences, cementing his reputation as a prolific and influential scholar.

هو الإمام زين الدين أبو يحيى زكريا بن محمد بن زكريا الأنصاري الخزرجي المصري مولدا، الشافعي الأشعري، شيخ مشايخ الإسلام، قاضي القضاة، ولد سنة (٨٢٤ هـ) في قرية «سنيكة) بمصر نشأ في قريته يتيما فقيرا ، وقامت على رعايته أم صالحة أسلمته إلى شيخ صالح تكفل به فحفظ القرآن وعمدة الأحكام ، ثم رحل إلى القاهرة والتحق بالأزهر سنة (٨٤١) هـ) وعانى الفقر والحرمان وقال كما في طبقات الشعراني»: جئت من البلاد وأنا شاب فلم أعكف على الاشتغال بشيء من أمور الدنيا ، ولم أعلق قلبي بأحد من الخلق ، وكنت أجوع في الجامع كثيرا ، فأخرج في الليل إلى الميضأة وغيرها؛ فأغسل ما أجده من قشيرات البطيخ واكلها ، وأقنع بها ، فأقمت على ذلك سنين، ثم إن الله تعالى قيض لي شخصاً مِن أولياء الله ، كان يعمل في الطواحين في غَرْبَلة القمح، فكان يتفقدني، ويشتري لي ما أحتاج إليه من الأكل والشرب والكسوة والكتب.
من شيوخه الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني، وعلم الدين البلقيني، والكافيجي، وغيرهم الكثير ، وورد أنه بلغ عددهم مئة وخمسين شيخا .
من تلامذته الشيخ الشعراني ، ولازمه عشرين سنة، والشيخ شهاب الدين عميرة البرلسي، والإمام شمس الدين الرملي ووالده الشهاب الرملي والإمام الشهاب أحمد بن حجر الهيتمي ، والعلامة الخطيب الشربيني ، وغيرهم خلق لا يحصون .
من مؤلفاته: إحكام الدلالة على تحرير شرح الرسالة وهو شرح على «الرسالة القشيرية» في التصوف. وتحفة الباري بشرح صحيح البخاري» وله: «الحدود الأنيقة والتعريفات الدقيقة» وله: «حاشية على شرح المحلي على جمع الجوامع وله أيضا: «المطلع شرح إيساغوجي في المنطق، وله فتح الإله الماجد بإيضاح شرح العقائد» ومن مؤلفاته الفقهية العالية: أسنى المطالب في شرح روض الطالب وقد قاربت مؤلفاته المئة . وفاته لما بلغ من العمر (۱۰۲) سنة ، توفي شيخ الإسلام زكريا في عام (٩٢٦ هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه، ودفن في القاهرة بالقرب من قبر إمام الدنيا الإمام الشافعي.
He is Imam Zayn al-Din Abu Yahya Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn Zakariyya al-Ansari al-Khazraji, Egyptian by birth, al-Shafi‘i al-Ash‘ari, Shaykh of the Shaykhs of Islam, Chief Judge. He was born in the year 824 AH in a village called 'Sunayka' in Egypt. He grew up in his village an orphan and poor, and a righteous mother took care of him and entrusted him to a righteous shaykh who took charge of him, so he memorized the Qur'an and 'Umdat al-Ahkam. Then he traveled to Cairo and joined al-Azhar in the year 841 AH, and endured poverty and deprivation. He said, as in Tabaqat al-Sha‘rani: 'I came from the countryside as a youth and did not occupy myself with anything of worldly affairs, nor did I attach my heart to any creature. I often went hungry in the mosque, so I would go out at night to the ablution place and other places, washing what I found of melon peels and eating them, and I was content with that. I remained like that for years. Then Allah Almighty provided for me a person from among Allah's saints, who worked in the mills sifting wheat; he would check on me and buy for me what I needed of food, drink, clothing, and books.' His teachers include al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-‘Asqalani, ‘Alam al-Din al-Bulqini, al-Kafiji, and many others, and it is reported that their number reached one hundred and fifty shaykhs. His students include al-Shaykh al-Sha‘rani (who accompanied him for twenty years), al-Shaykh Shihab al-Din ‘Umaira al-Burlusi, Imam Shams al-Din al-Ramli and his father al-Shihab al-Ramli, Imam al-Shihab Ahmad ibn Hajar al-Haytami, al-‘Allama al-Khatib al-Shirbini, and countless others. His works include: Ihkam al-Dalala ‘ala Tahrir Sharh al-Risala (a commentary on al-Risala al-Qushayriyya on Sufism); Tuhfat al-Bari bi-Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari; al-Hudud al-Aniqa wa al-Ta‘rifat al-Daqiqa; a gloss on al-Mahalli's commentary on Jam‘ al-Jawami‘; al-Mutalla‘ Sharh Isaghuji on logic; Fath al-Ilah al-Majid bi-Idah Sharh al-‘Aqa’id; and among his high-level fiqh works: Asna al-Mutalib fi Sharh Rawd al-Talib. His works nearly reached one hundred. His death: when he reached the age of 102 years, Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya died in the year 926 AH, may Allah have mercy on him and elevate his rank, and he was buried in Cairo near the grave of the Imam of the world, Imam al-Shafi‘i.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya al-Ansari (d. 926 AH), a prominent Shafi‘i-Ash‘ari scholar. It begins by giving his full name, lineage, and honorifics: Imam Zayn al-Din Abu Yahya Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn Zakariyya al-Ansari al-Khazraji, Egyptian by birth, Shafi‘i in fiqh, Ash‘ari in creed, known as Shaykh of the Shaykhs of Islam and Chief Judge. His birth year is given as 824 AH in a village called Sunayka in Egypt. He grew up orphaned and poor; his mother placed him under a righteous shaykh who taught him the Qur'an and the hadith collection 'Umdat al-Ahkam. Then he moved to Cairo and joined al-Azhar in 841 AH. The passage then quotes a personal account from Tabaqat al-Sha‘rani describing his extreme poverty and self-deprivation, yet he remained patient and dedicated to learning. Later, a pious person working in the mills supported him with food, clothing, and books. It then lists his teachers, including Ibn Hajar al-‘Asqalani, al-Bulqini, and al-Kafiji, numbering about 150. His students include al-Sha‘rani (who stayed with him 20 years), al-Ramli, Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, and many others. His many works are enumerated, covering hadith, fiqh, logic, creed, and Sufism, nearly 100 works. Finally, the notice records his death at age 102 in 926 AH and his burial near Imam al-Shafi‘i in Cairo.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Zakariyya al-Ansari endured years of hunger, eating discarded melon peels and relying on the charity of a mill worker, all for the sake of knowledge. What are you willing to give up in your own life—comfort, time, reputation—to truly seek knowledge that brings you closer to Allah? Write one concrete action you will take this week to prioritize sacred knowledge over worldly distractions.
?
He did not attach his heart to any creature (لم أعلق قلبي بأحد من الخلق). Is there a person, possession, or status that your heart clings to more than Allah? Identify it honestly. What would it cost you to detach your heart from it and realign your attachment solely to Allah, as Zakariyya did?
?
At the height of his scholarly career, Zakariyya taught hundreds of students, authored nearly 100 works, and became the Shaykh of Islam. Yet he started as an orphan in poverty, utterly dependent on Allah's provision. Do you believe that your current circumstances—whether privilege or hardship—are the ultimate determinant of your spiritual success? Or do you trust that Allah can elevate anyone? Repent of any despair or pride you feel about your situation, and write a prayer asking for reliance on Allah alone.

Biography of Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani
Shanwani gives a brief biography of Ibn Hajar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the key biographical details of the great hadith scholar Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, as summarized by Shanwani.

Core Idea
Ibn Hajar was called the Commander of the Faithful in Hadith.

Shanwani provides a concise biographical sketch of one of the most celebrated hadith scholars, Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani. This passage highlights his title, his birth and death dates, and a touching anecdote from his funeral. Let's explore the life of this towering figure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the biographical details emerge naturally.
Notice the respectful title 'Commander of the Faithful in Hadith'.
2
Identify key biographical facts
Extract the full name, birth year, death year, and the title given to Ibn Hajar. Write them down.
3
Reflect on al-Suyuti's statement
Consider al-Suyuti's claim that the art (of hadith) ended with Ibn Hajar. Ask yourself what this says about his stature.
This reflects the high esteem in which he was held.
4
Contemplate the funeral anecdote
Read about the miraculous rain during his funeral. Think about the symbolism of rain as a sign of blessing.
The poet's verse connects the collapse of a pillar to the loss of a great scholar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (قال الحافظ :أي: الإمام أحمد بن علي بن محمد بن علي بن حجر العسقلاني ، كان يدعى أمير المؤمنين في الحديث الله ، ولد سنة ثلاث وسبعين وسبع مئة ، وتوفي في ذي القعدة سنة اثنتين وخمسين وثمان مئة . قال السيوطي وختم به الفن، قال وحدثني الشهاب المنصوري شاعر العصر أنه حضر جنازته فأمطرت السماء على نعشه وقد قرب إلى المصلى، ولم يكن زمان مطر فأنشدت في الوقت: قد بكث السُّحب على قاضي القضاة بالمطر وانهدَم الركن الذي كان مشيدا بالحجر. الشنواني .
His saying: 'Al-Ḥāfiẓ said' means: the Imām Aḥmad ibn ʿAlī ibn Muḥammad ibn ʿAlī ibn Ḥajar al-ʿAsqalānī, who was called the Commander of the Faithful in Hadith. He was born in the year 773 AH and died in Dhū al-Qaʿdah in the year 852 AH. Al-Suyūṭī said: The art came to an end with him. He said: And al-Shihāb al-Manṣūrī, the poet of the age, told me that he attended his funeral, and the sky rained upon his bier when it was brought near the prayer place, and it was not a time of rain, so he recited on the spot: 'The clouds have rained upon the judge of judges with rain, and the pillar that was erected with stone has collapsed.' Al-Shanwānī.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note about al-Ḥāfiẓ Ibn Ḥajar al-ʿAsqalānī, the renowned hadith scholar. It gives his full name, his title 'Commander of the Faithful in Hadith', his birth (773 AH) and death (852 AH) dates. It also includes a quote from al-Suyūṭī that the science of hadith ended with him, and an anecdote from a poet about a miraculous rain during his funeral. The note concludes with the commentator's attribution (al-Shanwānī).

Biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Biography of Imam al-Ash‘ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, lineage, and legacy of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari, the founder of the Ash‘ari school, and his role in preserving Sunni creed.

Core Idea
Al-Ash‘ari was not just a theologian; he was a defender of orthodoxy with a lineage to a Companion.

This biography introduces us to the man whose name defines a school. Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari was a pivotal figure in Islamic theology. The passage covers his lineage, birth, titles, students, and death, showing his integral role in Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic source passage carefully, then read the English translation. Notice the flow from lineage and titles to achievements and students.
Pay special attention to the list of students; they are part of his lasting legacy.
2
Identify key titles and lineage
Look at how the author describes al-Ash‘ari: 'shaykh of the school', 'Imam of the mutakallimun', 'defender of Islam'. Note that his lineage goes back to a Companion, Abu Musa al-Ash‘ari.
This lineage gives him added credibility in Sunni tradition.
3
Summarize his life milestones
Extract the birth year (260 AH), death year (324 AH on the most correct view), and the names of his prominent students mentioned. This forms the core biographical data.
The author also mentions his lasting effort in preserving creed.
4
Reflect on his legacy and the author's prayer
The passage ends with a prayer for al-Ash‘ari. Consider why the author emphasizes that his students are among his 'good deeds' and what this means for the Ash‘ari school.
This connects his personal role to the continuity of the school after his death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو شيخُ المذهب ورأسه، أبو الحسن علي بن إسماعيل بن أبي بشر بن إسحاق بن سالم بن إسماعيل بن عبد الله بن موسى بن أبي بردة بن أبي موسى الأشعري، صاحب رسول الله , ولد سنة (٢٦٠هـ) فهو شيخ طريقة أهل السنة والجماعة , وإمام المتكلمين , وناصر سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم , والذَّاب عن عقائد الإسلام، سعى في حفظ عقيدة أهل السنة والجماعة سَعياً يبقى أثره إلى يوم الدين , وشهرته العظيمة في الآفاق تُغني عن الإطالة بالتعريف به. توفي الأشعري له سنة (٣٢٤هـ) على الأصح , وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وثلاث مئة» ومن آثاره العظيمة أنه تَربَّى على يديه تلاميذُ كبار القدر في العلم والعمل، أكملوا بعده جهد شيخهم وحموا حمى أصول الدين، منهم: الإمام ابن مجاهد الطائي , وأبو الحسن الباهلي، وأبو بكر القفال الشاشي , وأبو سهل الصعلوكي وغيرهم كثير , وكلهم من حسنات الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري برَّد الله مضجعه ورضي عنه، وجزاه الله عن أهل السنة والجماعة خيراً كثيراً .
He is the shaykh of the school (madhhab) and its head, Abu al-Hasan ‘Ali ibn Isma‘il ibn Abi Bishr ibn Ishaq ibn Salim ibn Isma‘il ibn ‘Abdullah ibn Musa ibn Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash‘ari, a Companion of the Messenger of Allah (ṣallā llāhu ‘alayhi wa-sallam). He was born in the year 260 AH. He is the shaykh of the way (ṭarīqa) of Ahl al-Sunna wa-l-Jamā‘a, the Imam of the mutakallimūn, the supporter of the Sunna of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the defender of the doctrines of Islam. He strove in preserving the creed of Ahl al-Sunna wa-l-Jamā‘a with an effort whose trace remains until the Day of Judgment. His great fame in the horizons dispenses with prolonging his introduction. Al-Ash‘ari died in the year 324 AH according to the most correct view, and it is said: a little over thirty and three hundred? And among his great achievements is that under his care there grew great students in knowledge and action who completed after him the effort of their shaykh and protected the principles of the religion. Among them: Imam Ibn Mujāhid al-Ṭā’ī, Abu al-Ḥasan al-Bāhilī, Abu Bakr al-Qaffāl al-Shāshī, Abu Sahl al-Ṣa‘lūkī, and many others. All of them are among the good deeds of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari. May Allah cool his resting place, be pleased with him, and reward him richly on behalf of Ahl al-Sunna wa-l-Jamā‘a.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This is a biographical sketch of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari, the founder of the Ash‘ari school of theology. The author begins by affirming his status as the shaykh and head of the madhhab. He provides his full lineage, tracing back to Abu Musa al-Ash‘ari, a Companion of the Prophet. His birth year is given as 260 AH. He is described as the guide of Ahl al-Sunna, the imam of the mutakallimūn, and the defender of the Prophet's Sunna and Islamic creeds. The author emphasizes his lasting efforts in preserving Sunni creed. His death is given as 324 AH, with an alternative opinion. The passage then highlights his contribution through his students, listing four prominent disciples who continued his work and protected usul al-din (principles of religion). The author concludes with a prayer for him, acknowledging his great impact.

Correction: The passage shows his lineage to a Companion, his titles as supporter of the Sunna and defender of Islam, and his role as shaykh of Ahl al-Sunna, confirming his orthodox credentials.

Who is al-Qadi al-Baqillani?
Identifying al-Baqillani as the 'Qadi' and highlighting his scholarly status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity, scholarly rank, and significance of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani within the Ash'ari tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani is the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna and mujaddid of the fourth century.

This lesson introduces a key figure in Ash'ari theology. Whenever you see 'al-Qadi' in classical Ash'ari works on usul al-din, it refers to Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. His biography clarifies his lineage, rank, and legacy as a leading mutakallim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall content.
2
Identify his connection to al-Ash'ari
Notice that al-Baqillani is a student of a student of Imam al-Ash'ari, placing him in the second generation of Ash'aris.
This shows his direct intellectual lineage.
3
Understand his titles
The passage calls him 'standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna' and 'renewer of the fourth century'. Reflect on what these titles imply about his role.
These titles highlight his leadership and orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندما يُطلق القاضي في كتب أصول الدين عند السادة الأشاعرة فالمراد به الباقلاني، وهو القاضي أبو بكر محمد بن الطيب الباقلاني البصري الأشعري، تلميذ تلميذ الإمام الأشعري شيخ المذهب، وناصر طريقته , فهو من الطبقة الثانية من أصحاب الأشعري، وهو حامل لواء أهل السنة , مُجدد المئة الرابعة , يُضرب به المثل في سعة العلم وشدة الذكاء، من كبار المتكلمين وأجلهم قدراً , توفي ببغداد سنة (٤٠٣هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه.
When 'al-Qāḍī' is used in the books of Uṣūl al-Dīn among the Ash‘arī masters, what is meant by him is al-Bāqillānī. He is al-Qāḍī Abu Bakr Muḥammad ibn al-Ṭayyib al-Bāqillānī al-Baṣrī al-Ash‘arī, the student of the student of Imam al-Ash‘arī, the shaykh of the madhhab, and the supporter of his way. So he is from the second layer of the companions of al-Ash‘arī. He is the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna, the renewer (mujaddid) of the fourth century. He is proverbial in the breadth of knowledge and sharpness of intelligence. He is among the greatest mutakallimūn and the most eminent in rank. He died in Baghdad in the year 403 AH. May Allah have mercy on him and elevate his station.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This brief biography identifies the commonly used title 'al-Qāḍī' in Ash‘arī works as referring to Abu Bakr al-Bāqillānī. The author provides his full name, his connection to al-Ash‘arī (student of a student), and places him in the second generation of Ash‘arīs. He is described as the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna and the mujaddid (renewer) of the fourth Islamic century. His reputation for vast knowledge and intelligence is proverbial. His death year is given as 403 AH in Baghdad. The author concludes with a supplication for mercy and elevation of his rank.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that 'al-Qadi' in Ash'ari usul al-din books specifically means al-Baqillani, not any other Qadi.

Al-Qadi al-Baqillani: Standard-Bearer of Ahl al-Sunna
Biographical sketch of the prominent Ash'ari theologian al-Baqillani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pivotal role of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani within the Ash'ari school and why he is called the reviver of the fourth century.

Core Idea
al-Baqillani was the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna and the reviver of the fourth Islamic century.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most towering figures in Ash'ari theology: al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. Known as the 'sword of the Sunna,' he earned a reputation for sharp intellect, deep knowledge, and fierce defense of the Ash'ari creed. As you read his biography, you'll see why his name became synonymous with the title 'al-Qadi' in later Ash'ari works.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overall sense of al-Baqillani's life and achievements. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice the strong language used: 'standard-bearer', 'reviver', 'sword of the Sunna'.
2
Identify key titles and descriptions
List the specific titles and phrases used to describe al-Baqillani. What do they tell you about his status?
The most important is 'mujaddid al-mia al-rabi'a' (reviver of the fourth century).
3
Connect with the broader Ash'ari tradition
Think about why al-Baqillani is given the unqualified title 'al-Qadi' in Ash'ari works. How does this reflect his authority?
This shows he was the foremost theologian of his time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندما يُطلق القاضي في كتب أصول الدين عند السادة الأشاعرة فالمراد به الباقلاني، وهو القاضي أبو بكر محمد بن الطيب الباقلاني البصري الأشعري، تلميذ تلميذ الإمام الأشعري شيخ المذهب، وناصر طريقته، فهو من الطبقة الثانية من أصحاب الأشعري، وهو حامل لواء أهل السنة، مُجدد المئة الرابعة، يُضرب به المثل في سعة العلم وشدة الذكاء، من كبار المتكلمين وأجلهم قدراً، توفي ببغداد سنة (٤٠٣هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه. قال عنه ابن الأهدل: سيفُ السُّنة القاضي أبو بكر بن الباقلاني الأصولي الأشعري المالكي مجدد الدين على رأس المئة الرابعة على الصحيح. وقال عنه ابن خَلّكان: القاضي أبو بكر: محمد بن الطيب بن محمد بن جعفر بن القاسم، المعروف بالباقلاني البصري المتكلم المشهور كان على مذهب الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري، ومؤيداً اعتقاده، وناصراً طريقته، وصنف التصانيف الكثيرة المشهورة في علم الكلام وغيره، وكان أوحد زمانه وانتهت إليه الرئاسة في مذهبه، وكان موصوفاً بجودة الاستنباط، وسرعة الجواب، وسمع الحديث، وكان كثير التطويل في المناظرة، مشهوراً بذلك عند الجماعة. من شيوخه: ابن مجاهد الطائي، وأبو الحسن الباهلي تلميذا أبي الحسن الأشعري، والدارقطني، وأبو سهل الصعلوكي. من تلاميذه: أبو ذر الهروي المالكي الأشعري، وابن الأنباري، والقاضي عبد الوهاب البغدادي المالكي، وغيرهم كثير.
When al-Qadi is mentioned absolutely in books of principles of religion among the Ash'aris, what is meant is al-Baqillani. He is al-Qadi Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Tayyib al-Baqillani al-Basri al-Ash'ari, the student of the student of Imam al-Ash'ari, the master of the school, and the supporter of his way. He is from the second generation of al-Ash'ari's companions. He is the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna, the reviver of the fourth century. He is cited as an example in breadth of knowledge and sharp intelligence. He is among the greatest theologians and most eminent in rank. He died in Baghdad in the year 403 AH. May God have mercy on him and elevate his station. Ibn al-Ahdal said about him: 'The sword of the Sunna, al-Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Baqillani, the Ash'ari Maliki jurist, reviver of the religion at the head of the fourth century, correctly.' Ibn Khallikan said about him: 'Al-Qadi Abu Bakr: Muhammad ibn al-Tayyib ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn al-Qasim, known as al-Baqillani al-Basri, the famous theologian. He followed the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, supported his belief, and aided his way. He authored many famous books on theology and other fields. He was unique in his time and leadership in his school ended with him. He was described as having good deduction and quickness of answer. He heard hadith. He was lengthy in debate, famous for that among the people.' Among his teachers: Ibn Mujahid al-Ta'i, Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili, both students of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, al-Daraqutni, and Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki. Among his students: Abu Dharr al-Harawi al-Maliki al-Ash'ari, Ibn al-Anbari, and al-Qadi Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi al-Maliki, and many others.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH), a key figure in the Ash'ari school. It begins by noting that when the term 'al-Qadi' is used in books of usul al-din among the Ash'aris, it refers specifically to al-Baqillani. It gives his full name and describes him as a student of a student of al-Ash'ari, placing him in the second generation of the school. He is hailed as the standard-bearer of Ahl al-Sunna and the reviver (mujaddid) of the fourth Islamic century. The text praises his vast knowledge and intelligence. His death in Baghdad in 403 AH is mentioned. Then two quotations are provided: one from Ibn al-Ahdal calling him the 'sword of the Sunna' and affirming his role as reviver; another from Ibn Khallikan detailing his scholarly achievements, his adherence to the Ash'ari school, his prolific authorship, his quickness in debate, and his hadith studies. The passage lists his teachers (including students of al-Ash'ari like Ibn Mujahid and al-Bahili, and also al-Daraqutni) and his students (such as Abu Dharr al-Harawi, Ibn al-Anbari, and Abd al-Wahhab al-Baghdadi).

Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini: An Ash'ari Theologian and Jurist
Biography of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini and his contributions to Ash'ari theology and usul.

Core Idea
Al-Isfarayini was a brilliant scholar who combined theology, jurisprudence, and usul.

Before diving into the theological arguments of Jawharat al-Tawhid, it is helpful to know the scholars who shaped the Ash'ari tradition. This lesson introduces Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a major figure whose works and teaching influenced generations. The passage provides a concise biography highlighting his status and achievements.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of al-Isfarayini's life and titles.
Notice the honorific 'Rukn al-Din' (Pillar of the Faith).
2
Identify his scholarly profile
Note his fields: Shafi'i jurisprudence, theology (kalam), and usul. He was also praised for intelligence and depth.
He taught the 'two sciences' (usul al-din and usul al-fiqh) in Nishapur.
3
Understand the quote and its significance
The quote from Tarikh Naysabur states he reached the level of ijtihad. Reflect on why this is a high accolade in Islamic scholarship.

هو الإمام أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن مهران الإسفراييني، ولقبه ركن الدين، فقيه شافعي متكلم، أصولي بارع متبحر في العلوم، من أذكياء العالم، عامة شيوخ نيسابور علم الأصلين، توفي بنيسابور يوم عاشوراء، سنة (٤١٨ هـ)، ثم نُقل ودفن في إسفرايين. قال عنه أبو الحسن الفارسي في تاريخ نيسابور: أحد من بلغ حد الاجتهاد من العلماء؛ لتعمقه في العلوم، واستجماعه شرائط الإمامة. له مؤلفات وتصانيف عظيمة القدر، منها: جامع الحلى في أصول الدين والرد على الملحدين.
He is Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Mihran al-Isfarayini, his title is Rukn al-Din. He was a Shafi'i jurist, theologian, brilliant usuli, deeply learned in the sciences, among the intelligent of the world. He generally taught the scholars of Nishapur the two sciences (usul). His death occurred in Nishapur on the day of Ashura in 418 AH, after which his body was moved to Isfarayin for burial. The passage ends by listing one of his major works, 'Jami' al-Hila fi Usul al-Din wa al-Radd 'ala al-Mulhidin', a treatise on theology and refutation of atheists.

A biographical entry on the Ash'ari theologian al-Baqillani, including his teachers and students.

Al-Baqillani was the mujaddid of the fourth century and the leading Ash'ari theologian of his time.

Through the words of later scholars, we learn about his title as the 'sword of the Sunna', his role as a mujaddid, and his scholarly network. Ibn al-Ahdal said about him: 'The sword of the Sunna, the judge Abū Bakr ibn al-Bāqillānī, the uṣūlī, the Ashʿarī, the Mālikī, the renewer of religion at the head of the fourth century, according to the correct [view].' Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on the prominent Ashʿarī theologian Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī. It opens with a citation from Ibn al-Ahdal, who praises al-Bāqillānī as 'the sword of the Sunna' and identifies him as a judge, a uṣūlī (specialist in principles), an Ashʿarī, a Mālikī, and the renewer of religion (mujaddid) at the head of the fourth century. This is followed by a longer citation from Ibn Khallikān's biographical dictionary, which gives his full name and lineage, notes his adherence to al-Ashʿarī's school, his support of its beliefs, and his many famous works. It emphasizes his uniqueness and leadership in his school, his skill in deduction and quick response, his hearing of ḥadīth, and his reputation for lengthy debates. The passage then lists his teachers: Ibn Mujāhid al-Ṭā'ī, Abū al-Ḥasan al-Bāhilī (a direct student of al-Ashʿarī), the famous ḥadīth scholar al-Dāraquṭnī, and Abū Sahl al-Ṣaʿlūkī. His students include Abū Dharr al-Harawī, Ibn al-Anbārī, and Judge ʿAbd al-Wahhāb al-Baghdādī. Finally, there is a footnote (1) about another scholar, Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī, who is identified as a shaykh of al-Bāqillānī? Actually the footnote is numbered (1) and appears to correspond to a reference in the main text, but it provides a separate biography of al-Isfarāyīnī, likely because he is mentioned as a teacher elsewhere. The footnote describes al-Isfarāyīnī's full name, his title, his expertise in uṣūl, his death date, and a quote praising his ijtihād. It also mentions his work 'Jāmiʿ al-Ḥilā fī Uṣūl al-Dīn'. Overall, the passage serves to establish the scholarly credentials of al-Bāqillānī and his network.

Imam al-Mahalli: A Profile in Scholarship and Piety
Biography of Imam al-Mahalli covering his life, teachers, students, works, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, teachers, students, and major works of Imam Jalāl al-Dīn al-Maḥallī, a key Shafi'i-Ash'ari scholar.

Core Idea
Imam al-Mahalli's unfinished Tafsir al-Jalalayn remains a cornerstone of Qur'anic exegesis.

Imam Jalāl al-Dīn al-Maḥallī (791–864 AH) was a towering figure in the Islamic scholarly tradition, known for his sharp intellect and concise writings. This biography traces his lineage, education, and legacy, highlighting his contributions to jurisprudence, theology, logic, and exegesis. Understanding his life helps appreciate the scholarly milieu that produced works like Tafsīr al-Jalālayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's identity
Read the opening to know his full name, lineage, and scholarly attributions (Shafi'i, Ash'ari, etc.).
Notice the nickname 'al-Mahalli' comes from a place in Egypt.
2
Explore his teachers and students
List the notable teachers (e.g., Ibn Hajar) and students (e.g., al-Suyuti) to see the chain of transmission.
3
Reflect on his character and intellect
The passage quotes contemporaries praising his intelligence and his own claim of error-free understanding. Consider how this shaped his scholarly output.
He was known for his sharpness and truthfulness.
4
Review his scholarly output
Note his major works, especially the incomplete Tafsir al-Jalalayn. Observe the pattern of concise yet authoritative writing.
His commentary on al-Shamsiyyah in logic was left unfinished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) هو الإمام المحقق جلال الدين أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن محمد الأنصاري، المحلي الأصل، القاهري ، الشافعي الأشعري . كان الفقيه النفس ، منطقيا، متكلما ، أصوليا ، مفسرا. سبب تسميته بالمحلي: نسبةً إلى المحلة الكبرى مِن الغَربية من القاهرة . ولد في القاهرة سنة : (۷۹۱) (هـ) ونشأ في بيت علم وصلاح فوالده أبو العباس أحمد أخذ العلم عن الإمام البلقيني .
من شيوخه: الحافظ ولي الدين العراقي، وشمس الدين البرماوي، والحافظ ابن حجر، وانتفع كثيرا في العلوم العقلية في قراءته على العلامة علاء الدين البخاري ، وغيرهم الكثير . تلامذته الحافظ السخاوي، والحافظ السيوطي ، والحافظ ابن قطلوبغا الحنفي، وابن أبي شريف المقدسي ، والشريف السمهودي ، وخلق آخرون. أوصافه : كان علامة ، محققا نظارا ، مفرط الذكاء آية في الفهم، صحيح الذهن، حتى قال عنه بعض المعاصرين له: إن ذهنه يثقب الماس» وقال الإمام المحلي عن نفسه: «إن فهمي لا يقبل الخطأ وكان شديدا في الحق، وعدم المحاباة فيه، لا يخاف في الله لومة لائم ، وكان يتكسب بتجارة القمح ، عفيف النفس ، وقد وصفه ابن العماد: بتفتازاني العرب. مؤلفاته: ألف كتبا محررة ، في غاية الاختصار والتنقيح ، تشد إليها الرحال ، أقبل عليها الأئمة وتلقوها بالقبول ، ومنها: «البدر الطالع في حل جمع الجوامع وله: «الأنوار المضية في مدح خير البرية» وهو شرح للبردة ، وله : (كنز الراغبين شرح منهاج الطالبين» ومن مؤلفاته المنطقية: شرح الشمسية لكنه لم يكتمل، ومن مؤلفاته المشهورة تفسير القرآن المسمى بـ«تفسير الجلالين» بدأ من أول سورة الكهف إلى آخر القرآن ، ثم توفي فأتمه تلميذه الإمام السيوطي. وفاته: توفي في مستهل سنة : ( ٨٦٤) (هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه.
(2) He is the verifying imam Jalāl al-Dīn Abū ʿAbd Allāh Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad al-Anṣārī, of al-Maḥallah origin, al-Qāhirī, al-Shāfiʿī al-Ashʿarī. He was a profoundly learned jurist, logician, theologian, legal theorist, and exegete. The reason for his being named al-Maḥallī is his attribution to al-Maḥallah al-Kubrā in the Gharbiyyah district of Cairo. He was born in Cairo in the year 791 AH, and grew up in a house of knowledge and righteousness; his father Abū al-ʿAbbās Aḥmad acquired learning from Imam al-Bulqīnī.
Among his teachers: al-Ḥāfiẓ Walī al-Dīn al-ʿIrāqī, Shams al-Dīn al-Barmāwī, al-Ḥāfiẓ Ibn Ḥajar; he benefited greatly in the rational sciences from his study under the distinguished scholar ʿAlāʾ al-Dīn al-Bukhārī, and many others. His students: al-Ḥāfiẓ al-Sakhāwī, al-Ḥāfiẓ al-Suyūṭī, al-Ḥāfiẓ Ibn Qaṭlūbughā al-Ḥanafī, Ibn Abī Sharīf al-Maqdisī, al-Sharīf al-Samhūdī, and many others. His qualities: He was a scholar, a verifier, a contemplative, extremely intelligent, a sign of understanding, sound of mind, to the extent that some of his contemporaries said of him: 'His mind pierces diamonds.' Imam al-Maḥallī said of himself: 'My understanding does not accept error.' He was severe in the truth, showing no favoritism, and feared not the blame of any blamer for the sake of God. He earned his living through the wheat trade, and was chaste in himself. Ibn al-ʿImād described him as 'the Taftāzānī of the Arabs.' His works: He authored books that are refined, extremely concise and thoroughly revised, towards which journeys are undertaken; the imams turned to them and accepted them. Among them: 'al-Badr al-Ṭāliʿ fī Ḥall Jamʿ al-Jawāmiʿ'; 'al-Anwār al-Muḍiyyah fī Madḥ Khayr al-Bariyyah', which is a commentary on al-Burdah; 'Kanz al-Rāghibīn Sharḥ Minhāj al-Ṭālibīn'; among his logical works: a commentary on al-Shamsiyyah which he did not complete; among his famous works is the Qur'anic exegesis known as 'Tafsīr al-Jalālayn', which he began from the beginning of Sūrat al-Kahf to the end of the Qur'an, then he died and it was completed by his student Imam al-Suyūṭī. His death: He passed away at the beginning of the year 864 AH. May God Most High have mercy on him and elevate his station.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Imam Jalāl al-Dīn al-Maḥallī. It begins with his full name, lineage, and attributions. He was a Shafi'i-Ash'ari scholar of the highest caliber, a jurist, logician, theologian, legal theorist, and exegete. The reason for his name 'al-Maḥallī' is explained. Then details his birth in 791 AH, his father who was also a scholar, and his upbringing. The passage lists his notable teachers, including the hadith master Ibn Hajar, and his students, including al-Suyūṭī. It highlights his exceptional intelligence and quotes contemporary praise. His own statement about his infallible understanding is noted. The passage then enumerates his major works, emphasizing their conciseness and acceptance among scholars. Notably, his famous Tafsīr al-Jalālayn was left incomplete and finished by his student al-Suyūṭī. The passage concludes with his death date in 864 AH and a prayer for mercy.

Checkpoint
Why is the Tafsir al-Jalalayn attributed to both al-Mahalli and al-Suyuti?
A) They wrote it together from the beginning.
B) Al-Mahalli started it but died before completion, and al-Suyuti finished it.
C) Al-Suyuti wrote it and al-Mahalli reviewed it.
D) It is a compilation of both their independent works.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Mahalli was a brilliant and prolific scholar whose incomplete Tafsir al-Jalalayn, finished by al-Suyuti, exemplifies his concise and authoritative style.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Mahalli was described as 'severe in the truth, showing no favoritism, and feared not the blame of any blamer for the sake of God.' In what specific area of your life are you softening the truth to avoid conflict or please others? What one step will you take today to speak truth without compromise?
?
He said, 'My understanding does not accept error.' When was the last time you truly accepted that you were wrong in a matter of faith or practice? How does his confidence challenge your own humility and openness to correction?
?
Al-Mahalli earned his living through the wheat trade while being a renowned scholar. Do you view your daily work as separate from your pursuit of knowledge and piety? How can you make your profession a means of drawing closer to Allah, as he did?

Biography of Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi
Biography of the scholar al-Khattabi, his learning and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly stature, major works, and lineage of Imam Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi.

Core Idea
Al-Khattabi was a giant of Hadith and Fiqh, authoring foundational commentaries.

Every great tradition has its architects. In the sciences of Hadith, one such figure is Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi. This brief biography introduces his full name, his standing as an Imam and Hafiz, and the lasting works he left behind. As you read, note how his contributions laid the groundwork for later scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the author's own description come through.
Notice the honorifics used: 'Imam', 'Hafiz', 'Faqih'.
2
Identify key biographical elements
Look for the full name, scholarly titles, list of works, teachers, students, and birth/death years.
These elements are typical in classical biographical entries.
3
Reflect on the significance of 'Ma'alim al-Sunan'
Consider why being the first commentary on Sunan Abi Dawud after its abridgment is important. What does it say about al-Khattabi's role?
4
Connect to broader context
Think about how al-Khattabi's works, such as his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari, fit into the development of Hadith studies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو أبو سليمان حمد بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن خطاب البُسْتي الخطابي الشافعي ، الإمام ، كان أحد أوعية العلم في زمانه حافظا فقيها، مبرزا على أقرانه، صاحب التصانيف النافعة الجامعة، منها «معالم السنن» وهو أول شرح على سنن أبي داود بعد اختصاره، وله شرح على صحيح البخاري بعد أن اختصره اسمه (أعلام) الحديث» وله «غريب الحديث» و إصلاح غلط «المحدّثين» وغيرها. روى عن جماعة من الأكابر ، ، وروى عنه الحاكم وكان من أقرانه ، وأبو حامد الإسفراييني وطائفة سواهما ، ولد سنة بضع عشرة وثلاثمائة، وتوفي سنة : (۳۸۸) (هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه .
He is Abu Sulayman Hamd ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Khattab al-Busti al-Khattabi al-Shafi'i, the Imam, he was one of the vessels of knowledge in his time, a memorizer, a jurist, outstanding among his peers, author of beneficial comprehensive works, among them 'Ma'alim al-Sunan' which is the first commentary on Sunan Abi Dawud after its abridgment, and he has a commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari after he abridged it named 'A'lam al-Hadith', and he has 'Gharib al-Hadith' and 'Islah Ghalat al-Muhaddithin' and others. He narrated from a group of great scholars, and narrated from him al-Hakim who was among his peers, and Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini and a group besides them. He was born in the year [about 310s AH] and died in the year 388 AH. May Allah have mercy on him and elevate his station.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Sulayman al-Khattabi, a prominent Shafi'i scholar. It begins by stating his full name and lineage, then describes his scholarly stature: he was an 'Imam', a vessel of knowledge, a memorizer (hafiz), a jurist (faqih), and outstanding among his peers. It lists his most important works, among them 'Ma'alim al-Sunan' (the first commentary on Sunan Abi Dawud), a commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari titled 'A'lam al-Hadith', 'Gharib al-Hadith', and 'Islah Ghalat al-Muhaddithin'. The biography then mentions his teachers and students, noting that al-Hakim and Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini transmitted from him. It concludes with his birth year (early 310s AH) and death year (388 AH) and a prayer for mercy.

Key Terms

معالم السنن
غريب الحديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Khattabi was a prolific Shafi'i scholar whose commentaries on major Hadith collections are foundational.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Khattabi authored 'Ma'alim al-Sunan' as the first commentary on a major hadith collection, setting a foundation for generations. What contribution will you make to preserve or transmit sacred knowledge in your lifetime? Write one concrete step you will take this week.
?
He was described as 'a vessel of knowledge' and 'outstanding among his peers'. Are you actively striving to be a vessel of knowledge in your community, or are you content with being a passive recipient? What change in your daily routine would start today?
?
Al-Khattabi's works were 'beneficial comprehensive' because they served the ummah. When you learn a new hadith or lesson, do you ponder how to share it with others in a beneficial way? Identify one person you will teach something from this lesson before the week ends.
