Fakhr al-Din al-Razi: Life and Legacy
Biography of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi detailing his lineage, education, works, and legacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly lineage, major works, and legacy of the renowned Ash'ari theologian Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Core Idea
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi was the unparalleled master of both reason and tradition in his age.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi stands as one of the most influential figures in Islamic theology, whose works shaped later Ash'ari thought. This passage introduces his full identity, his scholarly chain connecting him to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, his major writings, and his role in defending Sunni orthodoxy. As you read, you will see how his comprehensive mastery earned him the unique title of 'al-Imam' among later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical details
Read the full name, birth year, lineage, and travels of al-Razi. Notice how the passage highlights his uniqueness in both rational and transmitted sciences.
2
Trace the scholarly chain
Follow the isnad from al-Razi through his father and teachers back to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. This chain establishes his authority in the two fundamental sciences.
3
Identify his contributions
Examine his major works and his role as a debater. Note how he brought many innovators back to the Sunni school and why the title 'al-Imam' refers specifically to him in later texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الإمام المتكلم الأصولي المفسر محمد بن عمر بن الحسن التيمي البكري الشافعي الأشعري ، المعروف بفخر الدين الرازي ، أبو عبد الله ، ولد سنة (٥٤٤هـ) أوحد زمانه في المعقول والمنقول وعلوم الأوائل، وهو قُرشي النَّسب ، يرجع نسبه إلى أبي بكر الصديق ه ، أصله من طبرستان ، ومولده في الرّي وإليها نسبته ، ويقال له: «ابن خطيب الرّي» رحل إلى خوارزم وما وراء النهر وخراسان . نسبه في علوم الأصلين اشتغل في الأصول على والده عمر ضياء الدين، وهو على أبي القاسم سلمان بن ناصر الأنصاري، وهو على إمام الحرمين، وهو على أبي إسحاق الإسفراييني، وهو على أبي الحسن الباهلي، وهو على شيخ المذهب وإمام المتكلمين أبي الحسن الأشعرى. من مؤلفاته المهمة: مفاتيح الغيب في التفسير، ونهاية العقول في دراية الأصول في علم الكلام، والمحصول في علم الأصول في أصول الفقه، وتأسيس التقديس في الرد على المجسمة والكرامية. وكان يحسن الفارسية ، وكان فارس علم الكلام، مناظرا لأهل البدعة من المجسمة والفلاسفة وغيرهم، وكانوا يخشون مناظرته ، ورجع بسببه خلق كثير من الكرامية وغيرهم من أهل البدعة إلى مذهب أهل السنة ، وإذا أطلق لقب «الإمام» عند المتأخرين في كتب العقيدة والكلام وأصول الفقه فهو المراد لا سواه، توفي في هراة، سنة (٦٠٦هـ) رحمه الله تعالى وأعلى مقامه في عليين.
He is the Imam, the theologian, the usuli, the exegete Muhammad ibn Umar ibn al-Hasan al-Taymi al-Bakri al-Shafi'i al-Ash'ari, known as Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, Abu Abdullah, born in 544 AH, the unique one of his time in rational and transmitted sciences and the sciences of the ancients. He is of Qurashi lineage, tracing back to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, his origin is from Tabaristan, and his birthplace is Rayy, to which he is attributed, and he is called 'Ibn Khatib al-Rayy'. He traveled to Khwarazm, Transoxiana, and Khorasan. His chain in the two fundamental sciences: he studied usul under his father Umar Diya al-Din, under Abu al-Qasim Salman ibn Nasir al-Ansari, under Imam al-Haramayn, under Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, under Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili, under the shaykh of the school and Imam of the mutakallimun Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Among his important works: 'Mafatih al-Ghayb' in tafsir, 'Nihayat al-Uqul fi Dirayat al-Usul' in kalam, 'al-Mahsul fi Ilm al-Usul' in usul al-fiqh, and 'Ta'sis al-Taqdis' in refutation of the mujassima and karamites. He was proficient in Persian, and was the knight of kalam, a debater against the people of innovation among the mujassima, philosophers, and others, and they feared his debating; many of the karamites and other innovators returned through him to the Sunni school. When the title 'al-Imam' is used among late scholars in books of creed, kalam, and usul al-fiqh, it refers to him alone. He died in Herat in 606 AH. May Allah have mercy on him and elevate his station in the highest heavens.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, the renowned Ash'ari theologian and exegete. It begins by listing his full name, titles, and attributes: Imam, mutakallim, usuli, mufassir. It gives his birth year (544 AH) and praises him as the unique scholar of his age in both rational and transmitted sciences. It then details his Qurashi lineage tracing back to Abu Bakr, his origin in Tabaristan, and his birthplace Rayy. The passage outlines his scholarly chain in the two fundamental sciences (usul al-din and usul al-fiqh), connecting him through his father and a line of teachers back to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It lists his major works, including his famous tafsir 'Mafatih al-Ghayb', and notes his role as a debater who brought many innovators back to Sunni Islam. Finally, it states that the title 'al-Imam' in later works refers specifically to him, and gives his death year (606 AH) with a prayer.

Key Terms
فخر الدين الرازي
مفاتيح الغيب
نهاية العقول
المحصول
تأسيس التقديس
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the title 'al-Imam' in later kalam and usul works refers to another scholar like al-Ghazali.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that when 'al-Imam' is used in these contexts, it refers exclusively to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the title 'al-Imam' signify when used in later works of creed, kalam, and usul al-fiqh?
A) It refers to Imam Abu Hanifa
B) It refers to Imam al-Shafi'i
C) It refers exclusively to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi
D) It is a general honorific for any great scholar

Key Takeaway
Fakhr al-Din al-Razi was the foremost Ash'ari theologian, whose works and debates solidified Sunni orthodoxy, earning him the exclusive title of 'al-Imam' among later scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi was a 'knight of kalam' who debated and brought countless people back to the truth. How many people have you guided—not just argued with—back to the path of Ahl al-Sunnah? What would it take for you to become a defender of truth like him, even if you are not a scholar?
?
Al-Razi's chain of teachers connects him through his father and a lineage of great scholars all the way to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Do you even know who taught your own teachers? How seriously do you take your own chain of Islamic knowledge, and what are you doing to strengthen it?
?
Al-Razi mastered both rational and transmitted sciences, and was proficient in Persian and Arabic. What have you sacrificed to gain deep, comprehensive knowledge of your religion? Are you satisfied with a shallow understanding, or are you willing to put in the effort to be an imam in your own right?

The Life and Authority of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni
Biographical account of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni with scholarly testimonies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly authority of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and why he is considered a pivotal figure in Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was the undisputed imam of his time, honored for his vast knowledge and teaching in the Two Sanctuaries.

This passage gives us a window into the life of one of the most influential scholars in Islamic theology. By learning his background, travels, and the accolades he received, we see why his works became foundational texts. The biography establishes not just his credentials but the intellectual environment that produced a major work like al-Jawhara.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation to understand the content.
Pay attention to the names and titles mentioned.
2
Identify key biographical milestones
List the most important facts: his lineage, birth, travels, the founding of the Nizamiyya school, and the reason for his title.
3
Examine the scholarly praise
The passage includes quotes from three prominent scholars. Why do these endorsements matter? They show his reputation.
Notice the superlative language used.
4
Reflect on the significance of his title
The title 'Imam al-Haramayn' indicates his direct connection to the sacred cities. Why was that so important for a scholar of kalam?
It shows his authority in both law and theology.

وهو الإمام الأصولي المتكلم عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن يوسف بن محمد الجويني، أبو المعالي ، ركن الدين، الملقب بإمام الحرمين ، أعلم المتأخرين ، من أكابر فقهاء الشافعية ، ولد سنة (٤١٩هـ) في جُوين من نواحي نيسابور ، ورحل إلى بغداد، فمكة ، ثم المدينة ، و لقب بإمام الحرمين؛ لأنه أفتى ودرس بمكة والمدينة، ثم عاد إلى نيسابور، فبنى له الوزير نظام الملك المدرسة النّظامية فيها ، وكان يحضر دروسه أكابر العلماء ، له مصنفات كثيرة نافعة ، قال عنه الإمام أبو إسحاق الشيرازي: تمتعوا بهذا الإمام ؛ فإنه نزهة هذا الزمان». وقال أيضاً يا مفيد أهل المشرق والمغرب ، لقد استفاد من علمك الأولون والآخرون». وقال عنه تاج الدين السبكي : هو الإمام ، شيخ الإسلام البحر الحبر المدقق المحقق ، النظار الأصولي المتكلم البليغ الفصيح الأديب ، العلم الفرد ، زينة المحققين، وإمام الأئمة على الإطلاق». وقال: «إذا قيل : قال الإمام ، أو اختاره الإمام ، أو نحو ذلك ، فلا إمام غيره، ولا تقال بهذا الإطلاق على أحدٍ سواه. وقال عنه ابن خَلَّكان: «أعلم المتأخرين من أصحاب الإمام الشافعي على الإطلاق المُجمع على إمامته ، المتفق على غزارة مادته، وتفننه في العلوم من الأصول والفروع ، والأدب، وغير ذلك». قال أبو عثمان الصابوني داعياً له: صرف الله المكاره عن هذا الإمام، فهو اليوم قرة عين الإسلام.
And he is the fundamentalist, the theologian, 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf ibn Muhammad al-Juwayni, Abu al-Ma'ali, Rukn al-Din, surnamed Imam al-Haramayn, the most learned of the later scholars, among the great jurists of the Shafi'ites. He was born in 419 AH in Juwayn, a region of Nishapur. He traveled to Baghdad, then to Mecca, then to Medina, and was titled Imam al-Haramayn because he gave legal opinions and taught in Mecca and Medina. Then he returned to Nishapur, where the vizier Nizam al-Mulk built for him the Nizamiyya school, and great scholars attended his lessons. He has many beneficial works. Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi said about him: 'Enjoy this Imam, for he is the delight of this age.' He also said: 'O benefactor of the people of the East and West, the earlier and later have benefited from your knowledge.' Taj al-Din al-Subki said: 'He is the Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, the sea, the scholar, the verifier, the investigator, the polemicist, the fundamentalist, the theologian, the eloquent, the eloquent, the literary, the unique scholar, the ornament of the verifiers, and the Imam of the Imams absolutely.' He said: 'When it is said: "The Imam said," or "the Imam chose," or the like, there is no Imam other than him, and it is not said with this absolute sense about anyone else.' Ibn Khallikan said: 'The most learned of the later scholars among the followers of Imam al-Shafi'i absolutely, whose Imamate is agreed upon, whose abundance of material and versatility in sciences from principles to branches, literature, and other things are unanimously acknowledged.' Abu Uthman al-Sabuni said in supplication for him: 'May Allah avert misfortunes from this Imam, for today he is the delight of Islam.'
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, a central figure in Ash'ari kalam and Shafi'i fiqh. It provides his full name, lineage, his birth in 419 AH in Juwayn, his travels to major centers of learning, and the reason for his famous title 'Imam al-Haramayn' (Imam of the Two Sanctuaries) due to his teaching in Mecca and Medina. It mentions the patronage of the vizier Nizam al-Mulk who built the Nizamiyya school for him. The passage then quotes several prominent scholars praising him: Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi calls him 'the delight of this age'; Taj al-Din al-Subki elevates him to the absolute Imamate, stating that the phrase 'the Imam' uniquely refers to him; Ibn Khallikan emphasizes his unmatched knowledge and versatility. These testimonies establish his authority and the respect he commanded.

Key Terms
إمام الحرمين
الجويني
نظام الملك
النظامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'Imam al-Haramayn' is an official title granted by a ruler.
Correction: Actually, it was an honorific given because he taught and gave legal rulings in Mecca and Medina, the two Harams.

Checkpoint
Why was al-Juwayni given the title 'Imam al-Haramayn'?
A) He was born in Mecca.
B) He taught and gave fatwas in Mecca and Medina.
C) He conquered the two cities.
D) He was the imam of all Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a towering scholar whose life and works continue to influence Islamic theology and law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about your own pursuit of knowledge. Al-Juwayni traveled to multiple cities and taught in the Two Sanctuaries solely for the sake of Allah. Does your daily routine reflect that same urgency for sacred knowledge, or are you satisfied with comfort and convenience? What one change can you make this week to prioritize learning Islam over distractions?
?
The scholars said of al-Juwayni that he was 'the delight of this age.' If the people who know you best were to describe your impact on Islam around you, would they say you are a delight—or a burden? What steps must you take today to become someone who brings joy and benefit to the Ummah?
?
Imam al-Haramayn's teachers and contemporaries praised him so highly that later scholars said 'the Imam' refers to none other than him. If you were to leave this world tonight, what would your teachers and friends honestly say about your contribution to Islam? Does that thought fill you with hope or with regret? Write down one thing you will start doing tomorrow to change that legacy.

Biography of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni
Biography of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly stature, and key contributions of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni as a leading Ash'ari theologian and Shafi'i jurist.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was the most learned scholar of his time, teacher of al-Ghazali.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most pivotal figures in Islamic theology and jurisprudence: Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni. His biography, as recorded by his student 'Abd al-Salam al-Laqqani, provides a window into the scholarly world of 5th-century Nishapur, Baghdad, and the Two Sanctuaries. You will read about his birth, his travels, his reception of praise from contemporaries, his mastery of earlier works, and his famous students.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Focus on the details of his life: birth, travels, title, and the school built for him. Let the narrative flow naturally.
2
Note the praises from scholars
Identify the four scholars quoted and what each said about al-Juwayni. Consider how these praises highlight his unique standing.
3
Examine his own teachers and students
He studied the works of al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani, and taught al-Ghazali among others. Reflect on the chain of knowledge transmission.
4
Reflect on his death and legacy
He died in 478 AH, leaving a profound impact on subsequent scholarship. Think about why his biography is still studied today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الإمام الأصولي المتكلم عبد الملك بن عبد الله بن يوسف بن محمد الجويني، أبو المعالي، ركن الدين، الملقب بإمام الحرمين، أعلم المتأخرين، من أكابر فقهاء الشافعية، ولد سنة (٤١٩هـ) في (جوين) من نواحي نيسابور، ورحل إلى بغداد، فمكة، ثم المدينة، ولقب بإمام الحرمين؛ لأنه أفتى ودرس بمكة والمدينة، ثم عاد إلى نيسابور، فبنى له الوزير نظام الملك المدرسة النظامية فيها، وكان يحضر دروسه أكابر العلماء، له مصنفات كثيرة نافعة، قال عنه الإمام أبو إسحاق الشيرازي: تمتعوا بهذا الإمام؛ فإنه نزهة هذا الزمان. وقال أيضا: يا مفيد أهل المشرق والمغرب، لقد استفاد من علمك الأولون والآخرون. وقال عنه تاج الدين السبكي: هو الإمام، شيخ الإسلام البحر الحبر المدقق المحقق، النظار الأصولي المتكلم البليغ الفصيح الأديب، العلم الفرد، زينة المحققين، وإمام الأئمة على الإطلاق. وقال: إذا قيل: قال الإمام، أو اختاره الإمام، أو نحو ذلك، فلا إمام غيره، ولا تقال بهذا الإطلاق على أحد سواه. وقال عنه ابن خلكان: أعلم المتأخرين من أصحاب الإمام الشافعي على الإطلاق المجمع على إمامته، المتفق على غزارة مادته، وتفننه في العلوم من الأصول والفروع، والأدب، وغير ذلك. قال أبو عثمان الصابوني داعيا له: صرف الله المكاره عن هذا الإمام، فهو اليوم قرة عين الإسلام. وإمام الحرمين هو ممن استوعب علوم أعلام كبار كالإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري، والقاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني، حتى قال الجويني عن نفسه: ما تكلمت في علم حفظت الكلام حتى من كلام القاضي أبي بكر اثني عشر ألف ورقة. من تلاميذه حجة الإسلام الغزالي، والإمام البارع الكيا الهراسي، والإمام الخوافي، وعبد الغافر الفارسي، والباخرزي، وغيرهم كثير، وكان إمام الحرمين خبيرا بتلاميذه يحسن رعايتهم ويشجعهم، ويسعد بنباهتهم، وقد وردت عنه كلمات في حقهم، حيث حكي أن الغزالي، والكيا الهراسي، والخوافي، تناظروا يوما في مجلسه أمامه، فقال موازنا بينهم: التحقيق للخوافي، والجزئيات للغزالي والبيان للكيا. وقال مرة: الغزالي بحر مغدق، والكيا أسد محدق، والخوافي نار تحرق. وفاته توفي سنة (٤٧٨هـ).
He is the fundamentalist theologian 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf ibn Muhammad al-Juwayni, Abu al-Ma'ali, Rukn al-Din, titled Imam al-Haramayn, the most learned of the later scholars, from the great jurists of the Shafi'is. He was born in the year 419 AH in Juwayn, a district of Nishapur. He traveled to Baghdad, then Mecca, then Medina, and was titled Imam al-Haramayn because he gave fatwas and taught in Mecca and Medina. Then he returned to Nishapur, and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk built for him the Nizamiyya school there, and the great scholars attended his lessons. He has many beneficial works. Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi said about him: 'Enjoy this imam, for he is the delight of this age.' He also said: 'O benefactor of the people of the East and the West, the earlier and later people have benefited from your knowledge.' Taj al-Din al-Subki said about him: 'He is the imam, the shaykh of Islam, the sea, the inkwell, the meticulous verifier, the speculative theologian, the eloquent, the articulate, the literary, the unique scholar, the adornment of the verifiers, and the imam of imams absolutely.' He said: 'When it is said: "the Imam said" or "the Imam chose" or the like, there is no imam other than him, and it is not said with this absolute sense of anyone else.' Ibn Khallikan said about him: 'The most learned of the later scholars from the school of Imam al-Shafi'i absolutely, upon whose imamate there is consensus, agreed upon his abundant material and his mastery in the sciences of principles and branches and literature and other things.' Abu 'Uthman al-Sabuni said, supplicating for him: 'May God avert troubles from this imam, for he is today the delight of Islam's eye.' And Imam al-Haramayn is among those who encompassed the sciences of great leading figures like Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, to the point that al-Juwayni said about himself: 'I did not speak about a science but that I memorized words, even from the words of al-Qadi Abu Bakr, twelve thousand folios.' Among his students are Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, and the eminent imam al-Kiya al-Harasi, and Imam al-Khafafi, and 'Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi, and al-Bakharzi, and many others. Imam al-Haramayn was knowledgeable about his students; he took good care of them, encouraged them, and was happy with their intelligence. Some words of his about them have been transmitted, such that it is related that al-Ghazali, al-Kiya al-Harasi, and al-Khafafi once debated in his presence in his gathering, and he said, balancing among them: 'Verification belongs to al-Khafafi, particulars to al-Ghazali, and exposition to al-Kiya.' And he said once: 'Al-Ghazali is a gushing sea, al-Kiya is a staring lion, and al-Khafafi is a burning fire.' His death: he died in the year 478 AH.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni (d. 478 AH), a leading Ash'ari theologian and Shafi'i jurist. It begins by stating his full name, titles, and his rank as the most learned of the later scholars. It notes his birth in 419 AH in Juwayn, a district of Nishapur, and his travels to Baghdad, Mecca, and Medina, where he was given the title 'Imam al-Haramayn' (Imam of the Two Sanctuaries) because he taught and issued fatwas there. Upon returning to Nishapur, the vizier Nizam al-Mulk built the Nizamiyya school for him, where great scholars attended his lessons. The passage then quotes several prominent scholars praising him: Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi calls him the 'delight of this age'; Taj al-Din al-Subki elevates him as the absolute imam; Ibn Khallikan affirms his unmatched knowledge. Abu 'Uthman al-Sabuni prays for him. The biography also mentions his mastery of the works of earlier leading figures like al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani, and his own claim to have memorized 12,000 folios of al-Baqillani's words. It lists his famous students: al-Ghazali, al-Kiya al-Harasi, al-Khafafi, and others. Al-Juwayni was attentive to his students, as shown by his characterizations of them: al-Khafafi for verification, al-Ghazali for particulars, and al-Kiya for exposition, and his vivid metaphors describing each. The passage concludes with his death in 478 AH.

Key Terms
إمام الحرمين (Imam al-Haramayn)
أبو المعالي الجويني (Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni)
المدرسة النظامية (Nizamiyya school)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Juwayni's title 'Imam al-Haramayn' refers to his high rank in general.
Correction: It specifically indicates his teaching activities in Mecca and Medina, as the passage states: 'because he gave fatwas and taught in Mecca and Medina.'

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a towering figure in Ash'ari theology and Shafi'i jurisprudence, whose life exemplified the transmission of knowledge from earlier authorities to later generations through his teaching and writings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Juwayni memorized 12,000 folios of al-Baqillani's words. How does your own diligence in seeking sacred knowledge measure up? What is one specific step you will take this week to deepen your study of a single Islamic text?
?
Many great scholars praised al-Juwayni while he was alive. If those who know you were to describe your character and knowledge, what would they say? Does that align with the person you want to be before Allah?
?
Al-Juwayni nurtured his students and recognized their unique strengths. Whom are you currently helping to grow in knowledge or character? If no one, what is holding you back from being a source of encouragement for others?

The Legacy of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni
Biographical notice with teachers, students, and anecdotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly stature of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, his teachers, and his famous students as portrayed in this biographical passage.

Core Idea
Al-Juwayni's legacy is defined by his mastery of earlier scholars and his mentoring of future giants.

This passage introduces us to Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, a towering figure in Ash'ari theology. It shows how he absorbed the works of earlier luminaries and then nurtured a generation of brilliant students, each with unique strengths. As you read, notice how al-Juwayni’s own words reveal his deep engagement with scholarship and his perceptive eye for talent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage silently, then the literal translation. Let the biographical details settle before analyzing them.
Pay attention to the numbers and metaphors – they are vivid.
2
Identify the key figures
List the teachers and students mentioned. Notice how al-Juwayni relates to each: his debt to al-Baqillani, his praise for al-Ghazali, al-Kiya, and al-Khawafi.
3
Reflect on al-Juwayni's character
From the anecdote and metaphors, what kind of teacher was al-Juwayni? How did he assess his students? This reveals his pedagogical insight.
He balances different strengths – tahqiq, juz'iyyat, bayan.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإمام الحرمين هو ممن استوعب علوم أعلام كبار كالإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري، والقاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني، حتى قال الجويني عن نفسه: «ما تكلّمتُ في علم حفظت الكلام حتى من كلام القاضي أبي بكر اثني عشر ألف ورقة». من تلاميذه حجة الإسلام الغزالي، والإمام البارع الكيا الهراسي، والإمام الخوافي، وعبد الغافر الفارسي، والباخرزي، وغيرهم كثير، وكان إمام الحرمين خبيراً بتلاميذه يحسن رعايتهم ويشجعهم، ويسعد بنباهتهم، وقد وردت عنه كلمات في حقهم، حيث حُكيَ أَنَّ الغزالي، والكيا الهراسي، والخوافي، تناظروا يوماً في مجلسه أمامه، فقال موازناً بينهم: التحقيق للخوافي، والجزئيات للغزالي والبيان للكيا وقال مرة: «الغزالي بحر مغدق، والكيا أسد محدق، والخوافي نار تحرق». وفاته توفي سنة (٤٧٨هـ).
And Imam al-Haramayn [al-Juwayni] is among those who comprehensively grasped the sciences of great luminaries such as Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, to the extent that al-Juwayni said about himself: 'I have not spoken in any science but that I have preserved the speech [of others], even from the speech of Qadi Abu Bakr twelve thousand folios.' Among his students are Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali, the eminent Imam al-Kiya al-Harrasi, Imam al-Khawafi, Abd al-Ghafir al-Farisi, al-Bakharzi, and many others. And Imam al-Haramayn was knowledgeable about his students, he treated them well, encouraged them, and rejoiced at their acumen. Reported statements from him about them include that one day al-Ghazali, al-Kiya al-Harrasi, and al-Khawafi debated in his presence, and he said, balancing among them: 'Investigation (tahqiq) belongs to al-Khawafi, details (juz'iyyat) belong to al-Ghazali, and exposition (bayan) belongs to al-Kiya.' And he said once: 'Al-Ghazali is a surging sea, al-Kiya is a scrutinizing lion, and al-Khawafi is a burning fire.' He died in the year 478 AH.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Imam al-Haramayn Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni (d. 478 AH), a leading Ash'ari theologian. It first highlights his comprehensive mastery of the teachings of major figures like al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani, quoting his own claim that he had preserved from al-Baqillani's works alone twelve thousand folios. The passage then lists his prominent students, including al-Ghazali, al-Kiya al-Harrasi, and al-Khawafi, among others. It also relates anecdotes about his interaction with his students, including his assessment of their strengths: al-Khawafi was strong in investigation, al-Ghazali in details, and al-Kiya in exposition. He also described them with vivid metaphors: al-Ghazali as a surging sea, al-Kiya as a scrutinizing lion, and al-Khawafi as a burning fire. The passage concludes with his death date in 478 AH.

Key Terms
إمام الحرمين (Imam al-Haramayn)
الجويني (al-Juwayni)
الغزالي (al-Ghazali)
الكيا الهراسي (al-Kiya al-Harrasi)
الخوافي (al-Khawafi)
أعلام (luminaries)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a master scholar who preserved vast knowledge from earlier giants and nurtured exceptional students, each with distinct intellectual gifts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
His students became towering figures. Whom are you investing in right now to carry forward what you have learned? If your answer is 'no one', what is stopping you from finding that person starting today?

The Life and Works of Ibn al-Arabi al-Maliki
A biography of Imam Abu Bakr Ibn al-Arabi al-Maliki al-Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be familiar with the biography of Imam Abu Bakr Ibn al-Arabi al-Maliki, including his teachers, major works, and his role as a leading scholar of al-Andalus.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Arabi combined Maliki fiqh and Ash'ari theology, studying under al-Ghazali and leaving enduring works.

This brief biography introduces us to Imam Abu Bakr Ibn al-Arabi, a towering figure from Islamic Spain. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the authority behind the theological positions he champions. As we read his tarjama, notice the key elements that establish his scholarly credentials: his lineage, his travels, his teachers, and his written legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: it begins with his full name and titles, then mentions his origin and stature, followed by his education, works, and dates.
2
Identify his academic lineage
Find the name of his famous teacher and note the schools he belonged to (Maliki and Ash'ari). This shows the transmission of knowledge from al-Ghazali to the Maghrib.
3
List his major works
Go through the listed books. Which subjects do they cover? (Qur'an, Hadith, creed, spirituality). This demonstrates his breadth.
4
Reflect on his historical context
Consider the significance of an Andalusian scholar traveling east and returning with knowledge. How does this biography underscore the interconnectedness of the Islamic world?

Abu Nasr al-Ash'ari was a Chief Judge and prolific author.

This biographical passage introduces the scholar Abu Nasr al-Ash'ari, a prominent Shafi'i jurist and historian. الأشعري، أبو نصر، قاضي القضاة، الأصولي، المؤرخ، الفقيه. ولد في القاهرة سنة (727هـ)، وانتقل إلى دمشق مع والده فسكنها وتوفي بها. نسبته إلى سبك (من أعمال المنوفية بمصر)، وكان طلق اللسان، قوي الحجة، انتهى إليه القضاء في الشام، وتوفي بها بالطاعون سنة (771هـ) رحمه الله وأعلى مقامه. من كتبه: طبقات الشافعية الكبرى، وجمع الجوامع، والأشباه والنظائر، وغيرها من الكتب المتقنة المحررة.
Al-Ash'ari, Abu Nasr, the Chief Judge, the usuli [أصولي], the historian, the jurist. He was born in Cairo in the year 727 AH, and moved to Damascus with his father, resided there, and died there. His lineage traces to Sabk (in the Menoufia governorate of Egypt). He was eloquent, strong in argument; the judiciary in Syria ended with him, and he died there of plague in the year 771 AH. May God have mercy on him and elevate his rank. Among his books are: 'The Great Layers of the Shafi'is' [طبقات الشافعية الكبرى], 'The Compilation of the Compendia' [جمع الجوامع], 'Similarities and Parallels' [الأشباه والنظائر], and other precise and refined books.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Abu Nasr al-Ash'ari. It gives his full name and titles (Chief Judge, usuli, historian, jurist). It notes he was born in Cairo in 727 AH, moved to Damascus with his father, and died there in 771 AH from plague. He was known for eloquence and strong argument. His major works include a biographical dictionary of Shafi'i scholars, a comprehensive compendium of legal maxims, and a work on similar cases in law.

The Best of the Companions: The Four Caliphs in Order
Proof that the four caliphs are best in order of succession using hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitive evidence that the four rightly-guided caliphs are the best of the companions in the order of their succession, based on the hadith of the thirty-year caliphate and the consensus of the majority.

Core Idea
The four caliphs are best in order of succession, proven by the thirty-year caliphate hadith and consensus.

In this passage, the author establishes a foundational belief in Sunni Islam: the superiority of the four caliphs in the order they ruled. He does not rely on mere opinion but anchors his argument in an explicit hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the position of the majority of scholars. Prepare to see how a single prophetic statement becomes a definitive proof for a key article of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the opening statement that the best of the companions are the four caliphs in order of the caliphate.
This is the thesis the author will prove.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The author cites the Prophet's hadith: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years.' Reflect on how this hadith directly supports the superiority of the four caliphs, as their combined rule exactly covers that period.
The hadith is presented as explicit (ṣarīḥ) proof.
3
Understand the definitive nature
The passage concludes that this preference is definitive (qaṭʿī) in both outward and inward, contrary to a minority view. Appreciate why the author emphasizes certainty.
This is not a matter of opinion but a firmly held belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ أنَّ أفضل الصحابةِ الخُلَفاء الأربعةُ على ترتيب الخِلَافة
٧٦ - وخيرهم من وُليَ الخِلافَة
وأشار إلى حكم واجب الاعتقاد أيضاً بقوله: (وخَيْرُهُمْ)، أي: أفضلُ أصحابها على الإطلاق: (مَنْ وُلّي، أي: النَّفْرُ الذين وُلُّوا (الخِلَافَة) العظمى ؛ وهي: النيابة عنه الله في عموم مصالح المسلمين ، من إقامة الدين وصيانة المسلمين، المقدرة مُدَّتها بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنةً - ثمَّ تصير مُلكًا عَضُوضا((١)) وهذا صريح في أنَّ الأئمة الأربعة أفضلُ الصَّحابةِ ؛ لأنَّ هذه المُدَّة كانتْ دَور ولايتهم ، وإلى هذا التفضيل ذهبَ الجمهور ، خلافا لما نقله المازري عن طائفة من عدم المُفاضلة بينهم، وهو قطعي ـ كما قال به إمامنا الأشعري ، رضي الله تعالى عنه ـ في الظاهر والباطن .
Explanation that the best of the companions are the four caliphs in the order of the caliphate. 76 - And the best of them are those who undertook the caliphate. And he also pointed to a ruling that must be believed with his saying: 'And the best of them,' i.e., the best of the companions absolutely: 'those who undertook,' i.e., the persons who assumed the great caliphate; it is the deputyship from God in the general interests of the Muslims, of establishing the religion and protecting the Muslims, its term being determined by his saying, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years - then it becomes a biting kingship.' And this is explicit that the four imams are the best of the companions; because this period was the era of their governance. And the majority went to this preference, contrary to what al-Māzarī transmitted from a group that there is no differentiation among them. And it is definitive (qaṭʿī) — as stated by our Imam al-Ashʿarī, may God be pleased with him — in the outward and inward.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a proof and declaration that the best of the Prophet's companions are the four rightly-guided caliphs in the order of their succession. The author begins by stating the thesis: 'The best of the companions are the four caliphs in the order of the caliphate.' He then cites the poetic verse (number 76) from the matn: 'And the best of them are those who undertook the caliphate.' The commentary explains that 'the best of them' means the best of the companions absolutely, and 'those who undertook' refers to the specific persons who assumed the great caliphate, which is defined as deputyship from God for the general interests of Muslims. The duration of their caliphate is indicated by the hadith: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years - then it becomes a biting kingship.' This hadith is taken as explicit proof that the four imams (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) are the best of the companions because the thirty-year period exactly covers their rule. The author then notes that this view of preferring the caliphs in order is the position of the majority of scholars, contrary to a group reported by al-Mazari who denied any differentiation. He emphasizes that this preference is definitive (qaṭʿī) in both outward and inward judgment, as affirmed by Imam al-Ash'ari.

Key Terms
الخلفاء الأربعة
الخلافة العظمى
أفضل الصحابة
قطعي
الجمهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the preference of the four caliphs is only a probable opinion (ẓannī).
Correction: The author states it is definitive (qaṭʿī) based on explicit hadith and the consensus of the majority.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Definition and Story of Bay'at al-Ridwan
Sanusi defines Bay'at al-Ridwan and narrates its story.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what Bay'at al-Ridwan is, its rank among Islamic pledges, the reason for its name, the number of participants, the story behind it, and the exception of the hypocrite Ibn Qays.

Core Idea
The Pledge of Pleasure under the tree earned divine approval and included nearly all companions except one.

Bay'at al-Ridwan is a significant event where the Prophet ﷺ gathered companions to pledge allegiance under a tree, prompted by a false rumor. This lesson explores its meaning, participants, and the lessons from this episode.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the author's style and key terms.
The first word 'قَبَيْعَةُ' is ambiguous; it likely means 'بيعة' (pledge).
2
Identify the rank and naming
Note that the rank of this pledge follows that of Uhud, and its name comes from the Qur'anic verse in Surat al-Fath.
The verse is a direct divine endorsement.
3
Understand the narrative
Follow the story: the Prophet's intention, the blockade, sending 'Uthman, the false rumor, and the call to pledge.
The pledge was for loyalty unto death or not fleeing.
4
Analyze the exception
Notice who stayed behind and why. Consider the description of Ibn Qays and his repentance.
This shows that even among the best, there can be hypocrisy.
5
Reflect on the outcome
Consider the peaceful resolution after 'Uthman's safety was known.
The Prophet's wisdom in making peace.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قَبَيْعَةُ)، أي: فرتبة أهل بيعة (الرّضْوَانِ) تلي رُتبةَ أَهلِ أُحُدٍ ، وقيل لها بيعة الرضوان (۱) ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَن الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ﴾ [الفتح: ۱۸] . وكانوا ألفًا وأربعمئة وقيل : وخمسمئة ؛ خرج بهم النبي لزيارة البيت ; فصده المشركونَ ; فأرسل إليهم عثمانَ للصلح، فشاعَ أَنَّهم قتلوه ; فقال عند ذلك: «لا نَبْرَحُ حَتَّى تُناجِزَهم الحربَ ودعا الناس عند الشَّجرة للبيعة على الموت، أو على أنْ لا يَفِرُّوا ، فبايعوه على ذلك ، ولم يتخلف عنها إلا بن قيس وكان مُنافقًا ، اختبأ تحت بطن ناقته، وهو ابن عم البراء بن معرور ، وكان من المؤلَّفَةِ قلوبهم أيضاً، ويقال: إنَّه تاب وحَسُن إسلامه، ثمَّ تبيَّنت حياة عثمان ، فصالحهم النَّبِيُّ الله على شرط ورجع إلى المدينة.
(Qubay'ah): meaning the rank of the people of the Bay'ah of al-Ridwan follows the rank of the people of Uhud, and it was called Bay'at al-Ridwan because of His statement, the Most High: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers' [al-Fath: 18]. And they were one thousand four hundred, and it was said: one thousand five hundred; the Prophet went out with them to visit the House, but the polytheists prevented him; so he sent 'Uthman to them for a truce, and it became rumored that they had killed him; so he said at that: 'We shall not cease until we engage them in war,' and called the people at the tree to pledge allegiance upon death, or upon not fleeing; so they pledged allegiance to him upon that, and none stayed behind except Ibn Qays, and he was a hypocrite; he hid under the belly of his she-camel, and he was the cousin of al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur, and he was also among those whose hearts are reconciled; and it is said that he repented and his Islam became good. Then the life of 'Uthman became apparent, so the Prophet made peace with them on a condition and returned to Medina.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage defines and narrates the history of Bay'at al-Ridwan. It begins by stating that the rank of the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan comes after the rank of the people of Uhud. The name 'Bay'at al-Ridwan' is derived from the Qur'anic verse 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers' (al-Fath: 18). The author then provides the number of participants: one thousand four hundred (or some say one thousand five hundred). The story is then recounted: the Prophet led them to visit the Ka'ba, but were blocked by the polytheists of Mecca. The Prophet sent 'Uthman as an envoy to negotiate peace. When news spread that 'Uthman had been killed, the Prophet called the people to pledge allegiance under a tree, vowing to fight to the death or to not flee. Everyone pledged except a hypocrite named Ibn Qays (identified as the cousin of al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur) who hid. It is said that he later repented. Eventually, it became known that 'Uthman was alive, so the Prophet made a peaceful treaty and returned to Medina.

Key Terms
بيعة الرضوان
الرضوان
أهل بيعة الرضوان
عثمان
الشجرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Bay'at al-Ridwan was about a different pledge or that all companions participated without exception.
Correction: The pledge was specifically under a tree at Hudaybiyyah, and it was prompted by a false rumor of 'Uthman's death. One companion, Ibn Qays, was a hypocrite who hid and did not participate.

Checkpoint
Why is Bay'at al-Ridwan called 'al-Ridwan' (pleasure)?
A) Because the Prophet was pleased with them.
B) Because Allah expressed His pleasure with the believers in Surat al-Fath.
C) Because they were all righteous.
D) Because they made peace with the polytheists.

Key Takeaway
Bay'at al-Ridwan is a testament to the companions' loyalty and the Prophet's leadership, while also showing that hypocrisy can appear even in great moments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had been among the companions at that moment, with the rumor of 'Uthman's death spreading, would you have hesitated to pledge your life? What is the one thing in your life right now that makes you hide your loyalty to Allah and His messenger like Ibn Qays hid under his camel?
?
The companions pledged not to flee from battle. In your own struggles against your desires and sins, do you flee when the battle gets tough? What would it take for you to make a firm covenant with Allah today to stand firm, regardless of the cost?
?
Allah declared His pleasure with those believers. Are you living in a way that seeks His pleasure above all else? If you were to die tonight, do you have the certainty that you are among those with whom Allah is pleased? What is the one change you can make starting now to earn that pleasure?

The Sabiqun: Definition, Quranic Excellence, and Dispute over Identity
Definition, Quranic proof of excellence, and dispute over identity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who the Sabiqun are, how their excellence is proven from the Quran, and the scholarly disagreement over their specific identification.

Core Idea
The Sabiqun are distinguished by Quranic text, but who exactly they are is debated.

This passage defines the Sabiqun (the foregoers) as those who prayed toward both qiblas, establishes their excellence from explicit Quranic verses, and then reveals a scholarly disagreement about exactly who they are. The author also clarifies that preference is for groups, not individuals, and gives examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: definition, proof, dispute.
The passage is a commentary on a verse line.
2
Identify the definition of Sabiqun
Note that the Sabiqun are defined as those who prayed toward both qiblas. Who is cited for this definition?
Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and others.
3
Understand the Quranic proof of excellence
The passage says their excellence is known from nass (Quranic text) and cites two verses. Identify the verses and what they imply.
Verses from al-Tawba and al-Hadid.
4
Grasp the dispute and the principle of group preference
Two opinions are given about the identity of the Sabiqun. Then the author states a key principle: preference is for the group over the group, not individuals over individuals. Understand this distinction.
Example: Uthman is a Badri in reward, not attendance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والسَّابِقُونَ الأَوَّلُونَ الذينَ صَلَّوْا إلى القبلتين كما قاله أبو موسى الأشعري وغيره من الأكابر (فَضْلُهُمْ)، أي: أرجحيتُهم في كثرة الثَّواب على غيرهم ممن لم يُشاركهم فيما ذكر ، (نَصَّا عُرِف)، أي: عُرف مِن نص القرآن ، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالسَّبِقُونَ الْأَوَّلُونَ مِنَ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ وَالْأَنْصَارِ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٠] الآية . لَا يَسْتَوِى مِنكُر مَنْ أَنفَقَ مِن قَبْلِ الْفَتْحِ وَقَتَلَ [الحديد: ١٠]. (قَدِ (هَذَا، وَفِي نَعْيِينِهِم) يعني: الوصف المقتضي له المنطبق عليهم اختُلِفْ)، أي: اختلف العلماء فيه، فقال الشَّعَبي: هم أهل بيعة الرضوان، وقال محمد بن كعب القرظي وجماعة: هم أهل بدر، والمُفضَّل في جميع هذه المراتب الجملة عن الجملة ، لا الأفراد على الأفراد، وبعض أهل هذه المراتب ربَّما دخل في بعضها ، وربَّما دخل في الجميع؛ فقد يكون سابقا خليفة بدريًّا أُحُديًّا رِضوانيًّا، كالمشايخ الأربعة: فإنَّ عثمان الله تعالى عنه بدري أجرًا لا حُضورًا ، فمزيَّة البدري من حيث هو
(And the first foregoers are those who prayed toward the two qiblas, as stated by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and other great scholars. (Their excellence): meaning their preponderance in abundance of reward over others who did not share with them in what was mentioned. (It is known from nass): meaning it is known from the text of the Quran, like His statement, the Most High: 'And the first foregoers among the emigrants and the helpers' [al-Tawba: 100] — the verse. 'Not equal among you [؟] are those who spent before the conquest and fought [؟]' [al-Hadid: 10]. (This being established, and concerning their identification) meaning the description that necessitates it applying to them, (there is disagreement): meaning the scholars differed about it. So al-Sha'bi said: they are the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan, and Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi and a group said: they are the people of Badr. And preference in all these ranks is of group over group, not individuals over individuals. And some people of these ranks may enter into some of them, and may enter into all of them; for one may be a foregoer, a caliph, a Badri, an Uhudi, a Ridwani, like the four shaykhs: for 'Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, is a Badri in reward but not in attendance; so the merit of the Badri as such...
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line: 'والسابقون فضلهم نصا عرف هذا وفي تعيينهم قد اختلاف'. It begins by defining the Sabiqun (the foregoers) as those who prayed toward both qiblas (first toward Jerusalem, then toward Makkah), citing Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and others. Their excellence (فضل) is explained as 'preponderance in reward' over others who did not share in that characteristic. This excellence is known from nass (explicit text of the Quran), specifically two verses: 'And the first foregoers among the emigrants and the helpers' (al-Tawba: 100) and 'Not equal among you are those who spent before the conquest and fought [؟]' (al-Hadid: 10). Then the passage addresses the dispute (اختلاف) about the precise identification (تعيين) of the Sabiqun. Al-Sha'bi identifies them as the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan, while Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi and others identify them as the people of Badr. The author then clarifies a key principle: preference is for the group as a whole over another group, not individuals over individuals. An individual may belong to multiple categories (e.g., a person could be at once a Sabiq, a caliph, a participant at Badr, Uhud, and Bay'at al-Ridwan). The example of the four 'shaykhs' (Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali) is given: 'Uthman is a Badri in reward but not in physical attendance because he was absent due to staying with his sick wife Ruqayyah. The passage ends by noting the merit of a Badri as such.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sabiqun are only those who prayed toward both qiblas.
Correction: Their definition includes that characteristic, but the exact identity is disputed; the author presents two opinions (Bay'at al-Ridwan or Badr).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Sabiqun's excellence is proven by Quranic text, but their precise identity is subject to scholarly difference, with preference given to groups over individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals that even the first generation, the best of creation, had ranks known by Allah but disputed among scholars. When you see disagreements among Muslims today about who is 'best' or 'most righteous', does this lesson humble your certainty? How often do you label others' groups without acknowledging that final ranking belongs to Allah alone? Will you now commit to suspending judgment about entire groups, knowing that even the Sahaba's ranks are debated?
?
The principle of group-over-group preference prevents comparing individuals as if their personal merit is absolute. Think of a time you compared yourself to another Muslim, feeling superior because of your actions or affiliations. What does this principle say about that comparison? How can you replace that attitude with recognizing that Allah prefers groups, and you may not even be part of the best group?
?
The Sabiqun's excellence is known only through nass. Do you ever feel pressured to prove your 'sabiqiyyah'—your early, consistent submission—through visible achievements? Yet the Quran only declares their excellence; it does not list all their details. How can you find comfort in knowing that your own early, private sacrifices are known to Allah, even if others dispute your rank? Will you stop seeking human validation and trust that Allah's text suffices to honor the sincere?

Biography of Ibn al-Imad
A biographical notice on the Shafi'i jurist Ibn al-Imad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, teachers, students, and works of the Shafi'i jurist Ibn al-Imad.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Imad was a prolific Shafi'i scholar who studied under greats and taught Ibn Hajar.

This passage introduces us to a key figure in the Shafi'i tradition: Ibn al-Imad. Knowing the biographies of scholars helps us appreciate the chains of knowledge transmission. Let's explore his life, his teachers, his students, and his contributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: birth, teachers, students, works, death.
The Arabic uses a concise style typical of biographical entries.
2
Identify the key relationships
List the teachers and students mentioned. How do these names connect to other scholars you may know?
Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani is a famous hadith scholar.
3
Appreciate his scholarly output
Review the list of his works. Note the variety of topics: fiqh, poetry, and critical works.
His works show his breadth of knowledge.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابن العماد أحد أئمة الفقهاء الشافعية، وصاحب التصانيف الكثيرة النافعة. كانت ولادته قبل الخمسين وسبعمئة من شيوخه: جمال الدين الإسنوي، سراج الدين البلقيني، وأبو الفضل العراقي، وغيرهم. من تلامذته الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني، والفقيه عبد العزيز بن عنبر البوتيجي، وسبط ابن العجمي. من مؤلفاته: «تسهيل المقاصد لزوار المساجد» وله أرجوزة في طبقات الأنبياء و«القول التام في أحكام المأموم والإمام» و«البيان التقريري في تخطئة الكمال الدميري» وله: التعقيبات على المهمات لشيخه الإسنوي، وغيرها من المؤلفات الكثيرة النافعة في مختلف العلوم. توفي سنة ۸۰۸ هـ رحمه الله ورفع مقامه في عليين.
Ibn al-Imad, one of the imams of the Shafi'i jurists, and author of many beneficial works. His birth was before 750 AH. Among his teachers: Jamal al-Din al-Isnavi, Siraj al-Din al-Bulqini, and Abu al-Fadl al-Iraqi, and others. Among his students: al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, and the jurist Abd al-Aziz ibn Anbar al-Butiji, and Sibt ibn al-Ajami. He died in the year 808 AH. May Allah have mercy on him and raise his station in the highest heavens.

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Ibn al-Imad, a prominent Shafi'i scholar. It first notes his status as one of the leading Shafi'i jurists and a prolific author. His birth is given as before 750 AH. The text then lists his teachers: Jamal al-Din al-Isnavi, Siraj al-Din al-Bulqini, Abu al-Fadl al-Iraqi, and others. His students include the famous hadith scholar Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, the jurist Abd al-Aziz al-Butiji, and Sibt ibn al-Ajami. Several of his works are mentioned, including a manual for mosque visitors, a poem on the ranks of the prophets, a treatise on rulings for followers and imams, a work correcting al-Damiri, and glosses on his teacher al-Isnavi's works. The biography concludes with his death year 808 AH and a prayer for mercy.

Excellence of the Four Imams and Their Equals
The author explains the excellence of the four imams and others in preserving religious rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the excellence of the four imams and how the definite article 'al' in 'al-a'imma' signifies completeness, including other imams of their rank.

Core Idea
The four imams and their equals are the guides of the community, with 'al' indicating completeness.

In this lesson, we examine a passage that highlights the superiority of the four great imams—Malik, Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal—and how the definite article 'al' in 'al-a'imma' is interpreted to include all imams of that caliber. The author clarifies that these imams are the guides of the Ummah in preserving the rulings of religion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the basic meaning.
Notice the verse naming Malik and 'the rest of the imams' and the commentary explaining them.
2
Identify the imams mentioned
The passage explicitly names Malik ibn Anas and lists Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal as examples of 'the rest.'
These four are the well-known founders of the Sunni schools of jurisprudence.
3
Understand the significance of 'al' for completeness
The author explains that the definite article in 'al-a'imma' is best understood as indicating completeness, so that it includes all imams of that rank, not just the four.
This prevents the misconception that only the four are included.
4
Reflect on the role of the imams
The passage calls them 'guides of the community' (hudat al-ummah), emphasizing their role in preserving religious rulings.
Consider why these imams are held in such high esteem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ أفضليّة الأئمة الأربعة ومَن في درجتهم في حفظ أحكام الدين
ومالك وسائر الأئِمَّة كَذَا أَبُو الْقَاسِمْ هُداةُ الأُمَّهُ
(وَمَالِكُ) بن أَنسِ (وَسَائِرُ) ، أي : وبَاقي (الأَئِمَّة) المعهودِين، يعني أئمة المسلمين ، كأبي عبد الله محمد بن إدريس الشافعي ، وأبي حنيفة النعمان ،، وأبي عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل، رضي الله تعالى عنهم.
والأولى جعل «أل» للكمال ؛ ليدخل
An exposition of the superiority of the four imams and those of their rank in preserving the rulings of religion. And Malik, and the rest of the imams, likewise Abu al-Qasim, are the guides of the community. 'And Malik' son of Anas, 'and the rest', i.e., the remaining well-known imams, meaning the imams of the Muslims, like Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, and Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, and Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Hanbal – may Allah be pleased with them all. And it is better to make the 'al' for completeness, so that it includes...
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a brief exposition on the excellence of the four great imams and those who are on their level in preserving the rulings of Islam. It begins with a verse from the poem: 'And Malik, and the rest of the imams, likewise Abu al-Qasim, are the guides of the community.' The author then explains the verse: 'Malik' refers to Malik ibn Anas, and 'the rest' refers to the other well-known imams such as al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Finally, the author notes that it is better to interpret the definite article 'al' in 'al-a'imma' as indicating completeness, so that it includes all imams of that caliber, not just the four.

Correction: The author clarifies that the definite article 'al' is for completeness, meaning it includes all imams of their rank, not just the four.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Virtue of the Four Imams and Other Scholars
The commentator explains the virtue of the four Imams and other scholars in preserving religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how this commentary extends honor beyond the four famous Imams to include other key scholars like al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, and al-Junayd, and why this matters for Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
The four Imams are honored, but so are al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, and al-Junayd as guides of the community.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid clarifies that the poem's praise is not limited to the four famous legal imams. It explicitly includes other great scholars, especially the two foundational theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah and the master of Sufism. This expands our understanding of who 'the guides' are.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the heading states the superiority of the four Imams and those of their rank in preserving religious rulings.
The heading sets the theme of honor and preservation.
2
Examine the enumeration of scholars
The commentator lists Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal as the four Imams, then adds al-Thawri, Ibn 'Uyaynah, al-Awza'i, al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, and al-Junayd.
The list covers fiqh, theology, and spirituality.
3
Understand the significance of al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi
The passage specifically highlights these two as 'Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah' in theology, and notes that al-Ash'ari's path is preferred in Ash'ari circles.
This connects the lesson to Ash'ari aqeedah.
4
Reflect on the inclusiveness of 'al' for completeness
The commentator recommends interpreting the definite article 'al' in 'al-aimma' as indicating completeness, meaning all worthy imams are included, not just a specific set.
This is a grammatical point with theological implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أفضليّة الأئمة الأربعة ومَن في درجتهم في حفظ أحكام الدين
ومالك وسائر الأئِمَّة كَذَا أَبُو الْقَاسِمْ هُداةُ الأُمَّهُ
(وَمَالِكُ) بن أَنسِ (وَسَائِرُ) ، أي : وبَاقي (الأَئِمَّة) المعهودِين، يعني أئمة المسلمين ، كأبي عبد الله محمد بن إدريس الشافعي ، وأبي حنيفة النعمان ، وأبي عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل، رضي الله تعالى عنهم.
والأولى جعل «أل» للكمال ليدخل [؟] لا تناسب مقامهم.
أفضلية الأئمة الأربعة في حفظ أحكام الدين
كالنَّورِي وابن عُيَيْنَة والأَوْزَاعِيَّ، خصوصاً إماما أهل السُّنَة : أبو الحسن الأشعري المُقدَّمَة طريقه في العقائد عندنا على غيره، وأبو منصور الماتُريدي كَذَا، أي : مِثلُ مَن ذُكِر في الهداية، واستقامة الطريق أَبُو القَاسِم ابن محمد الجنيد
Statement of the superiority of the four Imams and those of their rank in preserving the rulings of the religion. And Malik and the rest of the Imams, likewise Abu al-Qasim, are guides of the community. 'And Malik' son of Anas 'and the rest' meaning the remaining well-known Imams, i.e., the Imams of the Muslims, such as Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, and Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, and Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with them. And it is better to make 'al' for completeness, to include [؟] not befitting their rank. The superiority of the four Imams in preserving the rulings of the religion: like al-Thawri, and Ibn 'Uyaynah, and al-Awza'i, especially the two Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, whose path is preferred in beliefs with us over others, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi likewise, i.e., like those mentioned in guidance, and the straightness of the path is Abu al-Qasim ibn Muhammad al-Junayd.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of the poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid'. The commentator first states the heading: 'Statement of the superiority of the four Imams and those of their rank in preserving the rulings of the religion.' The poem line then says: 'And Malik and the rest of the Imams, likewise Abu al-Qasim, are guides of the community.' The commentator explains that 'and Malik' refers to Malik ibn Anas, and 'the rest' refers to the other well-known Imams of the Muslims, specifically naming al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah be pleased with them. He then notes that it is better to interpret the definite article 'al' in 'al-aimma' as indicating completeness (li al-kamal), meaning it includes all worthy imams, not just a specific set, but the text has an unclear phrase about 'not befitting their rank' which may be a marginal note. Continuing, the commentator lists other scholars of high rank: al-Thawri, Ibn 'Uyaynah, al-Awza'i, and especially the two Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah in theology: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (whose methodology in beliefs is preferred in the Ash'ari school) and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. Finally, he mentions Abu al-Qasim al-Junayd as one who embodies the straightness of the path. Thus the passage affirms the virtue and authority of these imams in preserving the religion, both in law (fiqh) and in doctrine (aqeedah).

أبو الحسن الأشعري
أبو منصور الماتريدي
أبو القاسم الجنيد
أل للكمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the poem only honors the four famous Imams (Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, Ahmad).
Correction: The passage explicitly extends honor to many other scholars, including al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, and al-Junayd, showing a broader appreciation for scholars in theology, law, and spirituality.

D) al-Junayd and al-Thawri

Key Takeaway
This passage affirms that the guides of the Muslim community include not only the four legal Imams but also key theologians like al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi, and spiritual masters like al-Junayd, reflecting a comprehensive view of Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you truly revere the scholars mentioned in this passage as your personal guides, or have you allowed modern opinions to take precedence over their teachings? What one step can you take this week to learn from one of their works?
?
When you face a religious question, do you instinctively turn to the legacy of these Imams or to easier, less authoritative sources? How can you realign your search for knowledge to honor their role as 'guides of the community'?
?
The passage honors al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi for their theological guidance. Are you aware of the beliefs you hold regarding Allah's attributes, and do they align with the path of Ahl al-Sunnah? If not, what are you willing to study to correct this?

The Three Categories of Guided Scholars: Fuqaha, Mutakallimun, and Sufis
Classifies guided scholars into three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the guidance of the Ummah is not limited to fiqh alone but includes the scholars of 'aqeedah and tasawwuf.

Core Idea
The Ummah needs three types of guides: jurists, theologians, and spiritual masters.

This passage establishes that the guided scholars of the Ummah form three essential categories: those who preserve the rulings of fiqh, those who safeguard the principles of 'aqeedah, and those who purify the hearts through tasawwuf. It names the key exemplars of each category and emphasizes that all three are needed for complete religious guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's classification come through.
2
Identify the three categories
Find where the passage explicitly divides guidance into fiqh, 'aqeedah, and tasawwuf. Note the specific imams mentioned for each.
The final sentence gives the summary.
3
Understand the obligation to believe
The passage states it is obligatory (yajib) to believe that these guides are the best after the Companions. Reflect on why this belief is important.
4
Connect to the broader purpose
Consider how each category addresses a different dimension of the religion: law, creed, and spiritual purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضلية الأئمة الأربعة في حفظ أحكام الدين كالنوري وابن عيينة والأوزاعي خصوصاً إماما أهل السنة : أبو الحسن الأشعري المقدمة طريقه في العقائد عندنا على غيره، وأبو منصور الماتريدي كذا أي مثل من ذكر في الهداية، واستقامة الطريق أبو القاسم ابن محمد الجنيد من جبال العلم كما في المحلي على جمع الجوامع، وما نقل عن إمام الحرمين من ذم الظاهرية فمحمول على بعض أتباعه كابن حزم الأمير . فقوله هنا: والأولى جعل أل للكمال راجع لقوله قبل المعهودين . فهو استدراك . قسم النبوات الزاهد سيد الصوفية علماً وعملاً، وكان على مذهب أبي ثور صاحب الشافعي، وكذا أصحابه، فيجب أن يعتقد أن مالكًا ومن ذكر معه هداة هذه الأمة، فهم خيارها بعد من التي هي خير من ذكر من الصحابة ومن معهم. قوله: (وكذا أصحابه أي أصحاب الجنيد هداة الأمة، والحاصل: أن مالكا ونحوه هداة الأمة في الفروع، والأشعري ونحوه هداتهم في العقائد الدينية، والجنيد ونحوه هداتهم في علم التصوف.
The preference of the four imams in preserving the rulings of religion, such as al-Nuri, Ibn 'Uyaynah, and al-Awza'i, especially the two imams of Ahl al-Sunnah: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, whose path is foremost in beliefs according to us over others, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi likewise, i.e., like those mentioned in guidance; and the one who established the path, Abu al-Qasim ibn Muhammad al-Junayd, who is among the mountains of knowledge as in al-Mahalli on Jam' al-Jawami'. And what is transmitted from Imam al-Haramayn regarding criticism of the Zahiris is applied to some of his followers like Ibn Hazm al-Amir. So his statement here: 'And the best is to make 'al' for completeness' refers to his statement before the well-known ones. So it is a correction. Section of Prophethoods: The ascetic, the master of the Sufis in knowledge and action, and he was upon the madhhab of Abu Thawr, the companion of al-Shafi'i, and likewise his companions. So one must believe that Malik and those mentioned with him are guides of this Ummah; they are the best of it after the one who is the best — those mentioned of the Companions and those with them. His statement: 'And likewise his companions' means the companions of al-Junayd are guides of the Ummah. The summary: Malik and his like are guides of the Ummah in branches (fiqh), al-Ash'ari and his like are their guides in religious beliefs, and al-Junayd and his like are their guides in the science of tasawwuf.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the guided scholars of the Ummah. It begins by highlighting the preference of the four great Imams (al-Nuri, Ibn 'Uyaynah, al-Awza'i) in preserving religious rulings, and specifically singles out the two Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah in creed: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, stating that al-Ash'ari's path is foremost in beliefs. It then mentions Abu al-Qasim al-Junayd as a mountain of knowledge. A clarification is made that criticism of the Zahiris by Imam al-Haramayn is directed only at certain followers like Ibn Hazm, not the method in general. The passage then transitions under the heading 'Section of Prophethoods' to discuss al-Junayd as the master of the Sufis, noting his adherence to the madhhab of Abu Thawr. The main point follows: it is obligatory to believe that Malik and those mentioned (the four Imams, al-Ash'ari, al-Maturidi, and al-Junayd) are guides of this Ummah, and they are the best after the Companions. Finally, the commentary of al-Shanwani summarizes the three categories: Malik and his like are guides in fiqh (legal rulings), al-Ash'ari and his like are guides in 'aqeedah (religious beliefs), and al-Junayd and his like are guides in tasawwuf (mystical knowledge). Thus, the passage establishes a tripartite division of guidance necessary for the Ummah.

أبو الحسن الأشعري
أبو منصور الماتريدي

أبو ثور

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that only the fuqaha are the guides of the Ummah, neglecting the essential roles of the mutakallimun in beliefs and the sufis in spiritual purification.
Correction: The passage explicitly teaches that all three categories are necessary and that each group guides the Ummah in a specific dimension: fiqh, 'aqeedah, and tasawwuf.

Checkpoint

A) Two: fuqaha and mutakallimun
B) Three: fiqh, 'aqeedah, and tasawwuf
C) Four: the four Imams only
D) Only one: the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Ummah requires three complementary types of guidance: fiqh from the fuqaha, 'aqeedah from the mutakallimun, and tasawwuf from the sufis.

Is there any part of your heart that resists submitting to the authority of the spiritual masters? What would it mean for you to truly accept their guidance in the purification of your soul?

Biography of al-Hafiz al-Suyuti
A biographical account of al-Suyuti's life, teachers, works, and claim to ijtihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly achievements, and controversial claim to ijtihad of al-Hafiz al-Suyuti.

Core Idea
Al-Suyuti's claim to absolute ijtihad sparked debate about scholarly authority.

This lesson introduces the renowned scholar Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti. We explore his early life, prodigious memory, teachers, his famous claim of reaching absolute ijtihad while adhering to the Shafi'i school, and the response of his contemporaries. Understanding his biography helps contextualize his vast works and influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Get an overall sense of the biography before analyzing details.
Notice the personal tone when al-Suyuti speaks about himself.
2
Identify key biographical facts
List the following: birth year and place, orphanhood, age at Quran memorization, texts memorized, intentions at Zamzam. This gives a picture of his early brilliance.
His teachers are also important – note at least three.
3
Analyze the ijtihad claim
Focus on the paragraph where al-Suyuti describes his level of ijtihad. Observe the distinction between 'mutlaq' (absolute) and 'mustaqill' (independent). Note his justification of unmatched knowledge in hadith and Arabic.
He excludes only saintly figures like al-Khidr from his claim.
4
Consider the scholarly reception
The passage ends with 'لَمْ يُسَلِّمْ لَهُ عُلَمَاءُ عَصْرِهِ' – his contemporaries did not accept his claim. Reflect on why such a claim might be contested.
This shows the high bar for claiming ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسبة إلى مدينة أسيوط المعروفة في صعيد مصر . ولد سنة ٨٤٩ هـ) في القاهرة ، نشأ يتيما ، حيث مات والده وهو ابن خمس سنوات وأشهر ، وشبَّ في عناية الكمال بن الهمام الحنفي حيث تولى تربيته، ختم القرآن حفظاً، وهو دون الثامنة، وحفظ عمدة الأحكام، ومنهاج البيضاوي في الأصول ، ومنهاج النووي في الفقه، وألفية ابن مالك، أخبر عن نفسه أنه لما حج شرب ماء زمزم بنية أن يصل في الفقه إلى رتبة الشيخ سراج الدين البلقيني، وفي الحديث إلى رتبة الحافظ ابن حجر . من شيوخه : علم الدين البلقيني ، وشرف الدين المُناوي ، والشيخ محي الدين الكافيجي وغيرهم الكثير . أخبر عن نفسه أنه بلغ درجة الاجتهاد فقال : وقد كملت عندي الآن آلات الاجتهاد بحمد الله تعالى ، أقول ذلك تحدثا بنعمة الله تعالى لا فخرا» وقال: «والذي ادعيناه هو الاجتهاد المطلق لا الاستقلال، بل نحن تابعون للإمام الشافعي ، وسالكون طريقه في الاجتهاد امتثالا لأمره، ومعدودون من أصحابه، وكيف يُظن أن اجتهادنا مقيد، والمجتهد المقيد إنما ينقص عن المطلق بإخلاله بالحديث أو العربية، وليس على وجه الأرض من مشرقها أو مغربها أعلم بالحديث والعربية مني، إلا أن يكون الخَضِرُ أو القطب أو وليا الله ؛ فإن هؤلاء لم أقصد دخولهم في عبارتي» لكن لم يسلم له علماء عصره. وله مؤلفات كثيرة جدا يصعب حصرها ، نحو (٥٠٠) مؤلفا . توفي في القاهرة سنة: (٩١١ هـ) وله من العمر إحدى وستون سنة وعشرة أشهر وثمانية عشر يوما .
Relative to the city of Asyut, known in Upper Egypt. He was born in the year 849 AH in Cairo, raised an orphan, as his father died when he was five years and some months old. He grew up under the care of al-Kamal ibn al-Humam al-Hanafi who undertook his upbringing. He completed memorizing the Quran before the age of eight, and memorized 'Umdat al-Ahkam, Minhaj al-Baydawi in usul, Minhaj al-Nawawi in fiqh, and Alfiya of Ibn Malik. He reported about himself that when he performed Hajj, he drank Zamzam water with the intention of reaching in fiqh the rank of Shaykh Siraj al-Din al-Bulqini, and in hadith the rank of al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar. Among his teachers are: 'Alam al-Din al-Bulqini, Sharaf al-Din al-Manawi, and Shaykh Muhyi al-Din al-Kafiji, and many others. He reported about himself that he reached the level of ijtihad, saying: 'The tools of ijtihad are now complete for me, by the praise of Allah. I say that as a recounting of Allah's blessing, not as a boast.' And he said: 'What we claim is absolute ijtihad (al-ijtihad al-mutlaq), not independence (al-istiqlal). Rather, we are followers of Imam al-Shafi'i, and we follow his path in ijtihad in compliance with his command, and we are counted among his companions. How could it be thought that our ijtihad is restricted? The restricted mujtahid is only inferior to the absolute due to deficiency in hadith or Arabic, and there is no one on the earth from its east to its west more knowledgeable in hadith and Arabic than me, unless it be al-Khidr or the Qutb or a saint of Allah; for these I did not intend to include in my statement.' However, the scholars of his time did not accept that from him. He has very many writings that are difficult to enumerate, about 500 works. He died in Cairo in the year 911 AH, at the age of sixty-one years, ten months, and eighteen days.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of al-Hafiz Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti. It begins by noting his lineage relative to Asyut in Egypt. He was born in 849 AH in Cairo, orphaned at a young age, and raised by al-Kamal ibn al-Humam. He exhibited brilliance, memorizing the Quran before eight and key texts. He performed Hajj and drank Zamzam with specific intentions to attain high ranks in fiqh and hadith. His teachers included prominent scholars like al-Bulqini and al-Manawi. He claimed to have reached the level of absolute ijtihad, asserting that the tools of ijtihad were complete for him. However, he clarified that he was not independent but followed Imam al-Shafi'i, and that his ijtihad was absolute (mutlaq) as opposed to restricted (muqayyad). He boasted of unparalleled knowledge in hadith and Arabic, except for saintly figures like al-Khidr. Despite this, contemporary scholars did not accept his claim. He authored about 500 works and died in 911 AH at age 61.

Key Terms
السيوطي
الاجتهاد المطلق
الحفاظ
ألفية ابن مالك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Suyuti claimed independent ijtihad (mustaqill) and broke away from the Shafi'i school.
Correction: Al-Suyuti explicitly claimed absolute ijtihad (mutlaq) while remaining a follower of Imam al-Shafi'i, as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
What did al-Suyuti claim regarding ijtihad?
A) He was an independent mujtahid (mustaqill).
B) He was an absolute mujtahid (mutlaq) while following Imam al-Shafi'i.
C) He was a restricted mujtahid (muqayyad).
D) He did not claim ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Al-Suyuti was a prolific scholar who claimed absolute ijtihad while adhering to the Shafi'i school, a claim not universally accepted by his contemporaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Suyuti drank Zamzam with the intention to reach the level of specific scholars. If you could make a single du'a while drinking Zamzam for your religious knowledge, what would you ask for? Be specific—what rank or benefit are you seeking, and is it for Allah or for prestige?
?
He said his claim of ijtihad was 'a recounting of Allah's blessing, not a boast.' When you accomplish something in your religious studies, do you tend to attribute it to yourself or to Allah? Think of a recent success—how did you feel inside? Write down one way you can genuinely thank Allah for it right now.
?
The scholars of his time did not accept his claim despite his vast knowledge. Have you ever been dismissed or not taken seriously in a matter of deen? How did you react? In light of this lesson, what can you learn about seeking acceptance from people versus seeking Allah's approval?

Biography of Imam Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti
Provides biographical details of al-Suyuti from birth to death, including his controversial ijtihad claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events of al-Suyuti's life and the nature of his controversial claim to absolute ijtihad within the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Al-Suyuti's mastery of hadith and Arabic fueled his bold claim to absolute ijtihad.

Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti stands as one of the most prolific and debated scholars of the late Mamluk period. His biography, as presented in this passage, not only traces his personal journey from orphanhood to scholarly eminence but also highlights his daring assertion of reaching the rank of absolute ijtihad—a claim that stirred controversy among his contemporaries. This lesson walks through his life milestones and examines the defense he offered for his ijtihad claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing details. Then read the English translation. Let the narrative flow before focusing on specific parts.
2
Identify the key biographical phases

3
Analyze his ijtihad claim
Focus on al-Suyuti's own words about ijtihad.
