Attributed to the city of Asyut known in Upper Egypt. He was born in the year 849 AH in Cairo. He grew up an orphan, as his father died when he was five years and some months old. He was raised under the care of al-Kamal ibn al-Humam al-Hanafi, who undertook his upbringing. He completed memorization of the Qur'an before age eight. He memorized 'Umdat al-Ahkam, Minhaj al-Baydawi in usul, Minhaj al-Nawawi in fiqh, and Alfiya of Ibn Malik. He reported about himself that when he performed Hajj, he drank Zamzam water with the intention of reaching in fiqh the rank of Shaykh Siraj al-Din al-Bulqini, and in hadith the rank of al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar. Among his teachers: 'Alam al-Din al-Bulqini, Sharaf al-Din al-Munawi, and Shaykh Muhyi al-Din al-Kafiji, and many others. He reported about himself that he reached the degree of ijtihad, saying: 'Now the tools of ijtihad have been perfected for me, by the praise of Allah; I say that recounting Allah's blessing, not vaingloriously.' He said: 'What we claim is absolute ijtihad, not independent ijtihad; rather, we are followers of Imam al-Shafi'i, walking his path in ijtihad in compliance with his command, and counted among his companions. How can it be thought that our ijtihad is restricted? The restricted mujtahid falls short of the absolute only by deficiency in hadith or Arabic, and there is no one on the earth, from its east to its west, more knowledgeable in hadith and Arabic than I, unless it is al-Khidr, or the Qutb, or a saint of Allah; I did not intend to include these in my statement.' But the scholars of his time did not concede this to him. He has very many works, difficult to count, around 500 works. He died in Cairo in the year 911 AH, at the age of sixty-one years, ten months, and eighteen days.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti. It traces his lineage to Asyut, his birth in Cairo in 849 AH, and his orphanhood. It details his early education under al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, his rapid memorization of the Qur'an and key texts in hadith, usul, fiqh, and Arabic grammar. It recounts his famous niyyah (intention) when drinking Zamzam water—to attain the rank of al-Bulqini in fiqh and Ibn Hajar in hadith. His teachers include prominent scholars like al-Bulqini, al-Munawi, and al-Kafiji. The biography highlights al-Suyuti's controversial claim to have reached absolute ijtihad (al-ijtihad al-mutlaq), while clarifying that he remained a follower (tabi') of Imam al-Shafi'i. He defends his claim by arguing that restricted mujtahids fall short in hadith or Arabic, and he asserts his unparalleled mastery of these disciplines, excepting superhuman figures like al-Khidr or saints. Nevertheless, his contemporaries did not accept his claim. The entry concludes with his prolific output (500 works) and death in 911 AH at age 61 years, 10 months, 18 days.

Biography of Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya: A Critical Account
Biographical account with harsh criticism of Ibn Qayyim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life of Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya and the controversy surrounding his association with Ibn Taymiyya, as seen from a critical Ash'ari perspective.

Core Idea
Ibn Qayyim's legacy is inseparable from his teacher Ibn Taymiyya, attracting both fierce loyalty and condemnation.

This lesson presents the biography of Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya as recorded from a critical Ash'ari perspective. As you read, you'll encounter not only his life events but also the polemical accusations that shaped his reputation. Understanding this context is key to appreciating the theological battles of his time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for understanding, then the English translation. Note the author's tone.
The passage is not neutral; it is a hostile source.
2
Identify key biographical events
List the major events: birth, death, relationship with Ibn Taymiyya, imprisonment, teaching.
3
Note the critical assessments
Find the evaluations by Ibn Hajar, al-Dhahabi, al-Kawthari, and al-Subki. What do they criticize?
Especially the accusation of reviving Hashwiyya and Mujassima.
4
Analyze the accusation
Consider the claim that he revived anthropomorphism. Why is this important for the Ash'ari author?
This is a central polemical point.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with hope for repentance. What does this reveal about the author's stance?
It shows a mix of condemnation and hope.

هو الشيخ محمد بن أبي بكر بن أيوب بن حريز الزُّرعي الدمشقي المشهور بـابن قيم الجوزية ، ولد سنة : (٦٩١ هـ) وتوفي سنة : (٧٥١) وقد بلغ من العمر ستين سنة. من أكثر شيوخه تأثيرا عليه شيخه ابن تيمية الحراني ، قال الحافظ ابن حجر: غلب عليه حبُّ ابن تيمية حتى كان لا يخرجُ عن شيءٍ مِن أقواله ، بل ينتصر له في جميع ذلك ، وهو الذي هذَّبَ كُتبه ونشر علمه ، وكان له حظ عند الأمراء المصريين، واعتقل مع ابن تيمية بالقلعة، أنْ أُهين وطِيفَ به على جمل مضروبا بالدرة، فلما مات أُفرج عنه، وامتحنَ مرّة أخرى بعد ذلك بسبب فتاوی ابن تيمية ، وكان ينال من علماء عصره وينالون منه . قال عنه عصريه الذهبي في المختص : حُبس مرة لإنكاره شد الرحل لزيارة قبر الخليل، ثم تصدر للأشغال ونشر العلم، ولكنَّه مُعجب برأيه، جرئ على الأمور، وكانت مدة ملازمته لابن تيمية منذ عاد من مصر سنة (۷۱۲) إلى أن مات . اهـ . ويعتبر هو وشيخه مَن بَعَثَا مذهب الحشوية والمجسمة من مرقدها، ومن مؤلفاته: نظم النونية) وقد وصف كتابه هذا الشيخ الكوثري بقوله: من أبشع كتبه ، وأبعدها غورا في الضلال، وأشنعها إغراء للحشوية ضد أهل السنة، وأوقحها في الكذب على العلماء . اهـ . وقد اطلع على نونيته عصريه الإمام تقي الدين السبكي فردَّ عليه في كتاب سماه: «السيف الصقيل في الرد على ابن زفيل» وابن زفيل هو ابن قيم الجوزية، وفيه من السب والكلام البذيء في حق أئمة أهل السنة الكثير، ومما جاء فيها مثلا : حتى أتى من أرض آمد آخــرا ثور كبير حقيرُ الشَّـان يقصد به الإمام سيف الدين الآمدي رحمه الله ورضي عنه ، وأغلب منظومته على هذا المنوال ستة آلاف بيت إلَّا واحدا وخمسين بيتا ، ونأمل أن يكون قد تاب من عقيدته السوء ومن وقوعه في علماء أهل السنة وأن يتجاوز عنه ربه وله كتب أخرى منها: «زاد المعاد في هدي خير العباد» و«الروح» وهي .
He is Shaykh Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr ibn Ayyub ibn Hurayz al-Zur'i al-Dimashqi, known as Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya. He was born in the year 691 AH and died in the year 751 AH, reaching the age of sixty. Among his most influential teachers was his shaykh Ibn Taymiyya al-Harrani. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: Love of Ibn Taymiyya overcame him until he would not deviate from any of his statements, but rather supported him in all of that; and it was he who edited his books and spread his knowledge. He had favor with the Egyptian rulers, and was imprisoned with Ibn Taymiyya in the citadel, where he was humiliated and paraded on a camel, beaten with a whip. When [Ibn Taymiyya] died, he was released, and he was tested another time thereafter due to Ibn Taymiyya's fatwas. He would disparage the scholars of his time and they would disparage him. His contemporary al-Dhahabi said in al-Mukhtass: He was imprisoned once for denying the preparation of saddles for visiting the grave of al-Khalil (Abraham). Then he took up teaching and spreading knowledge, but he was conceited in his opinion, bold in matters. His companionship with Ibn Taymiyya lasted from his return from Egypt in the year 712 until his death. End. He and his teacher are considered to have revived the doctrine of the Hashwiyya (anthropomorphists) and the Mujassima (corporalists) from their graves. Among his works is the versification (Nazm al-Nuniyya). Shaykh al-Kawthari described this book as 'one of his most hideous books, furthest in error, most appalling in inciting Hashwiyya against Ahl al-Sunna, and most insolent in lying against the scholars.' End. His contemporary Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki examined his Nuniyya and responded to him in a book titled 'al-Sayf al-Saqil fi al-Radd 'ala Ibn Zafil' — Ibn Zafil being Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya. In it there is much insult and foul speech against the imams of Ahl al-Sunna. For example, in it: 'Until there came from the land of Amid a great bull, contemptible in status' — meaning Imam Sayf al-Din al-Amidi, may God have mercy on him and be pleased with him. Most of his poem is on this pattern, six thousand minus fifty-one verses. We hope that he repented from his evil creed and from his attacks on the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna, and that his Lord will forgive him. He has other books including 'Zad al-Ma'ad fi Hidayat Khayr al-'Ibad' and 'al-Ruh'. And it is...
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note (tarjama) about Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya, taken from the hashya of the commentary. It provides his full name, birth and death years, and highlights his close association with Ibn Taymiyya, his editing of Ibn Taymiyya's works, his political favor, and his imprisonment. It then presents critical assessments from later scholars: Ibn Hajar notes his extreme partisanship for Ibn Taymiyya; al-Dhahabi mentions his imprisonment for rejecting travel to visit the grave of Abraham and describes him as conceited and bold. The passage accuses him and Ibn Taymiyya of reviving the doctrines of Hashwiyya and Mujassima. It details criticism of his poem 'al-Nuniyya' by al-Kawthari and al-Subki, giving an example of an insulting verse against al-Amidi. It ends with a hope for his repentance and lists some of his other works. The passage is strongly polemical and reflects the doctrinal conflicts of the time.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya, though a prolific scholar, remains a controversial figure due to his unwavering support for Ibn Taymiyya and the theological positions attributed to Hashwiyya and Mujassima.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Qayyim was so devoted to his teacher that he 'would not deviate from any of his statements.' Is there any person, scholar, or author to whom you give this level of unquestioning loyalty? What would it take for you to critically examine their views if they contradicted evidence?
?
The passage ends with a wish that Ibn Qayyim repented from his 'evil creed.' When did you last honestly examine your own beliefs for errors that might distance you from Allah? What one belief about Allah or the deen are you most afraid to question, and why?
?
Al-Kawthari called Ibn Qayyim's poem 'one of his most hideous books, furthest in error, most insolent in lying.' If someone you respect wrote a book that contained clear falsehoods about scholars, would you have the courage to denounce it publicly? Or would you remain silent out of loyalty? What does your answer reveal about your priorities?

Biography of Al-Mawardi
Biographical note on Al-Mawardi listing his teachers, students, works, and a critical remark.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key aspects of Al-Mawardi's life, his scholarly contributions, and the notable criticism regarding his I'tizali leanings.

Core Idea
Al-Mawardi was a towering Shafi'i scholar with a hint of I'tizali leanings in his Tafsir.

This lesson introduces you to the prominent Shafi'i scholar Al-Mawardi, a chief judge and prolific author. The passage from the commentary provides his biography, listing his teachers, students, major works, and a critical remark from Al-Subki about his theological leanings. By reading this, you'll get a concise snapshot of his scholarly profile.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of Al-Mawardi's life.
Notice the structure: name, birth, teachers, students, works, quote, death.
2
Identify key biographical details
Extract his full name, birth year and place, and the origin of his nisbah.
The nisbah comes from rose water trade.
3
List his teachers, students, and works
Note the names of his teachers and students, and his major works like Al-Hawi Al-Kabir and Al-Ahkam Al-Sultaniyya.
4
Examine Al-Subki's comment and the criticism
Read Al-Subki's praise and the note about his I'tizali leanings. Consider what this means for his scholarly reputation.
This shows that even great scholars can have controversial aspects.
5
Reflect on his legacy
Think about why Al-Mawardi is still studied today, particularly his works on constitutional law and fiqh.
His works remain influential.

هو أقضى القضاة أبو الحسن علي بن محمد بن حبيب البصري الماوردي الشافعي. والماوردي نسبة إلى عمل المَاوَرْدِ، لأن بعض أجداده كان يعمله أو يبيعه. ولد سنة 364 هـ في البصرة ونشأ بها على طلب العلم. من شيوخه: عبد الواحد بن الحسين الصيميري من أصحاب الوجوه، والشيخ أبو حامد الإسفراييني، وأخذ الحديث عن جعفر بن محمد البغدادي، وغيرهم. من تلامذته الخطيب البغدادي، وأبو بكر الحلواني البغدادي، وأبو العز ابن كادش العكبري، وغيره. من مؤلفاته: الحاوي الكبير في الفقه، شرح به مختصر المزني، وله: «الأحكام السلطانية» وأعلام النبوة وغيرها من الكتب العالية. قال عنه السبكي: الإمام الجليل القدر، الرفيع الشأن، له اليد الباسطة في المذهب، والتفنن التام في سائر العلوم [؟] وكان له ميل إلى الاعتزال في بعض المسائل في تفسيره. [؟] توفي سنة 450 هـ وله من العمر ست وثمانون سنة، وصلى عليه الخطيب البغدادي.
He is the Chief Judge Abu Al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Habib Al-Basri Al-Mawardi Al-Shafi'i. And Al-Mawardi is a relative attribution to the work of Al-Maward (rose water), because one of his ancestors used to make or sell it. He was born in 364 AH in Basra and grew up there seeking knowledge. Among his teachers: Abdul Wahid ibn Al-Hussein Al-Saymari, one of the prominent figures, and Sheikh Abu Hamid Al-Isfarayini, and he studied hadith from Ja'far ibn Muhammad Al-Baghdadi, and others. Among his students: Al-Khatib Al-Baghdadi, Abu Bakr Al-Halwani Al-Baghdadi, Abu Al-Izz ibn Kadish Al-`Ukbari, and others. Among his works: Al-Hawi Al-Kabir in fiqh, with which he commented on the Mukhtasar of Al-Muzani, and he has 'Al-Ahkam Al-Sultaniyya' and 'A'lam Al-Nubuwwa' and other high-level books. Al-Subki said about him: The great imam of status, high dignity, he has the extensive hand in the school, and complete mastery in all sciences [؟] and he had a leaning toward I'tizal in some issues in his Tafsir. [؟] He died in 450 AH at the age of eighty-six years, and Al-Khatib Al-Baghdadi prayed over him.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on the scholar Al-Mawardi. It gives his full name and lineage, explaining the origin of his nisbah to rose water. It states his birth year and place, then lists his key teachers, including Abu Hamid Al-Isfarayini, and his students, including Al-Khatib Al-Baghdadi. It mentions his major works, particularly Al-Hawi Al-Kabir, Al-Ahkam Al-Sultaniyya, and A'lam Al-Nubuwwa. The passage then quotes Al-Subki's praise of Al-Mawardi's status and mastery, but notes a criticism: that he had a leaning toward I'tizal in some matters of his Tafsir. It concludes with his death date in 450 AH and that Al-Khatib Al-Baghdadi led his funeral prayer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Mawardi had a leaning toward I'tizal in some issues of his Tafsir, yet he is still considered a great imam. Is there any weakness in your own character or belief that you have been hiding behind your good deeds? Will you face it honestly today, or continue to cover it with your reputation?
?
He sought knowledge from multiple teachers and mastered various sciences. What is the one area of Islamic knowledge you have been neglecting because it is difficult? Will you take a concrete step this week—enroll in a class, read a book, or ask a scholar—to begin mastering it?
?
Al-Mawardi's teacher al-Saymiri is described as 'one of the prominent figures' (أصحاب الوجوه). Think of a scholar you respect. Have you ever truly thanked them for their contribution to your faith? Write to them today or make a sincere du'a for them.

Biographical Note on Abd al-Jabbar al-Hamadhani
A biographical note on Abd al-Jabbar, a Mu'tazili scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical context of the Mu'tazili scholar Abd al-Jabbar, including his teachers, students, works, and his sectarian classification in Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
Abd al-Jabbar was the leading Mu'tazili theologian of his era, considered an innovator in Sunni tradition.

This lesson introduces you to Abd al-Jabbar, a prominent Mu'tazili scholar. The passage provides his full name, titles, teachers, students, and key works. It also places him within the sectarian framework of Sunni orthodoxy, noting that the Mu'tazila are considered people of innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall content.
Notice the formal structure: name, title, teachers, students, career, works.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the full name, title (Qadi al-Qudat), teachers, students, and the city of his judgeship and death.
The title 'Qadi al-Qudat' is specifically used by the Mu'tazila for him.
3
Note the sectarian characterization
The passage states that his students followed the method of the Mu'tazila, who are described as 'people of innovation'. Understand that this reflects a Sunni evaluation.
4
Review the list of his works
Identify the three works mentioned: 'Tanzih al-Qur'an', 'al-Mughni', and 'al-Amali'. Consider their themes related to tawhid and justice.
These works are central to Mu'tazili theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦) عبد الجبار بن أحمد بن عبد الجبار بن أحمد بن خليل العلامة المتكلم، أبو الحسن الهمذاني، كان شيخ المعتزلة في عصره، وهم يلقبونه قاضي القضاة ، ولا يطلقون هذا اللقب على غيره من كبار فقهاء الشافعية . من شيوخه: علي بن إبراهيم بن سلمة القطان، وعبد الله بن جعفر بن فارس، والزبير بن عبد الواحد الحافظ. ومن تلاميذه: أبو القاسم التنوخي، والحسن بن علي الصيمري الفقيه ، وأبو يوسف عبد السلام القزويني المفسر ، وَليَ القضاء بالرَّيّ ، ومات فيها سنة (٤١٥هـ) تخرّج به خلق في الرأي على طريقة المعتزلة أهل البدعة وتصانيفه كثيرة، منها: تنزيه القرآن عن المطاعن ، والمغني في أبواب التوحيد والعدل»، و«الأمالي».
(6) Abd al-Jabbar ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Jabbar ibn Ahmad ibn Khalil, the eminent scholar, the mutakallim, Abu al-Hasan al-Hamadhani. He was the shaykh of the Mu'tazila in his time, and they would call him 'Qadi al-Qudat', and they do not apply this title to anyone else among the senior Shafi'i jurists. Among his teachers: Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn Salamah al-Qattan, Abdullah ibn Ja'far ibn Faris, and al-Zubayr ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Hafiz. Among his students: Abu al-Qasim al-Tanukhi, al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Saymari al-Faqih, and Abu Yusuf Abd al-Salam al-Qazwini al-Mufassir. He held the position of judge in Rayy, and died there in the year 415 AH. Many people graduated under him in opinion (ra'y) on the method of the Mu'tazila, the people of innovation, and his works are numerous, including: 'Tanzih al-Qur'an 'an al-Mata'in', 'al-Mughni fi Abwab al-Tawhid wa al-'Adl', and 'al-Amali'.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a biographical footnote about the Mu'tazili scholar Abd al-Jabbar al-Hamadhani. It provides his full name and title as a mutakallim (theologian). It notes that he was the leading figure of the Mu'tazila in his time and was given the title 'Qadi al-Qudat' (Judge of Judges), a title not applied to any other Shafi'i jurist. The note lists his teachers, students, his tenure as judge in Rayy, and his death year (415 AH). It mentions that many students followed his methodology (ra'y) on the path of the Mu'tazila (considered people of innovation in Sunni thought). Finally, it lists three of his major works: 'Tanzih al-Qur'an 'an al-Mata'in' (Vindication of the Qur'an from Objections), 'al-Mughni fi Abwab al-Tawhid wa al-'Adl' (The Sufficient on the Topics of Tawhid and Justice), and 'al-Amali' (Dictations).

Correction: The passage clarifies that he was the shaykh of the Mu'tazila, a group considered 'people of innovation' in Sunni orthodoxy, and his works are on Mu'tazili theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

In your own life, do you seek recognition from those who share your views, or do you measure yourself by the standards of the wider Muslim community? What is the true measure of a scholar in Allah's sight?

The Biography of al-Jazuli: A Stalwart Maliki Scholar
Biographical note on the scholar al-Jazuli, his expertise and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Jazuli's scholarly stature, his role in the Maliki school, and his major works.

Core Idea
Al-Jazuli was a towering Maliki jurist whose commentaries and teaching shaped the school for generations.

This lesson presents a concise biography of the great Maliki scholar al-Jazuli. It highlights his expertise, his vast study circle, and his enduring contributions through three commentaries on the Risala. This passage helps us appreciate the chain of scholarship that transmitted the Maliki tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get a sense of the scholar's life and achievements.
Notice the respectful language used in the biography.
2
Identify al-Jazuli's key attributes
Look for his full name, his school of jurisprudence (Maliki), his city of residence, and his reputation as a teacher.
Also note the astonishing number of students and their memorization of the Mudawwana.
3
Examine his written works
The passage mentions three commentaries on al-Risala. Note their sizes and the statement that they are all beneficial.
Consider why such works were important for the Maliki school.
4
Reflect on his lifespan and dedication
Al-Jazuli lived over 120 years and never stopped teaching. Reflect on the lesson of lifelong learning and dedication.
This connects to the Islamic tradition of seeking knowledge until death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الفقيه الكبير عبد الرحمن بن عفان الجزولي ، أبو زيد المالكي، نزيل فاس، كان أعلم الناس في عصره بمذهب مالك وكان يحضر مجلسَهُ أكثر من ألف فقيه معظمهم يستظهر «المدونة» ، وله ثلاثة شروح على «الرسالة» كبير ، ووسط ، وصغير ، وكلها مفيدة انتفع الناس بها بعده، مُعمّر قد عاش أكثر من مائة وعشرين سنة، وما قطع التدريس حتى توفي سنة (٧٤١ هـ) رحمه الله وأعلى مقامه .
He is the great jurist 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Affan al-Jazuli, Abu Zayd al-Maliki, resident of Fez. He was the most knowledgeable of his time in the Maliki school, and his study circle was attended by more than a thousand jurists, most of whom memorized the Mudawwana. He wrote three commentaries on the Risala: a large, a medium, and a small one, all beneficial, and people benefited from them after him. He was long-lived, living more than one hundred and twenty years, and he did not stop teaching until he died in the year 741 AH. May God have mercy on him and elevate his rank.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about the scholar al-Jazuli. It highlights his immense stature as a Maliki jurist, his large teaching circle, and his prolific authorship of three commentaries on the famous Maliki text al-Risala. It notes his remarkable longevity—over 120 years—and that he continued teaching until his death in 741 AH. The passage concludes with a prayer for mercy upon him.

الجزولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might confuse al-Jazuli with other scholars bearing the same nisba or name.
Correction: This biography provides clear identification: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Affan al-Jazuli, Abu Zayd al-Maliki, resident of Fez, died 741 AH. His specific works and teaching circle distinguish him.

Checkpoint
How many commentaries did al-Jazuli write on the Risala?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Al-Jazuli was a long-lived Maliki master who produced three key commentaries on the Risala and taught thousands of students.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Jazuli taught over a thousand jurists and wrote multiple commentaries, all while living over 120 years without ceasing teaching until his death. You are still young—what will you have to show for your years? Will you be found in service of knowledge until your last breath?
?
He produced three different commentaries on a single text. What does that say about the depth of his understanding? When was the last time you truly immersed yourself in one subject until you mastered it inside out?
?
Most of his students had memorized the Mudawwana—a massive text. Is your relationship with Islamic texts one of memorization, deep study, or only occasional reading? What change must you make today to follow in the footsteps of these scholars?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani
beginner
4 min
Biography of Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni
A biographical sketch of Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, education, and contributions of the Shafi'i scholar Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, father of Imam al-Haramayn.

Core Idea
A scholar's journey from Juwayn to mastery of the Shafi'i school.

This lesson introduces you to Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, a towering figure in Shafi'i jurisprudence. His biography illustrates the traditional path of seeking knowledge: studying under multiple teachers, traveling to centers of learning, and producing works that shaped the madhhab. The passage details his birth, teachers, students, works, and character.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Familiarize yourself with the names and flow of the biography.
Notice the structure: birth, teachers, students, works, praise, death.
2
Identify key stages in his education
Trace his educational journey: first in Juwayn, then Nishapur, then Merv. Note the names and specialties of his teachers.
He studied under Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi, a major Shafi'i authority.
3
Note his students and works
List his prominent students, especially his son Imam al-Haramayn. Recognize his authored works like 'Al-Silsila' and 'Al-Tabsira'.
His students became influential scholars themselves.
4
Reflect on his character
Read the descriptions from al-Subki and al-Dhahabi. Consider his dedication to seeking knowledge and his piety.
His qunut supplication shows his zeal for learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصره، ولد في جُويْن من نواحي نيسابور ، ونشأ في بيت علم وأدب ، لم تذكر كتب التراجم سنة ولادته ، لكن يغلب على الظن أنه ولد ما بين (۳۸۰ - ۳۹۰ هـ) تقريبا، والله أعلم. من شيوخه: درس على أبي يعقوب الأبيوردي في جوين ، ثم سافر إلى نيسابور وتفقه على أبي الطيب الصعلوكي ، ثم ارتحل إلى مرو قاصدا شيخ الخراسانيين العلامة الكبير أبو بكر القفال المروزي ؛ فلازمه حتى تخرج به مذهبا وخلافا وطريقة ، فأتقن المذهب وطريقة شيخه . من تلامذته: ابنه أبو المعالي إمام الحرمين عبد الملك ، وأبو بكر محمد الصفار مفتي نيسابور ، وأبو نصر الطوسي، وغيرهم الكثير . من مؤلفاته: «السلسلة» في معرفة القولين والوجهين وله التبصرة في ترتيب أبواب للتميز بين الاحتياط والوسوسة» وله كتاب التعليقة وغيرها من المؤلفات. وقال السبكي عنه: له المعرفة التامة بالفقه والأصول، والنحو والتفسير ومن صفاته : أنه كان حريصا على طلب العلم ، قال إمام الحرمين: كان والدي يقول في دعاء القنوت: اللهم لا تعقنا عن العلم بعائق ، ولا تمنعنا عنه بمانع . قال عنه الذهبي : أبو محمد شيخ الشافعية ، كان فقيها مدققا محققا نحويا مفسرا ، كان مجتهدا في العبادة مهيبا بين التلامذة، صاحب جد ووقار، وهو صاحب وجه في المذهب. وفاته توفي له سنة ٤٣٨ هـ ، وقيل : سنة ٤٣٤ هـ .
Of his era, he was born in Juwayn in the districts of Nishapur, and grew up in a house of knowledge and literature. The biographical books do not mention his birth year, but it is most likely that he was born between approximately 380-390 AH, and Allah knows best. Among his teachers: He studied under Abu Ya'qub al-Abiwardi in Juwayn, then traveled to Nishapur and studied fiqh under Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi, then journeyed to Merv intending to study under the shaykh of the Khorasanis, the great scholar Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi; he stayed with him until he graduated in madhhab, differing opinions, and methodology, mastering the madhhab and the method of his shaykh. Among his students: His son Abu al-Ma'ali Imam al-Haramayn 'Abd al-Malik, Abu Bakr Muhammad al-Saffar the mufti of Nishapur, Abu Nasr al-Tusi, and many others. Among his works: 'Al-Silsila' on knowledge of the two opinions and two aspects, and he has 'Al-Tabsira' on ordering chapters for distinguishing between caution and obsession, and he has the book 'Al-Ta'liqa' and other works. Al-Subki said about him: He has complete knowledge of fiqh, usul, grammar, and tafsir. Among his qualities: He was diligent in seeking knowledge. Imam al-Haramayn said: My father used to say in the Qunut supplication: 'O Allah, do not hinder us from knowledge by an obstacle, nor prevent us from it by a barrier.' Al-Dhahabi said about him: Abu Muhammad, shaykh of the Shafi'is, was a precise, thorough jurist, grammarian, exegete, diligent in worship, awe-inspiring among students, dignified and serious, and he is a recognized authority in the madhhab. His death: He died in the year 438 AH, and it is said 434 AH.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the Shafi'i scholar Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, the father of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni. It begins by mentioning his birthplace in Juwayn, near Nishapur, and his upbringing in a scholarly home. His birth year is estimated between 380-390 AH. The text then lists his teachers, showing his educational journey: first under Abu Ya'qub al-Abiwardi in Juwayn, then Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi in Nishapur, and finally the prominent Khorasani scholar Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi in Merv, whom he studied with until he mastered the Shafi'i madhhab and its methodology. His students include his own son, the famous Imam al-Haramayn, as well as other notable figures like Abu Bakr al-Saffar and Abu Nasr al-Tusi. His authored works are mentioned, including 'Al-Silsila', 'Al-Tabsira', and 'Al-Ta'liqa'. The passage then quotes al-Subki praising his comprehensive knowledge of fiqh, usul, grammar, and tafsir. It describes his personal qualities: his zeal for learning, as illustrated by a prayer his son narrated, and his meticulousness and piety. Al-Dhahabi's description sums up his stature: he was a precise jurist, grammarian, exegete, and a dignified teacher. Finally, his death date is given, with the primary year 438 AH and an alternate 434 AH.

Key Terms
جويين
نيسابور
شيوخ
تلامذة
مؤلفات
وجه في المذهب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni was only important because of his son, Imam al-Haramayn.
Correction: Though he is the father of Imam al-Haramayn, Abu Muhammad was himself a major Shafi'i scholar, a precise jurist, and author of several works, as praised by al-Dhahabi and al-Subki.

Checkpoint
From which school of law was Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni?
A) Hanafi
B) Maliki
C) Shafi'i
D) Hanbali

Key Takeaway
Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni was a distinguished Shafi'i jurist, teacher of Imam al-Haramayn, and a model of scholarly dedication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The du'a of Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni in qunut was: 'O Allah, do not hinder us from knowledge by an obstacle, nor prevent us from it by a barrier.' What obstacles—lack of time, laziness, distractions—do you allow to keep you from seeking sacred knowledge? Are you more concerned with comfort than learning your religion? Will you remove one barrier this week, starting today?
?
He traveled from Juwayn to Nishapur to Merv, leaving home and family, to study under the great scholars of his time. How far—in effort, sacrifice, or focus—have you gone to gain knowledge of Allah's religion? If your answer is 'not far,' what is the real reason you hold back?
?
Al-Dhahabi described him as 'diligent in worship, awe-inspiring among students, dignified and serious.' Examine your own attitude when you learn: Are you truly diligent, or do you treat knowledge casually? Do you carry yourself with the gravity that learning about Allah demands? What will you change about your approach to knowledge tonight?

Life of Imam al-Laqqani

The Life and Works of Imam al-Jujri
Biographical note on al-Jujri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, teachers, and scholarly contributions of Imam Muhammad ibn Abd al-Mun'im al-Jujri.

Core Idea
Al-Jujri: a scholar who learned from the greats and taught while his teachers were still alive.

This lesson introduces the commentator of our text, al-Jujri. We learn about his name, birth, education, teachers, and his own works. Understanding his background gives context to his commentary, which is part of the source text we study.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the details about his name, birth, and early education.
2
Identify his teachers
The passage lists several notable teachers. Note their names and think about their significance in Islamic scholarship.
Teachers include Ibn Hajar, al-Sakhawi, al-Mahalli, and al-Munawi.
3
Note his principal works
The passage mentions three commentaries. Identify each one and note their full titles.
Works include Tashil al-Masalik, a commentary on al-Irshad, and a commentary on Shudhur al-Dhahab.
4
Reflect on his teaching status
Al-Jujri taught during his teachers' lifetimes, even receiving their students. This shows his high scholarly standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( الجوجري) بجيمين على الصواب، وفي نسخة بدل الثانية هاء. الأمير. وهو محمد بن عبد المنعم بن محمد الجوجري القاهري الشافعي، ولد سنة: (۸۲۱ هـ) بجوجر، ثم رحل إلى القاهرة وحفظ القرآن، والمنهاج الفرعي، والأصلي، وألفية ابن مالك، ومن شيوخه: الحافظ ابن حجر ، والشهاب السخاوي ، والجلال المحلي، والمناوي وغيرهم، له غير واحد من شيوخه بالإقراء والإفتاء وتصدى لذلك في حياة مشايخه، حتى كان الجلال المحلي يرسل له الفضلاء للقراءة عليه في تصانيفه وغيرها، ومن مؤلفاته: كتب شرحا على عمدة السالك لابن النقيب سماه: تسهيل المسالك وله شرح على «الإرشاد» وله شرح على شذور الذهب وغيرها من المؤلفات. توفي سنة : (۸۸۹ هـ).
His saying: (al-Jujri) with two jeems correctly, and in one copy instead of the second a ha'. Al-Amir. He is Muhammad ibn Abd al-Mun'im ibn Muhammad al-Jujri al-Qahiri al-Shafi'i, born in the year (821 AH) in Jujar, then he traveled to Cairo and memorized the Qur'an, and al-Minhaj al-Far'i and al-Asli, and Alfiyyat Ibn Malik, and among his teachers: al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, and al-Shihab al-Sakhawi, and al-Jalal al-Mahalli, and al-Munawi and others. He had more than one teacher under whom he studied recitation and fatwa, and he devoted himself to that during the lifetime of his teachers, until al-Jalal al-Mahalli used to send the virtuous to read to him his compositions and others. Among his works: he wrote a commentary on 'Umdat al-Salik by Ibn al-Naqib called Tashil al-Masalik, and he has a commentary on al-Irshad, and a commentary on Shudhur al-Dhahab, and other works. He died in the year: (889 AH).
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note identifying the commentator al-Jujri. It begins by clarifying the correct spelling of his name: with two jeems, though some copies replace the second jeem with a ha. Then it gives his full name: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Mun'im ibn Muhammad al-Jujri al-Qahiri al-Shafi'i. It mentions his birth year (821 AH) and his birthplace (Jujar). It describes his education: he moved to Cairo, memorized the Qur'an, studied the Minhaj al-Far'i and al-Asli, and Alfiyyat Ibn Malik. It lists his notable teachers, including Ibn Hajar, al-Sakhawi, al-Jalal al-Mahalli, and al-Munawi. It notes his expertise in recitation and issuing fatwas, to the extent that his teachers sent students to him. It lists his major works: a commentary on 'Umdat al-Salik (Tashil al-Masalik), a commentary on al-Irshad, and a commentary on Shudhur al-Dhahab. It concludes with his death year (889 AH).

Key Terms
الجوجري
محمد بن عبد المنعم
تسهيل المسالك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what year did al-Jujri die?
A) 821 AH
B) 889 AH
C) 899 AH
D) 847 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Jujri was a prominent 9th-century AH scholar who studied under major figures and authored important commentaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Jujri traveled from Jujar to Cairo to seek knowledge, memorizing foundational texts and studying under great scholars. What have you sacrificed or left behind for the sake of learning? Are you willing to uproot yourself for what matters most?
?
He taught and issued fatwas during the lifetimes of his own teachers, and great scholars sent students to him. Are you actively sharing what you know with others, even while you are still learning? Or do you wait until you feel 'ready'?
?
His teachers entrusted him with students and his works continue to be studied. If your life's contribution were listed in a brief biography like this, would it show a commitment to preserving and transmitting sacred knowledge? What steps will you take today to ensure your legacy serves the deen?
